Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Jadha'a in Zakat and Gender Ruling
Intra-Hanafi dispute over jadha'a in zakat + gender permissibility

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding jadha'a in zakat, state the mufta bihi position, and identify the ruling on male/female animals.

Core Idea
In Hanafi zakat, a jadha'a (young sheep) is not acceptable except for da'n (sheep) due to a specific text; male and female are both valid.

This passage from Al-Hidayah presents an internal Hanafi dispute between Abu Hanifa and his two main disciples (the Sahibayn) on whether a young sheep (jadha'a) can be given for zakat. It also clarifies that both male and female animals are acceptable. Understanding this dispute reveals how the Hanafi school prioritizes certain proofs over others when resolving ikhtilaf.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two positions
Abu Hanifa holds that only a musinn (full-aged) or older is acceptable in zakat; jadha'a is too young. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) permit jadha'a for sheep (ghanam).
2
Examine the proofs (dalil)
Abu Hanifa relies on the hadith of 'Ali (ra) which explicitly says 'only musinn or above.' The Sahibayn rely on the hadith of Mis'ar where Prophet’s agents accepted a jadha'a, and analogy to sacrifice.
Note the hierarchy: hadith of 'Ali is considered stronger.
3
Analyze the Hanafi response to the Sahibayn
The hadith of Mis'ar is interpreted to refer to camel jadha'a, not sheep. Analogy to sacrifice is rejected because sacrifice has a specific text for da'n that does not extend to zakat.
4
Determine thamarah al-khilaf (practical difference)
According to Abu Hanifa, a person cannot give a jadha'a (young goat) to fulfill zakat; must give a musinn. Sahibayn would allow it.
5
Apply the ruling on gender
Both male and female sheep are acceptable for zakat because the word 'sha'ah' in the hadith includes both genders.
This part is not disputed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فِي بَطْنَهَا وَلَدُهَا ، قُلْتُ فَأَى شَيْءٍ تَأخُذَانِ قَالَا عِنَاقَا جِذْعَةً أُوثِنْيَةٌ فَأَخْرَجْتُ إِلَيْهِمَا عِنَاقَا فَتَنَا وَلَاهَا، یعنی ابوداؤد نسائي اور احمد نے اپنی مسند میں مسعر سے تخریج کی ہے مسعر کہتے ہیں کہ میرے پاس آگے پیچھے ہو کر دو آدمی آئے انہوں نے آکر کہا کہ ہم رسول اللہ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم کے قاصد ہیں۔ ہم کو آپ کی طرف بھیجا گیا ہے تا کہ آپ ہم کو اپنی بکریوں کی زکوۃ دیں۔ مسعر کہتے ہیں کہ میں نے کہا کہ زکوۃ کیا ہے تو انہوں نے کہا کہ بکری مسعر نے کہا کہ میں نے ایک گا بھن اور موٹی تازی بکری دینے کا ارادہ کیا تو انہوں نے کہا کہ یہ تو شافع ہے حالانکہ ہم کو رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے شافع لینے سے منع کیا ہے۔ اور شافع وہ ہوتی ہے جس کی پیٹ میں اس کا بچہ ہو۔ میں نے کہا کہ پھر تم کیا لو گے۔ انہوں نے کہا کہ عناق بکری کا بچہ سال پورا ہونے سے پہلے ) جذعہ ہو یا ثنیہ پس میں نے ان کو عناق نکال کر دیا تو انہوں نے اس کو لے لیا ( فتح القدیر) ان دونوں روایتوں سے ثابت ہو گیا کہ غنم کی زکوۃ میں جذعہ لینے کی اجازت ہے دوسری دلیل یہ ہے کہ جذعہ کی قربانی جائز ہے پس اس کو زکوۃ میں دینا بھی جائز ہے۔
ظاہر الروایہ کی وجہ حدیث علی ہے جس کو موقوفا اور مرفوعا دونوں طرح روایت کیا گیا ہے الفاظ حدیث یہ ہیں کہ لَايُو حَذْفِي الزَّکوة إلَّا النَّبِي فَصَا عِدا یعنی زکوۃ میں منی لیا جائے گا یا اس سے بڑھ کر یعنی شنی سے زیادہ عمر کا اور پہلے گذر چکا کہ جذعہ منی سے کم عمر کا ہوتا ہے اس لئے اس کو نہیں لیا جائے گا۔
دوسری دلیل یہ ہے کہ واجب تو اوسط درجہ کا ہے اور جذعہ چھوٹا ہونے کی وجہ سے ادنی درجہ میں ہے اس لئے جذعہ جائز نہ ہوگا۔ یہی وجہ ہے کہ بکری کا جذعہ زکوۃ میں لینا بالاتفاق جائز نہیں ہے اور رہاضان (بھیڑ دنبہ ) کے جذعہ کا قربانی میں جائز ہونا تو وہ نص سے پہچانا گیا ہے چنانچہ ارشاد ہے نِعْمَتِ الأَضْحِيَّةُ الْجِذْعَ مِنَ الضَّأْنِ ) عنايه ) یعنی ضان کا جذعہ بہترین قربانی ہے پس جذعہ قربانی سے زکوۃ کی طرف متعدی نہیں ہوگا۔ اور زکوۃ قربانی کے ہم معنی بھی نہیں ہے۔ کہ زکوۃ کو قربانی پر قیاس کر لیا جاتا ہے اور رہی صاحبین کی طرف سے پیش کردہ حدیث إِنَّمَا حَقْنَا الْجِدُعَةَ وَالنبي تو اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ اس حدیث میں جذعہ سے اونٹ کا جذعہ مراد ہے نہ کہ ضان کا ۔
زکوۃ میں مذکر اور مؤنث دونوں طرح کے جانور لینا درست ہے وَيُوجَدُ فِي زَكَوةِ الْغَنَمِ الذَّكُورُ وَالأنَاتُ لِأَنَّ اسْمَ الشَّاةِ يَنتَظِمُهُمَا وَقَدْ قَالَ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ فِي أَرْبَعِيْنَ شَاءَ شَاةٌ والله أعلم
ترجمہ اور غم کی زکوۃ میں نر اور مادہ دونوں کا لینا جائز ہے۔ کیونکہ لفظ شاہ دونوں کو شامل ہے حالانکہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا ہے کہ چالیس بکریوں میں ایک بکری ہے۔ واللہ اعلم
تشریح بکری، بھیڑ اور دنبہ کی زکوۃ میں نر کا لینا بھی جائز ہے اور مادہ کا لینا بھی جائز ہے دلیل یہ ہے کہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم کے قول فی اربعین شَاةٍ شَاةٌ“ میں شاہ کا لفظ آیا ہے اور لفظ شاہ نر اور مادہ دونوں کو شامل ہے۔ اس لئے زکوۃ میں خواہ نردے خواہ مادہ دونوں درست ہیں ۔ علم بالصواب ۔ جمیل احمد عفی عنہ
... (in her belly is her offspring) I said: 'Then what do you take?' They said: 'A young goat, a jadha'a or a thaniyya.' So I brought out to them a young goat, they took it... meaning Abu Dawud, Nasa'i, and Ahmad narrated from Mis'ar... Mis'ar said: Two men came to me, one behind the other, and said: 'We are messengers of the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him. We have been sent to you so that you may give us the zakat of your sheep.' Mis'ar said: I said: 'What is the zakat?' They said: 'A sheep.' Mis'ar said: I intended to give a pregnant, fat sheep, but they said: 'This is a shafi', and the Messenger of Allah has forbidden us from taking a shafi'. A shafi' is one with a fetus in its belly.' I said: 'Then what will you take?' They said: 'A young goat (before one year), whether jadha'a or thaniyya.' So I brought out a young goat to them, and they took it. (Fath al-Qadir). From these two narrations it is established that taking a jadha'a in zakat of ghanam is permissible. The second proof is that the sacrifice of a jadha'a is permissible, so giving it in zakat is also permissible. The reason for Zahir al-Riwayah is the hadith of 'Ali, narrated both as mauquf and marfu': its words are: 'La yu'khadhu fi al-zakat illa al-musinnu wa ma fawqaha' meaning in zakat, a musinn (full-aged) or older is taken, and it has passed that jadha'a is younger than musinn, so it will not be taken. The second proof: the wajib is of middle grade, and jadha'a, due to being young, is of low grade, so jadha'a will not be permissible. This is why taking a jadha'a of a goat in zakat is unanimously impermissible. As for the jadha'a of da'n (sheep) being permissible in sacrifice, that is known from the text; indeed it is said: 'Ni'mat al-udhiyyatu al-jidh'u min al-da'n' meaning the best sacrifice is the jadha'a of da'n. So the permissibility of jadha'a in sacrifice does not transfer to zakat, and zakat is not equivalent to sacrifice, that zakat could be analogized to sacrifice. As for the hadith presented by the Sahibayn: 'Innama haqquna al-jid'atu wa al-thanu', the answer is that in this hadith, jadha'a refers to the young of camels, not of da'n. In zakat of ghanam, it is permissible to take both male and female: 'Wa yujadu fi zakati al-ghanami al-dhukuru wa al-inathu li anna isma al-sha'ati yantazimuhuma wa qad qala 'alayhi al-salamu fi arba'ina sha'atan sha'atan.' Translation: In zakat of sheep, it is permissible to take both male and female, because the word 'sha'ah' encompasses both. Allah knows best. Explanation: In zakat of goats, sheep, and rams, it is permissible to take both male and female. The proof is that the words of the Prophet 'fi arba'ina sha'atan sha'atan' include the word 'sha'ah', which includes both male and female. Therefore, in zakat, whether male or female, both are valid.
Source pages p. 58

Commentary
This passage contains two main topics: (1) an intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) regarding whether a jadha'a (young sheep between 6-12 months for goats/sheep) can be given as zakat, and (2) the ruling that both male and female animals are acceptable in zakat of sheep. The passage begins by narrating a hadith from Mis'ar about two messengers of the Prophet (saw) who refused a pregnant ewe (shafi') and accepted a young goat (jadha'a or thaniyya). This is used by the Sahibayn to argue that jadha'a is permissible in zakat of ghanam. Abu Hanifa's position, based on the hadith of 'Ali (ra), is that only a musinn (full-aged) animal should be taken, and jadha'a is too young. The commentary explains that the Sahibayn's hadith is interpreted to refer to the young of camels, not sheep. The second part states that both male and female are acceptable in zakat of sheep because the word 'sha'ah' in the hadith 'fi arba'ina sha'atan sha'atan' includes both genders. This is a straightforward ruling with no dispute.

Key Terms
جذعہ (jadha'a/jidh'a): A young sheep or goat that has entered its second year but not yet completed it; generally between 6-12 months for goats, and for sheep up to one year. In this text, jadha'a is contrasted with musinn (full-aged).
ثنیہ (thaniyya/thaniyyah): A sheep that is entering its third year; a two-year-old. In this text, it is presented as an alternative to jadha'a for zakat.
شافع (shafi'): A pregnant ewe; literally 'one with a fetus' (shaf' means pair/double). In the hadith, it is prohibited to take a shafi' as zakat because it is too valuable.
عَناق ('anaq): A young goat or kid; a small young one before reaching one year. In the hadith, it is accepted as jadha'a or thaniyya.
ضأن (da'n): Sheep (as opposed to ma'z goats). In this text, jadha'a is only acceptable for da'n due to the hadith on sacrifice.
مُسِنَّة (musinnah/musinn): A full-aged animal, typically one that has completed its second year and entered the third. Required in zakat according to the hadith of 'Ali.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position (mufta bihi), in which case can a jadha'a (young animal) be given in zakat of sheep?
A) For all types of sheep and goats
B) Only for sheep (da'n) due to specific textual permission for sacrifice
C) For goats but not sheep
D) It is never acceptable; only a musinn may be given

Key Takeaway
In zakat of sheep (ghanam), the mufta bihi is that only a musinn (full-aged) is acceptable except for da'n (sheep) where jadha'a is allowed by special text; male and female are both acceptable.

Zakat on Sa'imah Horses: The Abu Hanifa – Sahibayn Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on zakat for pastured horses

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi mufta bihi position on zakat for sa'imah horses, identify the intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn, and explain how the apparent hadith conflict is resolved through takhsis.

Core Idea
Zakat on sa'imah horses: Abu Hanifa says wajib; Sahibayn say no; the warhorse hadith is an exception.

This passage from Al-Hidayah addresses a classic intra-Hanafi dispute: does zakat apply to horses that graze freely (sa'imah) when kept for breeding? The ruling depends on a careful reconciliation of two apparently contradictory hadiths. By the end of this lesson, you will be able to navigate this ikhtilaf and apply the relied-upon Hanafi position.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the act being ruled upon (zakat on sa'imah horses) and the hukm level according to Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Zufar: wajib, with a choice of payment method.
2
Identify the opposing view within the madhhab
The Sahibayn (Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani) hold that no zakat is due on horses at all. Their dalil is the hadith: 'Laysa 'ala al-Muslimi fi 'abdihi wa la fi farasihi sadaqah.'
3
Follow Abu Hanifa's proof
Abu Hanifa cites another hadith: 'Fi kulli farasin sa'imatin dinarun aw 'ashara darahim.' This is the primary evidence for wajib.
4
Analyse the reconciliation (takhsis)
Abu Hanifa interprets the Sahibayn's hadith as specific to the warhorse (faras al-ghazi), based on a transmission from Zayd ibn Thabit. Thus, the general ruling for other sa'imah horses remains wajib.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: under Abu Hanifa's view, an owner of mixed-gender sa'imah horses pays zakat; under the Sahibayn's view, no payment is required. The mufta bihi position is Abu Hanifa's.

گھوڑوں کی زکوة گھوڑوں میں نصاب ہے یا نہیں، مقدار ز کوۃ

Chapter on Horses. Translation: Chapter on (zakat of) horses. Zakat of horses: Is there a nisab in horses, and what is the amount of zakat? When horses are sa'imah (pastured), both male and female, then the owner has a choice: if he wishes, he gives from each horse a dinar, and if he wishes, he values them and gives from every two hundred (dirhams) five dirhams. This is according to Abu Hanifa, and it is the saying of Zufar. They two (Sahibayn) said: There is no zakat on horses, because of the saying of the Prophet, peace be upon him: 'There is no sadaqah on a Muslim for his slave nor for his horse.' And for him (Abu Hanifa) is the saying of the Prophet, peace be upon him: 'For every sa'imah horse, a dinar or ten dirhams.' And the interpretation of what they narrated is that it refers to the horse of a ghazi (warrior), and this is transmitted from Zayd ibn Thabit. And the choice between the dinar and valuation is reported from 'Umar. Translation: When horses are sa'imah, male and female, then their owner has a choice: if he wishes, he gives from each horse a dinar, and if he wishes, he values them and gives from every two hundred dirhams five dirhams. This ruling is according to Abu Hanifa, and this is the saying of Imam Zufar. The Sahibayn said: There is no zakat on horses because the Prophet said: 'There is no sadaqah on a Muslim for his slave nor for his horse.' Abu Hanifa's proof is that the Prophet said: 'For every sa'imah horse, a dinar or ten dirhams.' The interpretation of the hadith narrated by the Sahibayn is that it refers to the horse of a ghazi (warrior), and this is transmitted from Zayd ibn Thabit. The choice between the dinar and valuation is reported from 'Umar. Commentary: Shaykh al-Adab wrote in Sharh al-Niqayah, vol. 1, p. 150, footnote 5: A horse is not free from two states: either 'ulufah (fed at home) or sa'imah (pastured). If it is 'ulufah, then there are two situations: either it is fed for riding, carrying loads, or jihad fi sabilillah, or it is fed for trade. In the first, there is no zakat by consensus, because trade property is that which grows and is surplus to need. In the second, zakat is wajib by consensus, because in that case the property grows and is surplus to need, because designating them for trade is evidence of growth and surplus. If they are sa'imah, then again two situations: either they are pastured in free lands for riding, carrying loads, jihad, or ghazw, or they are pastured for trade. In the first case, by consensus zakat is not wajib. In the second case, by consensus zakat is wajib. If they are pastured for milk and breeding, then there are two situations: either the males and females are mixed, or they are not mixed. In the first situation, according to Imam Abu Hanifa, zakat is wajib, and the owner has a choice to give from each horse a dinar or to value them and give from every two hundred dirhams five dirhams. In the second situation, again two cases: either they are only females or only males. In both cases, there are two narrations from Abu Hanifa: one for obligation and one for non-obligation. For pure females, the prevalent narration is obligation, because it is possible to borrow a male horse from another for reproduction and breeding. And...
Source pages p. 59

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa (supported by Zufar) and the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) regarding the obligation of zakat on horses. The text first states the ruling: if horses are sa'imah (pastured, not fed at home) and include both males and females, then according to Abu Hanifa, zakat is wajib, and the owner has a choice between giving one dinar per horse or valuing the horses and giving 2.5% (i.e., 5 dirhams per 200 dirhams worth). The Sahibayn hold that no zakat is due on horses at all, citing the hadith: 'There is no sadaqah on a Muslim for his slave nor for his horse.' Abu Hanifa counters with another hadith: 'For every sa'imah horse, a dinar or ten dirhams.' The commentary then elaborates, classifying horses into categories: 'ulufah (fed at home) vs sa'imah (pastured), and within each, for personal use vs trade. For trade, zakat is wajib by consensus. For personal use, no zakat. For sa'imah horses kept for breeding (milk and offspring), if males and females are mixed, zakat is wajib according to Abu Hanifa. If only females or only males, there are two narrations, with the prevalent one being obligation for females (since breeding is possible with borrowed males). The text is incomplete at the end, cutting off during the discussion of pure males.

Key Terms
خیل (khayl): Horses, collectively. In this context, horses subject to zakat rules.
سائمہ (sa'imah): Pastured livestock that graze freely on public or natural vegetation without being fed at home. This is a key condition for zakat on animals.
علوفہ ('ulufah): Animals fed at home with stored fodder; opposite of sa'imah. Not subject to zakat unless for trade.
دینار (dinar): Gold coin; standard currency in early Islam. In this ruling, one dinar per horse or valuation option.
درہم (dirham): Silver coin; 10 dirhams = 1 dinar roughly. Used in valuation option: 5 dirhams per 200 dirhams value (2.5%).
فرس غازی (faras al-ghazi): Warhorse used by a ghazi (fighter in jihad). Exempted from zakat according to interpretation of Sahibayn's hadith.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bihi position in the Hanafi school, when is zakat due on horses?
A) On all horses, whether sa'imah or 'ulufah
B) Only on sa'imah horses when both males and females are present
C) Only on horses used for trade
D) Never; horses are exempt from zakat entirely

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school distinguishes between warhorses (exempt) and sa'imah breeding horses (zakat wajib if mixed gender), reconciling conflicting hadiths through takhsis.

Zakat — Almsgiving
intermediate
8 min
Zakat on Horses: Abu Hanifa vs. Sahibayn
Dispute on zakat on horses with proofs and response

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on zakat for saima horses and explain the intra-school dispute between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn, including the key proofs and the mufta bihi ruling.

Core Idea
Zakat on horses is wajib only if they are saima and mixed; the Sahibayn and other schools hold it is not due at all.

When is zakat due on horses? The Hanafi school has an internal disagreement. Imam Abu Hanifa holds that zakat is obligatory on grazing horses kept for breeding, while his two principal students, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, disagree. This lesson unpacks their proofs and the resolution within the school, showing how apparent contradictory hadiths are reconciled through interpretation.

Guided Path
1
State the position of Abu Hanifa and its conditions
Identify the exact ruling: zakat is wajib on horses that are sa'imah (free-grazing) and mixed male and female. Note that there is no minimum nisab; even one horse triggers zakat.
The owner has a choice: pay one dinar per head or 2.5% of estimated value.
2
State the opposing view of the Sahibayn
The Sahibayn (and the three other imams) hold that no zakat is due on horses at all, regardless of type, grazing, or purpose.
This is the default position in the zahir al-riwayah, but later fatwa prefers Abu Hanifa's view.
3
Analyze the proofs for each side
Identify the hadith evidence: Sahibayn cite hadiths negating sadaqah on slaves and horses. Abu Hanifa cites a specific hadith from al-Daraqutni on grazing horses and the 'horses are of three types' hadith mentioning 'the right of Allah on their necks.'
The hadith 'no sadaqah on a Muslim for his slave nor for his horse' is the strongest counter-evidence.
4
Understand the Hanafi response to the counter-hadith
The author of Hidayah interprets the negating hadith as referring specifically to the horse of a warrior (ghazi), based on the practice of Zayd ibn Thabit and Umar ibn al-Khattab.
This takhsis (specification) reconciles the apparent contradiction and upholds Abu Hanifa's view.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf and the mufta bihi position
The practical consequence: under Abu Hanifa's view, owners of saima mixed horses must pay zakat; under Sahibayn's view, nothing is due. The Hanafi school gives tarjih to Abu Hanifa's position, and it is the operative ruling for fatwa.
This is a case of legitimate ikhtilaf within the madhhab, resolved by the later masters.

وَسَلَّمَ لَيْسَ عَلَى الْمُسْلِم فِى عَبْدِهِ وَلَا فِى فَرَسِهِ صَدَقَةٌ ( شرح نقایہ بحوالہ کتب سبتہ ابو ہریرہ کہتے ہیں کہ رسول اکرم صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے فرمایا ہے کہ مسلمان پر اس کے غلام اور اس کے گھوڑے میں زکوۃ نہیں ہے۔ سنن ابی داؤ داور ترندی میں حدیث ہے عَنْ عَلِيّ قَالَ قَالَ رَسُولُ اللهِ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ قَدْ عَفَوْتُ لَكُمْ عَنْ صَدَقَةِ الْحَيْلِ وَالرَّقِيقِ حضرت علی نے کہا کہ رسول اللہ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے فرمایا ہے میں نے تم کو معاف کر دیا گھوڑے اور غلام کی زکوۃ سے ۔ امام بیہقی نے روایت ذکر کی ہے "عَنْ أَبِي هُرَيْرَةَ قَالَ قَالَ رَسُولُ اللهِ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ عَفَوْتُ لَكُمْ عَنْ صَدَقَةِ الْجَبْهَةِ وَالْكَسْعَة وَالسَّخَةِ وَالْجَبْهَةُ الخَيْلُ وَالنَّحةُ بالفتح والصّم الرَّقِيق وَالْكَسْعَةُ الْحَمِيرُ" حضرت ابو ہریرہ نے فرمایا ہے کہ اللہ کے رسول صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے فرمایا ہے کہ میں نے تم سے گھوڑے غلام اور گدھے کی زکوۃ معاف کر دی ہے جبھۃ کے معنی گھوڑے کے ہیں اور النخة نون کے فتحہ اور صنمہ کے ساتھ پڑھا گیا ہے معنی ہیں، غلام کے اور کسعہ گدھے کو کہتے ہیں ان تینوں احادیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ گھوڑے کے اندرز کو ۃ واجب نہیں ہے۔ امام ابوحنیفہ کی دلیل دار قطنی کی یہ روایت ہے فى كُلّ فَرَسٍ سَائِمَةٍ دِيْنَارٌ أَوْ عَشَرَةَ دَرَاهِمَ یعنی ہر سائمہ گھوڑے میں ایک دینار ہے یا دس درہم ہیں نیر وہ روایت بھی امام ابو حنیفہ کا مستدل ہے جس کو یحین (امام بخاری اور امام مسلم ) نے روایت کیا ہے متن حدیث یہ ہے عَنْ أَبِي هُرَيْرَةَ قَالَ قَالَ رَسُولُ اللهِ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ الْخَيْلُ ثَلاثَةٌ هي لرجلٍ أَجْرُو لِرَجُلٍ سَتَرُو عَلَى رَجُلٍ وِزُرٌ فَاَمَّا الَّتِي هِىَ لَهُ أَجْرٌ فَرَجُلٌ رَبَطَهَا فِي سَبِيلِ اللَّهِ وَ هِيَ لِذَالِكَ الرَّجُلِ أَجْرُ وَ رَجُلٌ رَبَطَهَاتَغُنياً وتعففاً وَلَمْ يَنْسَ حَقَّ الله فِى رِقَابِهَا وَلَا ظُهُورِهَا فَهِيَ لَهُ سِتَرٌ وَ رَجُلٌ رَبَطَهَا فَخُرًا وانواء فَهى عَلَى ذَالِكَ وزُرٌ فَسُئِلَ رَسُولُ اللهِ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ عَن الْحَمِيْر فَقَالَ مَا أنزلَ عَلَيَّ فِيهَا إِلَّاهذِهِ الآيَةُ الغاذة فَمَنْ يَعْمَلْ مِثْقَالَ ذَرَّةٍ خَيْرًا يَرَهُ وَمَنْ يُعْمَلُ مِثْقَالَ ذَرَّةٍ شَرًّائِرَهُ . حضرت ابو ہریرہ نے کہا کہ رسول اللہ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے فرمایا ہے کہ گھوڑا تین آدمیوں کے لئے ہے ایک آدمی کے لئے اجر ہے اور ایک کے لئے بہتر ہے اور ایک پر وبال ہے۔ بہر حال وہ آدمی جس کے لئے اجر ہے وہ ہے جس نے اللہ کے راستہ میں جہاد کرنے کے لئے باندھا یہ گھوڑا اس کے لئے اجر ہے اور ایک وہ آدمی ہے جس نے اس کو اظہار ثروت اور تعلف عن السوال کے لئے باندھا۔ اور اس کی گردن اور پیٹھ میں اللہ کا حق نہیں بھولا تو یہ گھوڑا اس کے لئے ستر ہے۔ یعنی پردہ اور ڈھال ہے۔ اور ایک وہ آدمی جس نے اس کو فخر و مباہات کے لئے باندھا تو یہ گھوڑا اس پر گناہ ہے۔ آنحضرت صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم سے گدھوں کی زکوۃ کے بارے میں دریافت کیا گیا تو آپ نے فرمایا کہ مجھ پر اس بارے میں علاوہ آیت فَمَنْ يَعْمَلْ مِثْقَالَ لا زال کے کچھ نازل نہیں کیا گیا ہے اس روایت میں "وَلَمْ يَنْسَ حَقَّ اللَّهِ فِي رَقَا بِهَا" کا لفظ ہے اور ظاہر ہے کہ گھوڑے کی گردن میں اللہ کا حق زکوۃ کے سواء اور کیا ہوسکتا ہے پس اس روایت سے بھی گھوڑوں میں زکوۃ کا واجب ہونا ثابت ہو گیا ہے۔ صاحب ہدایہ صاحبین کی طرف سے پیش کردہ روایت لَيْسَ عَلَى المُسلِم فِى عَبْدِهِ وَلَا فِي فَرْسِةٍ صَدَقَةٌ کا جواب دیتے ہیں جواب کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ اس روایت میں فرس غازی مراد ہے۔ یعنی غازی مسلمان پر اس کے گھوڑے کی زکوۃ نہیں ہے۔ یہ تاویل زید بن ثابت سے منقول ہے۔ صاحب عنایہ کے بیان کے مطابق مروان کے زمانہ میں یہ واقعہ پیش آیا کہ گھوڑے میں زکوۃ واجب ہے یا نہیں ؟ صحابہ سے اس بارے میں مشورہ کیا گیا حضرت ابو ہریرہ نے لَيْسَ عَلَى الرَّجُلِ فِى عَبْدِهِ وَلَا فِي قَرْسِهِ صَدَقَةٌ روایت بیان کی تو مروان نے زید بن ثابت کو مخاطب کر کے کہا " مَا تَقُولُ يَا اَبا سَعِید اے ابو سعید ! تم کیا کہتے ہو؟ ابو ہریرا نے کہا کہ مروان پر حیرت ہے میں حدیث رسول صلى الله عليه وسلم بیان کر رہا ہوں اور وہ کہتا ہے مَا تَقُولُ یا اَبا سَعِيد " ( یہ سن کر ) زید بن ثابت نے کہا کہ رسول اللہ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے سچ فرمایا ہے لیکن اس سے مراد فرس غازی ہے اور جو گھوڑ اطلب نسل کے لئے چرایا گیا ہو اس میں زکوۃ ہے۔ ابو ہریرہ نے کہا کتنی فرمایا فِى كُلِّ فَرَسٍ دِينَارًا اَوْ عَشَرَةَ دَرَاهِم " صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ دینار اور قیمت لگا کر ہر دوسو درہم سے پانچ درہم دینے میں اختیار دینا حضرت عمرؓ سے منقول ہے چنانچہ مروی ہے فَإِنَّهُ كَتَبَ إلى أبي عُبَيْدَةَ فِي صَدَقَةِ الْخَيلِ خَيْرَ اَربَا بَهَا أَنْ اَدوامِنْ كُلِّ فَرَسٍ دِيْنَارا والا فَقَومُهَا وَحُذْمِنْ كُلِّ مِاتَى دِرْهَم خَمْسَةَ دَرَاهِم یعنی حضرت عمر نے ابوعبیدہ بن الجراح کو گھوڑے کی زکوۃ کے بارے میں تحریر فر مایا اور گھوڑوں کے مالکان کو اختیار دیا کہ وہ ہر گھوڑے سے ایک دینارادا کریں ورنہ محصل کی قیمت لگا کر ہر دوسو درہم سے پانچ درہم لے لے۔
The ruling of non-obligation in pure male (horses) is prevalent. Because according to Abu Hanifa, its meat is not eaten and reproduction from it is not possible. Therefore the preponderant view is that zakat is not obligatory. The Two Companions (Sahibayn) said that zakat is not obligatory in horses, regardless of their type, whether fodder-fed or grazing, mixed or not mixed, for jihad or for trade, whether breeding is intended or riding and carrying. This is also the saying of Imam Shafi'i, Imam Malik, and Imam Ahmad. According to the statement of the author of Hidayah, the result of the issue is that according to Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Zufar, zakat is obligatory in horses on the condition that they are grazing (sa'imah) and that males and females are mixed, not exclusively male or exclusively female. However, the owner has a choice in paying zakat: either give one dinar per horse, or evaluate them and give five dirhams per two hundred dirhams. As for what is the nisab for horses according to Imam Abu Hanifa? The correct thing is that no specific nisab is considered for horses; even if there is one horse, zakat is obligatory on it. Some said that three horses are the nisab, some said five, and some said that for the nisab, two males and two females are necessary. The Two Companions and the three Imams said that zakat is absolutely not obligatory in horses. The proof of the Two Companions is the hadith of Abu Hurayrah: 'The Messenger of Allah said: There is no sadaqah on a Muslim for his slave nor for his horse.' Also in Sunan Abi Dawud and Tirmidhi, the hadith from Ali: 'The Messenger of Allah said: I have remitted for you the sadaqah of horses and slaves.' Al-Bayhaqi narrated: 'From Abu Hurayrah: The Messenger of Allah said: I have remitted for you the sadaqah of al-jabhah, al-kas'ah, and al-sakhah. Al-jabhah is horses, al-nahhah (with fatha on nun and sukun on ha) is slaves, and al-kas'ah is donkeys.' These three hadiths indicate that zakat is not obligatory on horses. The proof of Imam Abu Hanifa is the narration of al-Daraqutni: 'For every grazing horse, one dinar or ten dirhams.' Also, the narration that the two Shaykhs (Bukhari and Muslim) narrated is Abu Hanifa's proof: the text: 'From Abu Hurayrah: The Messenger of Allah said: Horses are of three types: for one man they are a reward, for another a covering, and for another a burden. As for the one for whom they are a reward: a man who ties them in the path of Allah, so they are a reward for him. And a man who ties them for enrichment and chastity, and does not forget the right of Allah on their necks and backs, so they are a covering for him. And a man who ties them for pride and hypocrisy, so they are a burden on him. The Messenger of Allah was asked about donkeys, and he said: Nothing has been revealed to me concerning them except this comprehensive verse: So whoever does an atom's weight of good will see it, and whoever does an atom's weight of evil will see it.' In this hadith, the phrase 'and does not forget the right of Allah on their necks and backs' appears. It is obvious that the right of Allah on the neck of a horse can only be zakat. So this hadith also proves the obligation of zakat on horses. The author of Hidayah responds to the hadith presented by the Two Companions: 'There is no sadaqah on a Muslim for his slave nor for his horse.' The answer is that in this hadith, 'horse' refers to the horse of a warrior (ghazi). That is, there is no zakat on a Muslim warrior's horse. This interpretation is narrated from Zayd ibn Thabit. According to the author of 'Inayah, this incident occurred during the time of Marwan: An inquiry was made about whether zakat is obligatory on horses. The Companions were consulted. Abu Hurayrah narrated the hadith 'There is no sadaqah on a man for his slave nor for his horse.' Marwan addressed Zayd ibn Thabit, saying, 'What do you say, O Abu Sa'id?' Abu Hurayrah said, 'I marvel at Marwan! I am narrating a hadith of the Messenger of Allah, and he says, "What do you say, O Abu Sa'id?"' Upon hearing this, Zayd ibn Thabit said, 'The Messenger of Allah spoke the truth, but it refers to the horse of a warrior. As for the horse that is grazed for breeding, there is zakat on it.' Abu Hurayrah said, 'How many?' He said, 'For every horse, one dinar or ten dirhams.' The author of Hidayah says that the option of giving one dinar or evaluating and giving five dirhams per two hundred dirhams is narrated from Umar. It is narrated that he wrote to Abu 'Ubaydah regarding the sadaqah of horses: 'Give the owners the choice: either one dinar per horse, or evaluate them and take five dirhams per two hundred dirhams.'
Source pages p. 60

Commentary
This passage presents the dispute (ikhtilaf) regarding zakat on horses. The author of Ashraf al-Hidayah explains the positions: According to Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Zufar, zakat is wajib on horses that are sa'imah (grazing freely for most of the year) and mixed (male and female). The owner has the option to pay either one dinar per horse or value them and pay 2.5% (5 dirhams per 200). There is no fixed nisab; even one horse requires zakat. The Two Companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) and the three other imams (Shafi'i, Malik, Ahmad) hold that zakat is not wajib on horses at all. The passage then provides the proofs: Sahibayn rely on hadiths stating 'no sadaqah on one's slave or horse' and a hadith of remission of zakat on horses. Abu Hanifa relies on a hadith from al-Daraqutni specifying 'for every grazing horse, one dinar or ten dirhams' and the well-known hadith of 'horses are of three types' where 'the right of Allah on their necks' is interpreted as zakat. The author of Hidayah resolves the apparent contradiction by interpreting the hadith of negation as referring specifically to the horse of a warrior (ghazi), not to horses kept for breeding or grazing. This interpretation is traced to Zayd ibn Thabit and endorsed by the practice of Caliph Umar, who prescribed zakat on horses with the option. The passage thus upholds Abu Hanifa's position as the relied-upon view within the Hanafi school, though it acknowledges the strength of the opposing evidence.

Key Terms
سائمہ (sa'imah): Livestock that graze freely on natural pasture for most of the year, as opposed to ma'lufah (fodder-fed). This condition triggers zakat on horses according to Abu Hanifa.
صاحبین (al-sahibayn): Refers to Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani, the two principal disciples of Abu Hanifa.
غازی (ghazi): A warrior engaged in jihad. The horse of a ghazi is exempt from zakat according to the interpretation of the hadith.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, under what condition is zakat wajib on horses?
A) Any horse regardless of type
B) Saima horses that are mixed male and female
C) Only horses used for trade
D) Only mares

Key Takeaway
Zakat on horses is subject to intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf; the mufta bihi position is Abu Hanifa's requirement of zakat on saima mixed horses.

Zakat — Almsgiving
intermediate
6 min
Zakat on Exclusive Male/Female Horses, Mules, and Donkeys
Rulings on zakat for single-gender horse herds, mules, and donkeys.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on zakat for exclusively male horses, exclusively female horses, and mules/donkeys, and explain the rationale based on reproduction and trade.

Core Idea
No zakat on male-only horses or mules/donkeys; zakat is wajib on female-only horses (the relied-upon view).

This passage from al-Hidayah presents the rulings for zakat on horses when the herd consists of a single gender, as well as on mules and donkeys. Understanding these specific cases helps clarify the general principle that zakat on animals is tied to natural increase (nasl) and textual prescription.

Guided Path
1
Identify the animals in question
The passage discusses four categories: exclusively male horses, exclusively female horses, mules, and donkeys.
2
State the default ruling for each
For male horses: no zakat. For female horses: one narration says no zakat, another says wajib. For mules and donkeys: no zakat. These are the starting points.
The mufta bihi for female horses is wajib.
3
Understand the rationale for horses
The key factor is the potential for reproduction (nasl). Male horses cannot reproduce without females, so no zakat. Female horses can breed with a borrowed stallion, so zakat is wajib.
This rationale is explicit in the text.
4
Recognize the intra-Hanafi difference
Abu Hanifa has three narrations: (1) no zakat on either gender, (2) zakat on females only, (3) zakat on both. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is the second.
The Hidayah commentary indicates the obligation on females is the stronger view.
5
Note the exception for trade
Mules and donkeys are exempt from zakat unless they are owned for trade, in which case zakat is calculated on their market value.
This exception is based on the general rule for trade goods.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تنہا گھوڑوں اور تنہا گھوڑیوں پر زکوة ہے یا نہیں وَلَيْسَ فِي ذُكُورِهَا مُنْفَرِدَةٌ زَكَوةً لِأَنَّهَا لَا تَتَنَاسَلُ وَكَذَا فِي الْأَنَاتِ المُنْفَرِدَاتِ فِي رِوَايَةٍ وَعَنْهُ الْوُجُوبُ فِيهَا لأنَّهَا تَتَنَاسَلُ بِالْفَحْلِ الْمُسْتَعَارِ بِخِلَافِ الذَّكُورِ وَعَنْهُ أَنَّهَا تَجِبُ فِى الذَّكُورِ الْمُنْفَرِدَةِ أَيْضًا وَلَا شَيَّ فِي الْبِغَالِ وَالْحَمِيْر لِقَوْلِهِ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ لَمْ يَنزِلُ عَلَيَّ فِيهِمَا شَى وَالْمَقَادِيرُ تَنْبُتُ سِمَاعًا إِلَّا أَنْ يَكُونَ لِلتِّجَارَةِ لأَنَّ الزَّكوةَ حِينَئِذٍ تَتَعَلَّقُ بِالْمَالِيَّةِ كَسَائِرِ أَمْوَالِ التِّجَارَةِ ترجمہ اور تنہا نرگھوڑوں میں زکوۃ نہیں ہے کیونکہ فقط نروں سے تناسل نہیں ہوتا اور ایک روایت میں تنہا گھوڑیوں میں بھی یہی حکم ہے۔ اور ابوحنیفہ سے دوسری روایت میں فقط گھوڑیوں میں وجوب زکوۃ ہے۔ کیونکہ گھوڑیاں مانگے ہوئے نرگھوڑوں سے جن سکتی ہیں برخلاف نروں کے اور امام صاحب سے ایک روایت میں فقط نر گھوڑوں میں بھی وجوب زکوۃ آیا ہے۔ اور خچروں اور گدھوں میں زکوۃ نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ حضور صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے فرمایا ہے کہ نیچروں اور گدھوں کی زکوۃ میں مجھ پر کچھ نازل نہیں کیا گیا ہے اور مقاد پر ثابت ہوتے ہیں سماعاً
And there is no zakat on their males (exclusively male horses) because they do not reproduce. Similarly, on exclusively female horses in one narration. And from him (Abu Hanifa) there is another narration that zakat is obligatory on them (exclusively female horses) because they can reproduce with a borrowed stallion, unlike the males. And from him also a narration that zakat is obligatory on exclusively male horses as well. And there is nothing (no zakat) on mules and donkeys because of his (peace be upon him) saying: 'Nothing has been revealed to me concerning them.' And the amounts (of zakat) are established by hearing (i.e., by transmission from the Prophet). Unless they are for trade, because then zakat attaches to their monetary value like other trade goods.
Source pages p. 61

Commentary
This passage addresses specific cases regarding zakat on horses and other equines. The base ruling (in the matn) states that there is no zakat on exclusively male horses because they cannot reproduce. The reasoning is that zakat on horses is tied to their potential for natural increase (nasl), which is absent in an all-male herd. For exclusively female horses, there is a difference of narration from Abu Hanifa: one narration says no zakat (analogous to males), another says zakat is wajib because females can be impregnated by a borrowed stallion, so they have breeding potential. Surprisingly, there is also a narration from Abu Hanifa that zakat is wajib even on exclusively male horses, though this is less consistent with the rationale. As for mules and donkeys, no zakat is due on them because the Prophet (peace be upon him) stated that no revelation came regarding their zakat, and their nisab is not established by textual transmission. However, an exception is made if these animals are owned for trade (tijarah), in which case zakat is calculated based on their market value, as with any other trade goods.

Key Terms
ذكور منفردة (dhukūr munfaridah): Exclusively male horses (i.e., herd with no females).
أناث منفردات (ināth munfaridāt): Exclusively female horses (i.e., herd with no males).
بغال (bighāl): Mules (offspring of a horse and a donkey).
حمير (hamīr): Donkeys.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the matn of Hidayah, what is the ruling on zakat for exclusively male horses?
A) Zakat is wajib on them.
B) Zakat is not wajib on them because they do not reproduce.
C) Zakat is wajib only if they are sa'imah.
D) Zakat is wajib at half the rate.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi ruling on zakat for horses depends on gender and breeding potential; mules and donkeys are exempt unless traded.

Zakah on Male and Female Horses
Intra-Hanafi dispute on zakah for horses alone

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on zakah for male horses alone and female horses alone, and identify the basis for the intra-madhhab ikhtilaf.

Core Idea
Zakah on horses depends on their ability to reproduce: females alone incur zakah, males alone do not.

The Hanafi school distinguishes between male and female horses for zakah, relying on the condition of reproductive growth (nama'). This passage explores the intra-madhhab dispute on whether zakah is due on horses kept alone without the opposite gender. Understanding this ikhtilaf sharpens your ability to apply the principle of nama' to similar cases.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling for male horses alone
State the ruling in the preferred view (mufta bihi) and the reason given in the text.
Males cannot reproduce alone, so they lack nama'.
2
Identify the two narrations for female horses alone
Note that there is a narration for no zakah and another for obligatory zakah. Understand the reasoning for each.
The difference hinges on whether females can reproduce via a borrowed stallion.
3
Examine the textual proof (dalil)
The hadith 'There is no zakah on a horse of a ghazi' is used, but its application is restricted.
Hanafis interpret it as specific to the fighter's horse, not all horses.
4
Determine the mufta bihi and tarjih
The preferred view is that females alone incur zakah, males alone do not. The tarjih is based on the stronger evidence for nama' in females.
This is the relied-upon position for fatwa.
5
Cross-madhhab note
Imam al-Shafi'i holds zakah on all horses, showing the practical difference.
This expands your understanding of school differences.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَلَيْسَ فِي ذُكُورِهَا مُنْفَرِدَةٌ زَكَوةً لِأَنَّهَا لَا تَتَنَاسَلُ وَكَذَا فِي الْأَنَاتِ المُنْفَرِدَاتِ فِي رِوَايَةٍ وَعَنْهُ الْوُجُوبُ فِيهَا لأنَّهَا تَتَنَاسَلُ بِالْفَحْلِ الْمُسْتَعَارِ بِخِلَافِ الذَّكُورِ وَعَنْهُ أَنَّهَا تَجِبُ فِى الذَّكُورِ الْمُنْفَرِدَةِ أَيْضًا
There is no zakah on their males alone because they do not reproduce. Likewise, on females alone in one narration. And from him (Abu Hanifa) obligation on them (females) because they reproduce through a borrowed stallion, unlike males. And from him that it is obligatory on males alone as well.
Source pages p. 61

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute on zakah for horses kept alone (without the opposite gender). The base ruling is that zakah is not obligatory on male horses alone because they cannot reproduce. A similar view is narrated for females alone in one transmission. However, another narration from Imam Abu Hanifa makes zakah obligatory on females alone because they can reproduce using a borrowed stallion, but after offsetting the cost. A third narration extends obligation to males alone as well, analogizing them to other grazing animals (sa'imah). The mufta bihi (relied-upon) view is that zakah is not due on male horses alone, but is due on females alone when kept for breeding. This reflects the Hanafi principle that growth (nama') is a condition for zakah, and for horses growth is primarily through reproduction. Thus, animals that cannot reproduce (males alone) are not subject to zakah.

Key Terms
سائمة (sā'imah): Livestock that graze freely in open pastures for most of the year.
تناسل (tanāsul): Reproduction and natural increase of animals.
استعارة الفحل (isti'ārat al-faḥl): Borrowing a male animal for breeding purposes.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Zakah is not obligatory on any horse because of the hadith.
B) Zakah is obligatory on both male and female horses alone.
C) Zakah is obligatory on female horses alone but not on male horses alone.
D) Zakah is obligatory on male horses alone but not on female horses alone.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi obligation of zakah on horses is determined by their capacity for reproduction: females alone incur zakah, males alone do not.

Zakah on Donkeys and Mules
Ruling with proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on zakah for donkeys and mules and explain the exception for trade goods.

Core Idea
No zakah on donkeys or mules unless they are trade goods — the limits are set by divine text.

This lesson addresses a specific category of livestock that is exempt from zakah in the Hanafi school: donkeys and mules. The Prophet ﷺ stated that no revelation came regarding them, so no zakah is due unless they become trade goods. Understanding this exception is crucial for proper zakah calculation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the animals
The passage discusses donkeys and mules, which are not considered sa'imah (grazing livestock) for zakah by default.
2
State the default ruling
There is no zakah on them based on the hadith: 'Nothing has been revealed to me concerning them.'
3
Recognize the exception
If they are held for trade (tijarah), zakah applies based on their monetary value, just like other trade goods.
Zakah on trade goods is calculated on value, not on animal count.
4
Understand the principle
Zakah amounts are tawqifi (based on revelation); they cannot be extended by analogy to animals not mentioned.
The hadith explicitly states no revelation came, so no zakah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَلَا شَيَّ فِي الْبِغَالِ وَالْحَمِيْر لِقَوْلِهِ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ لَمْ يَنزِلُ عَلَيَّ فِيهِمَا شَى وَالْمَقَادِيرُ تَنْبُتُ سِمَاعًا إِلَّا أَنْ يَكُونَ لِلتِّجَارَةِ لأَنَّ الزَّكوةَ حِينَئِذٍ تَتَعَلَّقُ بِالْمَالِيَّةِ كَسَائِرِ أَمْوَالِ التِّجَارَةِ. (ثم من صفحة 62) فَصَّلَّ، وَ لَيْسَ فِي الْفُصْلَانِ وَالْعَجَاجِيلِ وَالْحِمْلَانِ صَدَقَةً عِندَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ إِلَّا أَنْ يَكُونَ مَعَهَا كِبَارُ وَهَذَا آخِرُ اقوالِهِ وَهُوَ قَوْلُ مُحَمَّدٍ وَكَانَ يَقُولُ أَوَّلَا يَجِبُ فِيْهِمَا مَا يَجِبُ فِى الْمُسَانِ وَهُوَ قَولُ زُفُر و مَالِک ثُمَّ رَجَعَ و قَالَ فِيهَا وَاحِدٌ مِنْهَا وَهُوَ قَوْلُ أَبِى يُوسُفُ وَالشَّافِعِى وَجُهُ قَوْلِهِ الْأَوَّل أَنَّ الْإِسْمَ الْمَذْكُورِ فِى الْخِطَابِ يَنتَظِمُ
There is nothing (zakah) on mules and donkeys because of his statement (peace be upon him): 'Nothing has been revealed to me concerning them.' And the fixed amounts are based on hearing (revelation), unless they are for trade, because then zakah attaches to their monetary value like other trade goods. (Then from page 62) Section: There is no zakah on young camels, young cows, and young sheep according to Abu Hanifa unless adults are with them. This is his final view, and it is the view of Muhammad. He used to say initially: 'What is obligatory on adults is obligatory on them (the young).' That was the view of Zufar and Malik. Then he retracted and said: 'One of them (is sufficient).' That is the view of Abu Yusuf and al-Shafi'i. The basis of his first view is that the name mentioned in the address (zakah on livestock) includes the young.
Source pages p. 61

Commentary
This passage covers two rulings: (1) Zakah on donkeys and mules: There is no zakah on these animals unless they are trade goods, due to the hadith that no revelation came about them. Zakah amounts are determined by divine command (samā'ī), not analogy. However, if they are purchased for trade, zakah applies based on their monetary value, as with other trade goods. (2) Zakah on young livestock (fislan: young camels; ajajil: young cows; himlan: young sheep): Abu Hanifa's final view is that no zakah is due on young animals alone unless accompanied by adult animals. This is also the view of Muhammad al-Shaybani. Earlier, Abu Hanifa held that the same zakah is due on young as on adults, which was the view of Zufar and Malik. Then he retracted and said one young animal can be given in place of an adult, which is the view of Abu Yusuf and al-Shafi'i. The reasoning for the initial view is that the term 'zakah on livestock' linguistically includes the young. The Hanafi school adopts the final view of no zakah on young alone, as this is more in line with the principle that zakah is on the adult, productive animals.

Key Terms
بغال (bighāl): Mules, offspring of horse and donkey.
حمير (hamīr): Donkeys.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, on which of the following animals is zakah due?
A) A donkey used for riding.
B) A mule used for plowing.
C) A mule purchased for resale in a market.
D) A horse used for racing.

Key Takeaway
Zakah on donkeys and mules is not obligatory by default; it only applies if they are held as trade goods.

Zakah on Young Livestock: The Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute with final ruling

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to outline the different Hanafi positions on zakah for young livestock and state the mufta bihi ruling.

Core Idea
Young livestock alone are exempt from zakah; only when accompanied by adults does zakah become due.

This lesson explores an important intra-Hanafi dispute regarding young camels, cows, and sheep. Imam Abu Hanifa himself changed his view over time, from requiring zakah on young animals to exempting them unless adult animals are present. Understanding the progression and the final relied-upon position is essential for accurate fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the animals
Young camels (fislan), young cows (ajajil), young sheep (himlan) are the subjects.
2
State the final Hanafi view
Abu Hanifa's final view: no zakah on young alone unless adults (kibar) are present. This is also the view of Muhammad al-Shaybani.
This is the mufta bihi.
3
Trace the earlier views
Abu Hanifa initially held that young animals are subject to the same zakah as adults. Then he retracted and said one young animal suffices (view of Abu Yusuf and Shafi'i). Finally, he adopted the view of no zakah unless with adults.
Zufar and Malik held the initial view.
4
Understand the basis
The initial view relied on the general term 'an'am (livestock) which includes young. The final view considers that zakah is on productive, adult animals.
The final view aligns with the Prophet's practice.
5
Apply the thamarah
If a person owns only young animals, no zakah. If they own both adults and young, zakah is due on the combined flock when nisab is reached, because adults are present.

Source Text

(Then from page 62) Section: There is no zakah on young camels, young cows, and young sheep according to Abu Hanifa unless adults are with them. This is his final view, and it is the view of Muhammad. He used to say initially: 'What is obligatory on adults is obligatory on them (the young).' That was the view of Zufar and Malik. Then he retracted and said: 'One of them (is sufficient).' That is the view of Abu Yusuf and al-Shafi'i. The basis of his first view is that the name mentioned in the address (zakah on livestock) includes the young.

Commentary
This passage covers two rulings: (1) Zakah on donkeys and mules: There is no zakah on these animals unless they are trade goods, due to the hadith that no revelation came about them. Zakah amounts are determined by divine command (samā'ī), not analogy. However, if they are purchased for trade, zakah applies based on their monetary value, as with other trade goods. عجاجيل (ʿajājīl): Young cows (calves).

Zakah on Horses: Intra-Hanafi Ikhtilaf on Male and Female
Intra-Hanafi dispute with qiyas and tarjih

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on zakah for male and female horses, explain the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf, and apply the concept of nama' (growth) to distinguish horses from other livestock.

Core Idea
Male horses alone lack nama', so no zakah; female horses can achieve nama' by borrowing a stallion, so zakah is wajib.

This passage addresses a nuanced intra-Hanafi dispute regarding zakah on horses. While the community often assumes all grazing livestock (sa'imah) incur zakah, horses are treated differently due to the nature of their growth (nama'). We will explore the reasoning behind the preponderant view that female horses require zakah but male horses alone do not, and the two narrations from Imam Abu Hanifa on each.

Guided Path
1
State the basic ruling and proof
Identify the general rule: zakah is obligatory on male horses alone? No. Why? Because horses' growth only comes from reproduction, which is impossible without females. Contrast with camels, cows, goats where growth also comes from meat and hair.
The ruling for male horses alone is no zakah.
2
Address the objection (qiyas objection)
Anticipate an objection: if male camels incur zakah despite no reproduction, why not male horses? Trace the response: the difference is alternative sources of growth (meat/hair) exist in other livestock but not in horses.
This shows the precision of qiyas with attention to 'illa (effective cause).
3
Identify the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on male horses
Imam Abu Hanifa has two narrations: one for wajib, one for not wajib. Understand the proof for each: the wajib narration analogizes to other sa'imah based on grazing; the not wajib narration focuses on lack of growth. The preponderant view is no zakah.
Tarjih (preference) is exercised based on the strength of the 'illa.
4
Identify the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on female horses
Similarly, two narrations: one for no zakah (no reproduction without a male), one for wajib (can borrow a stallion). The preponderant view is zakah wajib on female horses alone.
The possibility of achieving growth through external means suffices for nama'.
5
Summarize the mufta bihi position
The relied-upon ruling: male horses alone: no zakah; female horses alone: zakah wajib. For mixed herds, further rules apply (not covered here).
This is the operative fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تشريح مسئلہ بيان كيا گيا ہے کہ نرگھوڑوں میں زکوۃ واجب نہیں ہوتی دلیل یہ ہے کہ سوائم کے اندر زکوۃ واجب ہوتی ہے افزائش نسل کی وجہ سے اور تناسل تنہا گھوڑوں سے ممکن نہیں ہے اور اس لئے فقط گھوڑوں میں زکوۃ واجب نہیں ہے تاوقتیکہ ان کے ساتھ گھوڑیاں نہ ہوں۔ سوال: یہاں ایک سوال ہو سکتا ہے وہ یہ کہ تنہا نر اونٹ اور نر بقر اور بن غنم سے بھی تناسل ممکن نہیں ہے لیکن اس کے باوجود اس میں زکوۃ واجب ہے۔ جواب: زکوۃ واجب ہونے کے لئے نماء شرط ہے اور گھوڑوں میں نمو فقط تناسل سے ہوتا ہے اور تنہا نرگھوڑوں میں تناسل نہیں ہو سکتا۔ جب تک کہ ان کے ساتھ گھوڑیاں نہ ہوں پس تنہا نر گھوڑوں میں نما نہیں ہے اور جب نما نہیں تو ان میں زکوۃ بھی واجب نہ ہوگی۔ اور اونٹ، بقرا اور غنم میں جس طرح تناسل سے نما ہوتا ہے۔ اسی طرح ان کے گوشت اور ان کے بالوں سے بھی نما ہوتا ہے پس اونٹ 'بقر اور غنیم کے نروں میں اگر چہ تناسل سے نما ممکن نہیں لیکن گوشت اور بالوں سے نما، ممکن ہے اس لئے ان کے تنہا نروں میں بھی زکوۃ واجب ہو جائے گی ۔ حضرت امام ابوحنیفہ سے ایک روایت یہ ہے کہ تنہا نرگھوڑوں میں بھی زکوۃ واجب ہے۔ اس روایت کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ سائمہ گھوڑا تمام انواع سوائم کی نظیر ہے پس جس طرح دوسرے سوائم کے نروں میں سوم (جنگل میں چرنے) کی وجہ سے زکوۃ واجب ہوتی ہے۔ اسی طرح نرگھوڑے کے اندر بھی چرنے کی وجہ سے زکوۃ واجب ہوگی۔ حاصل بحث : حاصل یہ ہے کہ امام ابو حنیفہ سے نرگھوڑوں کی زکوۃ میں دو روایتیں ہیں۔ ایک وجوب کی، دوسری عدم وجوب کی لیکن عدم وجوب کی روایت راحج ہے۔ اسی طرح مادہ گھوڑیوں میں امام ابو حنیفہ سے دو روایتیں ہیں، ایک روایت عدم وجوب کی ہے۔ دوسری روایت وجوب کی ہے۔ پہلی روایت کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ تنہا گھوڑیوں میں بھی بذریعہ توالد و تناس نما نہیں ہوتا اس لئے ان میں زکوۃ بھی واجب نہ ہوگی۔ اور دوسری روایت کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ اگر کسی کی ملک میں فقط گھوڑیاں ہوں تو ان سے توالد و تناسل ممکن ہے اس طور پر کہ جفتی کے لئے کسی کا گھوڑا مستعار ہے لیا جائے پس جب تناسل ممکن ہے تو ان میں نما بھی پایا گیا۔ اور جب فقط گھوڑیوں میں نما پایا گیا تو ان میں زکوۃ بھی واجب ہوگی تنہا گھوڑیوں میں وجوب زکوۃ کی روایت راج ہے۔
Explanation: It has been stated that zakah is not obligatory on male horses. The proof is that zakah is obligatory on sa'imah (freely grazing) animals due to reproduction, and reproduction is not possible from male horses alone. Therefore, zakah is not obligatory on male horses only, unless they are accompanied by mares. Question: A question may arise here: from male camels, male cows, and male goats, reproduction is also not possible, yet zakah is obligatory on them. Answer: Growth (nama') is a condition for zakah, and the growth of horses only comes from reproduction, and male horses alone cannot reproduce. Unless they have mares, there is no growth in male horses alone. When there is no growth, zakah will not be obligatory. As for camels, cows, and goats, growth comes not only from reproduction but also from their meat and hair. Thus, even if reproduction is not possible from their males, growth is possible from meat and hair, so zakah becomes obligatory on their males. A narration from Imam Abu Hanifa states that zakah is obligatory on male horses as well. The proof for this narration is that the sa'imah horse is analogous to all types of sa'imah. So just as zakah is obligatory on male sa'imah due to grazing, similarly, zakah is obligatory on male horses due to grazing. Summary: The summary is that from Imam Abu Hanifa there are two narrations regarding zakah on male horses: one for obligation, the other for non-obligation, but the narration of non-obligation is preponderant. Similarly, regarding female horses, there are two narrations from Imam Abu Hanifa: one for non-obligation, the other for obligation. The proof for the first narration is that in female horses alone, growth through reproduction does not occur, so zakah will not be obligatory. The proof for the second narration is that if someone owns only mares, reproduction is possible by borrowing a stallion for mating. Since reproduction is possible, growth is found. And when growth is found in only mares, zakah becomes obligatory. The narration of obligation for only mares is preponderant.
Source pages p. 62

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding zakah on horses. It begins by stating the relied-upon ruling that male horses alone do not incur zakah because their growth (nama') is solely through reproduction, which is impossible with only males. The author anticipates an objection: why do male camels etc. incur zakah? The response explains that camels, cows, and goats have alternative forms of growth (meat and hair), so their males incur zakah. Then two narrations from Imam Abu Hanifa are presented for both male and female horses. For male horses, the preponderant view is no zakah. For female horses, the preponderant view is zakah, despite the lack of a stallion, because reproduction can be achieved by borrowing. This shows the meticulous analogical reasoning (qiyas) and preference (tarjih) within the Hanafi school. The lesson emphasizes that horses are treated differently from other sa'imah due to the nature of their growth.

Key Terms
سائمہ (sa'imah): Animals that graze freely in pasture for most of the year.
نما (nama'): Growth or increase that forms the basis for zakah obligation.
توالد و تناسل (tawallud wa tanasul): Reproduction and procreation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the preponderant Hanafi view, what is the ruling on zakah for female horses owned without any male horse?
A) Zakah is obligatory on female horses.
B) Zakah is not obligatory on female horses.
C) Zakah is obligatory only if they are for trade.
D) Zakah is obligatory if they are sa'imah and there is a male horse.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, the obligation of zakah on individual horses depends on the presence of growth (nama'); male horses alone incur no zakah; female horses alone incur zakah because growth can be achieved externally.

Zakah on Donkeys and Mules
States ruling on zakah for donkeys and mules with prophetic evidence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on zakah for donkeys and mules and explain the basis for the exception for trade goods.

Core Idea
No zakah on donkeys and mules unless they are trade goods; zakah measures are revealed, not analogical.

In this lesson, we examine a clear ruling from the Hanafi school regarding zakah on donkeys and mules. The passage establishes that these animals are not subject to livestock zakah because the Prophet ﷺ received no revelation concerning them. However, an important exception is made for trade purposes, illustrating the broader principle that zakah on trade goods is based on value, not animal type.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is being ruled upon? It is the obligation of zakah on donkeys and mules. The ruling is that no zakah is due on them as livestock.
The ruling is clear: no wajib zakah.
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites a hadith: 'Nothing has been revealed to me concerning them.' This is the primary evidence.
The dalil is a hadith that shows absence of revelation.
3
Understand the principle behind the ruling
The passage explains that zakah measures (maqadeer al-zakah) are sama'i (based on revelation), not qiyasi (analogical). Therefore, no obligation exists without textual basis.
This principle applies to all zakah categories.
4
Note the exception
If the animals are for trade, trade zakah becomes wajib because it is based on value, not animal type. This is consistent with zakah on other trade goods.
The exception is not for livestock zakah but for trade zakah.
5
Evaluate the cross-madhhab status
This ruling is muttafaq alayh (agreed upon) among the Hanafi school, with no intra-school disagreement mentioned. Other schools also generally hold no zakah on these animals.
It is a settled ruling in Hanafi fiqh.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
گدھوں ونچروں میں زکوۃ کا حکم : گدھوں اور خچروں میں زکو نہیں ہے۔ دلیل فرمان رسول لَمْ يَنْزِلُ عَلَى فِيهَا شَى ہے میرے اوپر گدھوں اور خچروں کی زکوۃ کے بارے میں کوئی چیز نازل نہیں کی گئی ہے۔ اور مقادیر زکوۃ سماعی ہیں، قیاسی اور عقلی نہیں ہیں۔ پس جب حضور صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم سے اس بارے میں کچھ سماع نہیں ہوا تو ان میں زکوۃ واجب نہ ہوگی ہاں اگر گدھے اور خچر تجارت کے لئے ہوں تو ان میں تجارتی زکوۃ واجب ہوگی۔ کیونکہ اس صورت میں زکوۃ مالیت کے ساتھ متعلق ہوگی جیسے دوسرے اموال تجارت میں زکوۃ مالیت کے ساتھ متعلق ہوتی ہے۔
The ruling on donkeys and mules: There is no zakah on donkeys and mules. The proof is the saying of the Messenger (ﷺ): 'Nothing has been revealed to me concerning them.' The measures of zakah are based on revelation (sama'i), not on analogy or reason. So when nothing was heard from the Prophet ﷺ regarding this, zakah is not obligatory on them. However, if donkeys and mules are for trade, then trade zakah is obligatory on them, because in that case zakah relates to their value, just as it relates to value in other trade goods.
Source pages p. 62

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof regarding zakah on donkeys and mules. It begins by stating the ruling: no zakah is due on these animals. The proof is a hadith that the Prophet ﷺ said nothing was revealed to him about zakah on donkeys and mules. The commentary explains that the amounts and conditions of zakah are established by divine revelation (sama'i), not by human reasoning (qiyas). Therefore, in the absence of revelation, no zakah is imposed. An exception is made: if these animals are kept for trade, then zakah applies because trade zakah is based on the value of the goods, not on the animal type. This highlights the principle that zakah on livestock is limited to explicitly mentioned categories, whereas zakah on trade goods covers all items of value.

Key Terms
مقادیر زکوۃ (maqadeer al-zakah): The specific measures and thresholds for zakah obligation.
سماعی (sama'i): Based on what is heard from the Prophet ﷺ or revelation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is there no zakah on donkeys and mules according to the Hanafi school?
A) Because they are not considered livestock.
B) Because the Prophet ﷺ did not prescribe zakah for them.
C) Because they are not grazing animals.
D) Because they are seldom owned.

Key Takeaway
Zakah on livestock applies only to animals explicitly mentioned by revelation; donkeys and mules are exempt unless they are trade goods.

Zakah on Young Livestock: Hanafi Position vs. Other Schools
Detailed intra- and inter-madhhab dispute on zakah for young animals

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi final ruling on zakah for young livestock, explain the reasoning behind Abu Hanifa's three views, and identify the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
Young livestock alone do not incur zakah in the Hanafi school unless accompanied by a mature animal.

This passage presents a detailed intra- and inter-madhhab dispute over the obligation of zakah on young camels, cows, and sheep. Imam Abu Hanifa (may Allah have mercy on him) is reported to have held three different views over time, with the final view being that no zakah is due on young animals unless they are accompanied by a mature animal. This lesson will guide you through the positions, the evidence for each, and the operative ruling for fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue
The central question: Are young livestock (fislan, 'ajajil, himlan) subject to zakah independently?
2
State Abu Hanifa's three views
Understand the progression: (1) initial: full zakah on young as on mature; (2) intermediate: one young animal; (3) final: no zakah unless with a mature animal.
Each view corresponds to a different madhhab alignment.
3
Analyze the evidence for each view
First view (Zufar, Malik): general noun in the nass includes all ages. Second view (Abu Yusuf, Shafi'i): careful consideration like lean animals. Third view (final Hanafi): nisab amounts are fixed by revelation and not subject to analogy.
Identify the dalil type for each: general noun, qiyas, and 'adam al-qiyas.
4
Determine the mufta bihi
The final view of Abu Hanifa, shared by Muhammad, is the relied-upon position. Abu Yusuf's views are also presented but not mufta bihi.
See the tarjih authority: 'This is his final view and it is the view of Muhammad.'
5
Identify the thamarah al-khilaf
Practical difference: Under the Hanafi final view, one does not pay zakah on young animals alone; under other views, one does (full or partial).
This directly affects the zakah calculation for livestock owners.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اونٹوں کے بچوں، گائے کے بچوں اور بکریوں کے بچوں میں زکوۃ کا حکم، اقوال فقہاء فَصَّلَّ، وَ لَيْسَ فِي الْفُصْلَانِ وَالْعَجَاجِيلِ وَالْحِمْلَانِ صَدَقَةً عِندَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ إِلَّا أَنْ يَكُونَ مَعَهَا كِبَارُ وَهَذَا آخِرُ اقوالِهِ وَهُوَ قَوْلُ مُحَمَّدٍ وَكَانَ يَقُولُ أَوَّلَا يَجِبُ فِيْهِمَا مَا يَجِبُ فِى الْمُسَانِ وَهُوَ قَولُ زُفُر و مَالِک ثُمَّ رَجَعَ و قَالَ فِيهَا وَاحِدٌ مِنْهَا وَهُوَ قَوْلُ أَبِى يُوسُفُ وَالشَّافِعِى وَجُهُ قَوْلِهِ الْأَوَّل أَنَّ الْإِسْمَ الْمَذْكُورِ فِى الْخِطَابِ يَنتَظِمُ الصِّغَارَ وَالْكِبَارَ وَ وَجُهُ الثَّانِي تَحْقِيقُ النَّظَرِ مِنَ الْجَانِبَيْنِ كَمَا يَجِبُ فِى الْمَهَازِيلِ وَاحِدٌ مِنْهَا وَوَجُهُ الأَخِيرِ أَنْ الْمَقَادِيرِ لَايَدْخُلُهَا القِياسُ فَإِذَا امْتَنَعَ إِيجَابُ مَا وَرَدَ بِهِ الشَّرُعُ امْتَنَعَ أَصْلًا وَإِذَا كَانَ فِيْهَا وَاحِدَةً مِنَ الْمُسَانِ جَعَلَ الكُلّ تبَعَالَهُ فِى انْعِقَادِهَا نِصَا بَادُونَ تَأدِيَةِ الزَّكوةِ ثُمَّ عِنْدَ أَبِى يُوْسَفَ لَا يَجِبُ فِي مَادُونَ الْأَرْبَعِينَ مِنَ الْحِمْلَانِ وَ فِيْمَا دُونَ الثَّلاثِينَ مِنَ الْعَجَاجِيْل وَ يَجِبُ فِى خَمْسٍ وَ عِشْرِينَ مِنَ الفُصْلَانِ وَاحِدُ ثُمَّ لاَ يَجِبُ شَئ حَتَّى تَبْلُغَ مَبْلَعًا لَوْ كَانَتْ مُسَانَّ يُتَنِى الْوَاجِبِ ثُمَّ لَا يَجِبُ شَى حَتَّى تَبْلُغَ مَبْلَغَا لَوْ كَانَتْ سِمَانٌ يُثلِثُ الْوَاجِبُ وَلَا يَجِبُ فِيمَا دُونَ خَمْسٍ وَ عِشْرِينَ فِي رِوَايَةٍ وَ عَنْهُ أَنَّهُ يَجِبُ فِى الْخَمْسِ حُمْسُ فَصِلٍ وَ فِى العَشَرِ حُمَسا فَصِيلِ عَلى هَذَا الاِعْتِبَارِ وَعَنْهُ أَنَّهُ يُنظَرُ إِلى قِيِّمَةِ حُمُسُ فَصِيلِ فِى الْخَمْسِ وَإِلَى قِيْمَةِ شَاةٍ وَسَطِ فَيَجِبُ اَقَلَهُمَا وَ فِى العَشْرِ إلى قِيمَةِ شَاتَينِ وَإِلَى قِيمَةِ حُمُسَى فَصِيل عَلى هذا الاِغْتِبَارِ ترجمہ فصل اور اونٹوں کے بچوں اور گائے کے بچوں میں ابوحنیفہ کے نزدیک زکوۃ نہیں ہے مگر جبکہ ان بچوں کے ساتھ بڑے بھی ہوں۔ اور یہ امام اعظم کا آخری قول ہے اور یہی امام محمد کا قول ہے۔ اور ابو حنیفہ پہلے یہ کہتے تھے کہ ان بچوں میں وہ واجب ہوگا جو مستہ جانوروں میں واجب ہوتا ہے۔ اور یہ امام زفر اور امام مالک کا قول ہے۔ پھر ابو حنیفہ نے رجوع کیا اور کہا کہ ان بچوں میں انہیں میں کا ایک واجب ہوگا۔ اور یہی امام شافعی اور امام ابو حنیفہ کا قول ہے۔ قول اول کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ نص میں جو لفظ مذکور ہے وہ چھوٹے اور بڑے سب کو شامل ہے ۔ اور قول دوم کی وجہ طرفین کا پورا لحاظ ہے جیسے دبلے پتلے جانوروں میں انہیں میں سے ایک واجب ہوتا ہے اور قول اخیر کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ مقادیر نصاب میں قیاس کو کوئی دخل نہیں ہے پس جب اس چیز کا واجب کرنا ممتنع ہو گیا جس پر شرع وارد ہوئی ہے تو بالکل ممتنع ہو گیا اور جب ان بچوں میں کوئی ایک بچہ مسنہ ہو تو یہ سب بچے اس مسنہ کے زکوۃ کا نصاب منعقد ہونے میں تابع شمار کئے جائیں گے نہ کہ زکوۃ ادا ہونے میں ۔ پھر امام ابو یوسف کے نزدیک چالیس غنم کے بچوں سے کم میں اور تمیں ۳۰ گائے کے بچوں سے کم میں زکوۃ واجب نہیں ہوگی ۔ اور اونٹ کے پھپیں (۲۵) بچوں میں ایک واجب ہے پھر ( زائد میں ) کچھ واجب نہیں ہے۔ یہاں تک کہ اس تعداد کو پہنچ جائیں کہ اگر منیں ہوتے تو دو (۲) واجب ہوتے۔ پھر زائد میں کچھ واجب نہیں ہے۔ یہاں تک کہ اس تعداد کو پہنچ جائیں کہ مسنیں ہوتے تو تین واجب ہوتے ۔ اور امام ابو یوسف کی ایک روایت کے مطابق اونٹ کے پچیس (۲۵) بچوں سے کم میں زکوۃ واجب نہیں ہے۔ اور ابو یوسف سے دوسری روایت میں یہ ہے کہ پانچ بچوں میں ایک فصیل کا پانچواں حصہ واجب ہے۔ اور دس (۱۰) میں ایک فیصل کے دو پانچویں واجب ہیں۔ علی ہذا القیاس در امام ابویوسف سے تیسری روایت میں یہ ہے کہ پانچ فصلان (اونٹ کے بچے) میں ایک فصیل کی قیمت کے پانچو میں حصہ کو اور ایک اوسط درجہ کی بکری کی قیمت کو دیکھیں ۔ جو کم ہو دہ واجب ہے اور دس فصلان کی صورت میں دو بکریوں کی قیمت اور ایک فصیل کے دو پانچویں کی قیمت کو دیکھیں۔ علی ہذا القیاس تشریح سابقہ فصلوں میں سوائم کی زکوۃ کا حکم بیان کیا گیا ہے۔ اس فصل میں صفار کا حکم مذکور ہے۔ فصلان فصیل کی جمع ہے۔ فصیل اونٹنی کا وہ بچہ جو ابھی ابن مخاض نہ ہوا ہو۔ یعنی اونٹنی کا بچہ جو بھی پہلے سال میں ہے اس کو فصیل کہتے ہیں ۔ بجا جیل بقول علامہ ابن الہام کے مجوں کی جمع ہے۔ اور ملا علی قاری نے شرح نقایہ میں کہا ہے کہ عجل کی جمع ہے۔ بہر حال مجول یا عجل گائے یا بھینس کا وہ بچہ جو
The ruling on young camels (fislan), young cows ('ajajil), and young sheep (himlan): The jurists differed. There is no zakah on fislan, 'ajajil, and himlan according to Abu Hanifa unless they are accompanied by mature animals. This is his final view and it is the view of Muhammad. He used to say initially that the same is obligatory on them as on mature animals, which is the view of Zufar and Malik. Then he retracted and said one from among them is obligatory, which is the view of Abu Yusuf and al-Shafi'i. The basis of his first view is that the noun mentioned in the address includes small and large. The basis of the second view is a careful consideration from both sides, just as in lean animals, one from among them is obligatory. The basis of the final view is that measurements are not subject to analogy. So when it is impossible to make obligatory what is mentioned in the Sharia, it is completely impossible. And if among them there is one mature animal, then all of them are considered followers of it in forming the nisab, not in paying the zakah. Then according to Abu Yusuf, there is no zakah on less than forty young sheep, and less than thirty young cows, and on twenty-five young camels, one is obligatory. Then nothing is obligatory until they reach a number that would require two if they were mature. Then nothing is obligatory until they reach a number that would require three if they were fat. And in one narration, nothing is obligatory below twenty-five. And from him (Abu Yusuf) another narration: on five, a fifth of a fasil (young camel) is obligatory; on ten, two-fifths of a fasil, and so on. And from him a third narration: on five, one looks at the value of a fifth of a fasil and the value of a medium sheep, and the lesser becomes obligatory; on ten, one looks at the value of two sheep and the value of two-fifths of a fasil, and so on. Explanation: In previous chapters, the ruling on sa'imah was given. In this chapter, the ruling on young ones is mentioned. Fislan is the plural of fasil. Fasil is a young camel that has not yet reached ibn makhad – i.e., the first-year offspring of a she-camel. 'Ajajil, according to Allama Ibn al-Humam, is the plural of majj or 'ijl, as stated by Mulla Ali Qari in Sharh al-Niqayah. In any case, it means a young cow or buffalo.
Source pages p. 62

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute regarding zakah on young livestock (fislan, 'ajajil, himlan). It presents three positions: (1) Abu Hanifa's final view (shared by Muhammad): no zakah on young unless accompanied by a mature animal. (2) Abu Hanifa's earlier view (shared by Zufar and Malik): the same zakah as on mature animals. (3) Abu Hanifa's intermediate view (shared by Abu Yusuf and Shafi'i): one young animal is given. The reasoning for each is given: the first considers the general noun includes all; the second balances both extremes; the third asserts that nisab amounts are fixed by revelation, not analogy. Then details of Abu Yusuf's views follow: different thresholds for different species, and three narrations on how to calculate. The explanation at the end defines the terms: fasil is a first-year camel calf, 'ajajil are cow calves. This shows the nuanced treatment of young animals in Hanafi fiqh, highlighting that zakah is not independently due on them until they reach maturity or are accompanied by mature animals.

Key Terms
فصيل (fasil): A young camel in its first year, before it becomes ibn makhad.
عجاجيل ('ajajil): Plural of 'ijl or majj, meaning a young cow or buffalo.
حملان (himlan): Young sheep or lambs.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the final view of Imam Abu Hanifa, when is zakah obligatory on young camels (fislan)?
A) When they number 25 or more.
B) Only if accompanied by a mature camel.
C) Always, as long as they are sa'imah.
D) When they reach the age of one year.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, young livestock alone do not incur zakah; the obligation arises only when a mature animal is present, reflecting the principle that zakah amounts are fixed by revelation and not subject to analogy.

Zakat — Almsgiving

Zakat on Young Livestock: The Three Positions of Imam Abu Hanifah
Intra-Hanafi dispute commentary on zakat for young animals.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three positions of Imam Abu Hanifah on zakat for young livestock, identify the final mufta bihi position, and explain the Hanafi proof that nisab amounts are not subject to qiyas.

Core Idea
Nisab amounts are fixed by revelation; qiyas cannot determine them, so young animals alone do not trigger zakat.

This lesson dives into a famous intra-Hanafi dispute where Imam Abu Hanifah changed his view twice in a single sitting, producing three distinct positions on zakat for young livestock. Understanding this development reveals how the Hanafi school prioritizes textual certainty over analogy when the Shari'ah has fixed specific thresholds. We will trace the reasoning behind each position, the decisive proof for the final view, and the practical implication for fatwa today.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three positions of Imam Abu Hanifah
List the three views he expressed: (1) zakat like mature animals, (2) one young animal from among them, (3) no zakat unless with a mature animal.
These correspond to the views of Zufar/Malik, Abu Yusuf/Shafi'i, and Muhammad (final of Abu Hanifah).
2
Examine the proofs for each position
First view uses generality of the text (young and old). Second view analogizes to thin animals where one is taken. Third view holds that nisab amounts are fixed and not subject to qiyas.
The third view rejects analogy because it cannot determine specific amounts.
3
Trace the development to the final position
Imam Abu Hanifah first adopted the first view, then retracted to the second after Abu Yusuf's objection about value, then finally settled on the third when Abu Yusuf noted that young animals cannot be taken in zakat.
This story from al-'Inayah shows his ijtihad and humility.
4
Apply the Hanafi principle that nisab is not subject to qiyas
Understand that the Shari'ah fixed specific numbers (e.g., 5 camels, 40 sheep). These cannot be extended or modified by analogy. Therefore, if the text does not explicitly obligate zakat on young animals alone, it remains non-obligatory.
This is the key usul principle underlying the final position.
5
Identify the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
If one has only young animals (e.g., 40 young goats), the Hanafi mufta bihi says no zakat; the opposing views say zakat is due. If young animals accompany a mature that completes the nisab, all agree zakat is due on the whole.
The difference only arises when young animals are alone.
