⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
صاحب ہدایہ نے فرمایا کہ اگر ان بچوں میں کوئی ایک بھی منہ یعنی ایک سال سے زائد کا ہو تو یہ سب بچے اس مسئہ کے تابع ہوں گے مگر نصاب منعقد ہونے میں تابع ہیں نہ کہ ادائے زکوۃ میں مثلاً کسی کے پاس انتالیس حملان ( بکری کے سال بھر سے کم کے بچے ہیں اور ایک مسنہ ہے یعنی ایک سال سے زائد عمر کی بکری ہے تو اس صورت میں امام ابو حنیفہ اور امام محمد کے نزدیک بھی زکوۃ کا نصاب منعقد ہو جائے گا۔ اور اس انعقاد نصاب میں تمام صغار کو اس ایک منہ کے تابع شمار کیا جائے گا۔ البتہ زکوۃ ادا ہونے میں صغار کہار کے تابع شمار نہیں ہوں گے یعنی زکوۃ میں فقط مسنہ (ایک سالہ بکر ہی ) ہی دیا جائے گا حمل ایک سال سے کم کا بچہ دینے سے زکوۃ ادانہ ہوگی ۔ یہ بھی خیال رہے کہ طرفین کے نزدیک کبار میں سے زکوۃ ادا کرنا اس وقت واجب ہوگا۔ جبکہ مقدار واجب نصاب کے اندر موجود بھی ہو۔ اور اگر مقدار واجب موجود نہ ہوتو واجب نہ ہوگا۔ مثلا ایک صاحب کے پاس ایک سوانفیس حمل ( بکری کے سال بھر سے کم کے بچے ) ہیں اور دو سنیں (سال بھر سے زائد کے ) نہیں تو اس صورت میں دو سنیں واجب ہو جائیں گے کیونکہ ایک سو اکیس بکریوں میں دو بکریاں واجب ہوتی ہیں اور اگر ایک سو میں حمل ہوں اور ایک مسنہ ہو تو طرفین کے نزدیک فقط ایک مسنہ واجب ہوگا۔ اور ابو یوسف کے نزدیک ایک مسنہ اور ایک حمل واجب ہوگا کیونکہ طرفین کے نزدیک حمل کو زکوۃ میں نہیں لیا جاتا بلکہ مسنہ لیا جاتا ہے اور اس صورت میں مقدار واجب یعنی دو مسنیں موجود نہیں ہے۔ اس لئے جو موجود ہے یعنی ایک مسنہ اس کو لے لیا جائے گا۔ اور باقی کو چھوڑ دیا جائے گا۔ اور امام ابو یوسف کے نزدیک چونکہ حمل سے بھی زکوۃ ادا ہو جاتی ہے اس لئے ایک مسنہ لے لیا جائے اور ایک حمل لے لیا جائے اسی پر اونٹ اور بقر کے بچوں کو قیاس کیا جائے گا۔ (فتح القدیر) اور اگر کسی کے پاس ایک سو بیس حمل ہوں اور ایک مسند ہو اور سال گذر کر منہ مر گیا تو طرفین کے نزدیک باقی بچوں میں زکوۃ باطل ہوگئی ۔ اور اگر بچے مر گئے اور مسنہ رہ گیا تو اس کا چالیسواں حصہ لیا جائے گا۔ اور امام ابو یوسف کے نزدیک مسنہ مرجانے کی صورت میں حمل کا چالیسواں حصہ ساقط ہوگا۔
The author of Hidayah said: If among these young animals there is any one musinnah (one year old or more), then all these young animals will be subject to this issue, but they are subordinate in the formation of the nisab, not in the payment of zakat. For example, someone has forty-nine hamlaan (kids of goats less than one year) and one musinnah (a goat more than one year old), then in this case according to Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad, the nisab for zakat will be established. And in this establishment of nisab, all the young ones will be considered subordinate to that one musinnah. However, in the payment of zakat, the young ones will not be considered subordinate to the older ones, i.e., only the musinnah (one-year-old goat) will be given as zakat; giving a haml (young one less than one year) will not fulfill zakat. Also note that according to the two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad), paying zakat from mature animals is obligatory only when the required quantity is present within the nisab. And if the required quantity is not present, it will not be obligatory. For example, a person has one hundred and one hamlaan (young goats) and does not have two sunn (two-year-olds), then in this case two sunn will be obligatory because one hundred and twenty-one goats require two goats. And if one hundred are hamlaan and one is musinnah, then according to the two only one musinnah is obligatory. And according to Abu Yusuf, one musinnah and one haml are obligatory because according to the two, a haml is not accepted for zakat, only a musinnah is taken, and in this case the required quantity of two musinnah is not present. Therefore, what is present, i.e., one musinnah, will be taken, and the remainder will be omitted. And according to Imam Abu Yusuf, since zakat can be paid from a haml, therefore one musinnah will be taken and one haml will be taken, and by analogy the same applies to young camels and cows. (Fath al-Qadir) And if someone has one hundred and twenty hamlaan and one musinnah, and after the year passes the musinnah dies, then according to the two the zakat becomes invalid for the remaining animals. And if the young ones die and the musinnah remains, then one-fortieth of it will be taken. And according to Imam Abu Yusuf, in the case of the death of the musinnah, one-fortieth of the haml will be dropped.
Source pages p. 66

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding zakat on sheep and goats when young animals (hamlaan) are mixed with a mature one (musinnah). The author of Hidayah explains that according to Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad, the nisab is established by considering the mature animal as the basis, but the zakat payment must be from mature animals. They require that the exact number of mature animals prescribed for that nisab be present. Abu Yusuf allows paying from young animals as well, so he would take a haml if the prescribed mature number is not fully present. The passage also covers cases where animals die after the year, affecting zakat obligation.

Key Terms
حمل (haml): A young goat or sheep less than one year old.
مسنہ (musinnah): A goat or sheep that has entered its second year (one year old or more).
نصاب (nisab): The minimum threshold of wealth that makes zakat obligatory.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If someone has 49 hamlaan and 1 musinnah, what is the obligatory zakat according to Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad?
A) One musinnah only
B) One haml only
C) One musinnah and one haml
D) No zakat is due

Key Takeaway
Young animals count for zakat nisab but are not acceptable for payment in the relied-upon Hanafi position.

Zakat on Young Camels: The Views of Imam Abu Yusuf
Ruling on zakat on young camels with detailed narrations from Abu Yusuf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three narrations of Imam Abu Yusuf regarding zakat on young camels and calculate the obligation for numbers above 25 by analogy with adult camels.

Core Idea
Abu Yusuf's three views on zakat for young camels below 25: nothing, fractional shares, or lesser of fraction vs goat value.

Imam Abu Yusuf held that zakat is obligatory on young camels (fussalaan) themselves, not just on their owners. However, multiple narrations from him give different methods for calculating the amount when the herd is below 25. This lesson unpacks those narrations and the later clarification from the author of Al-Hidayah on how to handle larger numbers.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core ruling and dispute
Recognize that Imam Abu Yusuf considers young camels as zakatable property. The dispute is about how to calculate zakat when the number is below 25.
For numbers 25 and above, the same thresholds as adult camels apply (e.g., 25→1, 76→2, 145→3, etc.).
2
Analyze the first narration (no zakat below nisab)
According to one narration, nothing is due on fewer than 25 young camels, just as for adult camels
This is the most conservative view.
3
Examine the second narration (fractional shares)
This narration divides the obligation into fifths: 5 young camels require 1/5 of a young camel, 10 require 2/5, etc., until 25 require 1 full.
It treats the obligation as proportional to the herd size.
4
Understand the third narration (lesser of two values)
This method compares one-fifth of the price of a young camel to the price of an average goat; the lesser value is given.
This incorporates a valuation approach.
5
Apply the Hidayah's explanation for numbers above 25
For numbers beyond 25, the author confirms that the same thresholds as adult camels should be applied, using the numbers 76, 145, 196, etc.
This maintains consistency with the standard zakat schedule.

ثُمَّ عند ابی یوسف سے امام ابو یوسف کے قول کی تشریح کی گئی ہے چونکہ امام ابو یوسف کے نزدیک حملان عجا جیل اور فصلان کے اندرز کو ۃ واجب ہوتی ہے۔ اور انہیں میں سے واجب ہوتی ہے اس لئے امام ابو یوسف نے فرمایا کہ بچوں کے اندرز کو وہ اسی وقت واجب ہوگی جبکہ نصاب کی مقدار کو پہنچ جائیں۔ چنانچہ چالیس حملان سے کم میں اور میں بھا جیل سے کم میں زکوۃ واجب نہیں ہے جیسے اس وقت جبکہ یہ بڑے ہوں تو اس نصاب سے کم میں زکوۃ واجب نہیں ہوتی ۔ اور اونٹ کے فصیل یعنی بچوں میں جبکہ پچیس ہوں تو ایک بچہ واجب ہے۔ پچھیں بچوں کے اندر ایک بچہ کا واجب ہونا یہ تو ٹھیک ہے یعنی برے اونٹوں میں چھتیں پر ایک بنت لبون اور چھیالیس پر ایک حقہ تھا۔ پس بچوں کی صورت میں چھتیں اور چھیالیس پر کیا واجب ہوگا۔ اس کے جواب میں صاحب ہدایہ نے فرمایا کہ پچھیں بچوں سے زائد میں کچھ واجب نہ ہوگا یہاں تک کہ بچوں کی تعداد اس مقدار کو پہنچ جائے کہ اگر یہ بڑے اونٹ ہوتے تو اس میں شئی واجب دو ہوتی مثلاً چھپتر اونٹوں میں دو بنت لبون واجب ہوتی ہیں تو چھہتر بچوں میں دو بچے واجب ہوں گے پھر چھہتر سے زائد میں کچھ واجب نہ ہوگا۔ یہاں تک کہ بچوں کی تعداد اس مقدار کو پہنچ جائے کہ اگر یہ بڑے اونٹ ہوتے تو ان میں تین واجب ہوتے مثلا ایک سو پینتالیس اونٹوں میں تین حقہ واجب ہوتے ہیں۔ تو ایک سو پینتالیس بچوں میں تین بچے واجب ہوں گے۔ اسی طرح ایک سو چھیانوے اونٹوں میں چار حصے واجب ہیں لہذا ایک سو چھیانوے بچوں میں چار بچے واجب ہوں گے، علی ہذا القیاس اور اونٹ کے پچیس سے کم بچوں میں امام ابو یوسف کی ایک روایت کے مطابق کچھ واجب نہ ہوگا۔ اور دوسری روایت یہ ہے کہ پانچ بچوں میں ایک بچہ کا پانچواں حصہ واجب ہوگا ۔ دس میں دو پانچویں اور پندرہ میں تین پانچویں اور میں میں چار پانچویں اور پچھپیس میں پورا ایک بچہ واجب ہوگا اور امام ابو یوسف سے تیسری روایت یہ ہے کہ پانچ فصلان (اونٹ کے بچوں ) کی صورت میں ایک فصیل (اونٹ کا بچہ ) کی قیمت کے پانچویں حصہ کو اور ایک اوسط درجہ کی بکری کی قیمت کو دیکھیں پس جو دونوں میں سے کم ہو وہ واجب ہے یعنی اگر فصیل کی قیمت کا پانچواں حصہ کم ہے اور بکری کی قیمت زائد ہے تو فصیل کی قیمت کا پانچواں حصہ واجب ہوگا۔ اور اگر بر عکس ہے تو بکری واجب ہوگی۔ اور اونٹ کے دس بچوں کی صورت میں اوسط درجہ کی دو بکریوں کی قیمت اور فصیل کی قیمت کے دو پانچویں حصوں کی مقدار کو دیکھیں جو کم ہو وہ واجب ہے اسی پر پندرہ اور میں فصلان کی صورتوں کو قیاس کیا جائے مثلاً پندرہ فصلان میں اوسط درجہ کی تین بکریوں کی قیمت اور فصیل کی قیمت کے تین پانچویں حصوں کی مقدار کو دیکھیں جو کم ہو وہ واجب ہے۔ واللہ اعلم
Then at Abu Yusuf: Explanation of Imam Abu Yusuf's statement is given because according to Imam Abu Yusuf, zakat is obligatory on hamlaan (kids), 'ajaajil (young goats), and fusaalaan (young camels), and it is obligatory from among them. Therefore, Imam Abu Yusuf said that zakat on young animals becomes obligatory only when they reach the quantity of the nisab. Thus, for less than forty hamlaan and less than [something] young goats, zakat is not obligatory, just as when they are adult, zakat is not obligatory for less than that nisab. And for young camels (fusul) when they are twenty-five, one young camel is obligatory. For twenty-five young animals, one being obligatory is correct, i.e., for bad [low quality] camels, at thirty-six one bint labun, and at forty-six one hiqqah. So for young animals, at thirty-six and forty-six what will be obligatory? In response, the author of Hidayah said: For more than twenty-five young animals, nothing will be obligatory until the number of young animals reaches the quantity at which, if they were adult camels, something would be obligatory. For example, at seventy-six adult camels two bint labun are obligatory, so at seventy-six young animals two young ones are obligatory. Then for more than seventy-six, nothing is obligatory until the number reaches the point where if adult, three would be obligatory, e.g., at one hundred forty-five adult camels three hiqqah are obligatory, so at one hundred forty-five young animals three young ones are obligatory. Similarly, at one hundred ninety-six adult camels four shares are obligatory, so at one hundred ninety-six young animals four young ones are obligatory, and so on by analogy. And for less than twenty-five young camels, according to one narration of Abu Yusuf, nothing is obligatory. And the second narration is that for five young ones, one-fifth of a young camel is obligatory; for ten, two-fifths; for fifteen, three-fifths; for twenty, four-fifths; and for twenty-five, one full young camel. And the third narration from Abu Yusuf is that for five fasaalaan (young camels), look at one-fifth of the price of a fasil (young camel) and the price of an average goat; whichever is less is obligatory. So if one-fifth of the price of a fasil is less and the price of a goat is more, then one-fifth of the price of a fasil is obligatory. And if vice versa, then a goat is obligatory. And for ten young camels, look at the price of two average goats and two-fifths of the price of a fasil; whichever is less is obligatory. Similarly for fifteen and twenty, analogize. So for fifteen fasaalaan, look at the price of three average goats and three-fifths of the price of a fasil; whichever is less is obligatory. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 66

Commentary
This passage discusses the detailed rulings of Imam Abu Yusuf regarding zakat on young camels. He considers that young camels themselves are subject to zakat when they reach the nisab thresholds equivalent to mature camels. The author of Hidayah explains that for numbers above the first threshold (25), the obligation increases only when the count reaches the next threshold where adult camels would require more. For numbers below 25, Abu Yusuf has three narrations: (1) no zakat, (2) fractional shares of a young camel based on increments of five, and (3) comparing the value of the fraction to that of an average goat and taking the lesser. This shows the flexibility within the Hanafi school in calculating zakat on animals that have not reached maturity.

Key Terms
فصیل (fasil): A young camel before it completes its first year.
فصلان (fussalaan): Plural of fasil; young camels.
قیمت (qimah): Price or value; used to determine the lesser of two amounts in zakat calculation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the second narration of Imam Abu Yusuf, what is the zakat on 10 young camels?
A) One young camel
B) Two-fifths of a young camel
C) Two goats
D) No zakat

Key Takeaway
Imam Abu Yusuf's multiple narrations on zakat for young camels below 25 illustrate the flexibility of Hanafi fiqh in determining obligations.

Ruling When the Prescribed Zakat Animal is Unavailable
Ruling on alternatives when the specific zakat animal is absent

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on taking value (qiimah) in zakat and apply the collector's options when the prescribed animal is absent.

Core Idea
Zakat must be paid even if the exact animal is missing — the collector may take a higher or lower animal with compensation.

When a person owes a specific type of animal for zakat (e.g., a musinnah) but does not have it, the Hanafi school provides a practical solution. The collector can either take a superior animal and refund the surplus, or take an inferior animal and collect the deficit. This ruling is based on the permissibility of taking value (qiimah) in zakat, a distinctive Hanafi position supported by the hadith forbidding the best properties.

Guided Path
1
Identify the obligation
Determine what animal is wajib as zakat (e.g., a musinnah for camels of a certain number). The prescribed animal is of average quality.
2
Recognize the scenario
The owner does not possess the exact prescribed animal. The zakat obligation remains, but the method of payment changes.
3
Understand the collector's options
First option: take a superior animal and return the surplus value. Second option: take an inferior animal and collect the difference. Both are permissible.
4
Note the legal basis
The Hanafi school allows taking value (qiimah) in zakat based on istihsan and the principle of ease. This is opposed by the Shafi'i school.
5
Distinguish the two options
The first option is considered a purchase (shira'), so the collector has discretion to accept or demand the exact animal or its value. The second option is direct zakat payment (i'taa'), so the collector must accept it.
This distinction affects the collector's authority.

Source Text

زکوۃ میں جو جانور دینا لازم ہوا اگر وہ مالک کے پاس نہ ہو تو کس طرح زکوۃ ادا کرے قَالَ وَمَنْ وَجَبَ عَلَيْهِ مُسِنُّ فَلَمْ يُوْجَدْ أَخَذَ الْمُصَدِّقُ أَعْلَى مِنْهَا وَرَدَّ الْفَضْلَ أوْ اَخَذَ دُونَهَا وَأَخَذَ الْفَضْلَ وَهذَا يَبْتَنِى عَلَى أَنَّ أَخَذُ الْقِيْمَةٍ فِى بَابِ الزَّكوةِ جَائِزَ عِنْدَنَا عَلَى مَانَذَكُرُهُ إِن شَاءَ اللهُ إِلَّا أَنَّ فِي الْوَجهِ الْأَوَّلِ لَهُ أَنْ لا يَأخُذُو يُطَالِبُهُ بِعَيْنِ الْوَاجِبِ أَوْ بِقِيْمَتِهِ لِأَنَّهُ شِرَاءُ وَ فِى الْوَجهِ الثَّانِي يُجْبَرُ لأَنَّهُ لَا بَيْعٌ فِيهِ بَلْ هُوَ اعطاء بِالْقِيْمَةِ ترجمہ مصنف نے کہا ہے کہ اور جس شخص پر مسن ( ذات سن ) واجب ہوا تو مصدق اس سے اعلیٰ کو لے کر زیادتی کو پھیر دے۔ یا ادنی کو لے کر اور زیادتی کو لے ۔ اور یہ اس پر مبنی ہے کہ باب زکوۃ میں قیمت لینا ہمارے نزدیک جائز ہے۔ ہم اس کو ان شاء اللہ ذکر کریں گے۔ مگر پہلی صورت میں مصدق کو اختیار ہے کہ وہ اعلیٰ جانور کو نہ لے۔ اور مالک سے عین واجب کا مطالبہ کرے یا اس کی قیمت کا کیونکہ یہ تو خرید کرتا ہے اور دوسری صورت میں مصدق کو مجبور کیا جائے گا۔ کیوں کہ اس میں مبیع نہیں ہے بلکہ قیمت کے ذریعہ زکوۃ دینا ہے۔ تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ زکوۃ میں اوسط درجہ کا جانور واجب ہوتا ہے نہ بہت گھٹیا اور نہ بہت بڑھیا۔ چنانچہ اگر کسی پر بنت لبون واجب ہوا تو عامل اور مصدق ( زکوۃ وصول کرنے والا ) نہ تو اعلیٰ درجہ کا بنت لبون لے اور نہ ادنیٰ درجہ کا لے۔ بلکہ ان دونوں کے درمیان کا وصول کر لے ۔ کیونکہ رسول اکرم صلى الله عليه وسلم نے حضرت معاذ رضی اللہ عنہ کو جب یمن کا حکم بنا کر بھیجا تو فرمایا تھا۔ ايَّاكَ وَ كَرَائِمَ أَمْوَالِهِمْ یعنی زَكرة
Regarding the animal that becomes obligatory to give in zakat, if it is not present, how to pay zakat? He said: And the person upon whom a musinn (tooth-aged) is obligatory, and it is not found, then the collector (musaddiq) takes a better one and returns the excess, or takes a lower one and takes the excess. And this is based on the fact that taking the value (qiimah) in the chapter of zakat is permissible according to us, as we will mention if Allah wills. Except that in the first case, the collector has the option not to take [the better] and demand from him the exact obligatory or its value, because this is a purchase. And in the second case, he is compelled, because there is no sale in it; rather it is giving zakat by value. Translation: The author said: And the person upon whom a musinn (tooth-aged) is obligatory, the collector takes a better from him and returns the surplus, or takes a lower and takes the surplus. And this is based on the permissibility of taking value in the chapter of zakat according to us. We will mention this if Allah wills. But in the first case, the collector has the option not to take [the better] and demand from the owner the exact obligatory or its value because it is a purchase. And in the second case, he is compelled because there is no sale in it; rather it is giving zakat by value. Explanation: The issue is that in zakat, an average animal is obligatory, neither very inferior nor very superior. So if a bint labun is obligatory on someone, the agent and collector should not take a superior bint labun nor an inferior one, but should take between them. Because the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, when he sent Mu'adh ibn Jabal as governor to Yemen, said: 'Iyyaaka wa karaaima amwaalihim' i.e., avoid their best properties as zakat.
Source pages p. 67

Commentary
This passage provides the ruling when the exact prescribed animal for zakat is not available in the owner's possession. The collector has two options: either take a superior animal and refund the surplus value, or take an inferior animal and collect the difference in value. This is based on the Hanafi principle that taking value (qiimah) in zakat is permissible, unlike the Shafi'i view. However, the first option (taking higher) is considered a purchase, so the collector has discretion; the second option (taking lower) is compulsory because it is a direct zakat payment. The text emphasizes that the zakat should be from average quality, citing the hadith where the Prophet forbade taking the best properties of people as zakat.

Key Terms
مصدق (musaddiq): The official zakat collector appointed by the Islamic state.
قیمت (qiimah): Value or price; in zakat, taking the market value instead of the specific animal is permissible according to the Hanafi school.
مسن (musinn): An animal that has entered its second year, i.e., a mature animal.

According to the Hanafi ruling in this passage, what happens when the prescribed zakat animal is not available?
A) The zakat obligation is deferred until the animal is found.
B) The collector must take a superior animal without compensation.
C) The collector may take a superior animal with refund or an inferior animal with extra payment.
D) The owner must purchase the prescribed animal at any cost.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, when the exact zakat animal is absent, paying its value (qiimah) or taking a substitute with compensation is permissible, based on the principle of ease.

Zakat on Young Camels: Qiyas and Abu Yusuf's Narrations
Explains zakat calculation for young camels using adult camel thresholds and Abu Yusuf's variants.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to derive zakat obligations for young camels using analogical reasoning and identify the three narrations of Imam Abu Yusuf for herds under 25.

Core Idea
Young camels follow adult thresholds by qiyas; under 25, Abu Yusuf offers three views.

This lesson tackles the zakat calculation for a herd consisting entirely of young camels (under one year). The Hanafi school uses a clear analogy to adult camel thresholds for herds of 25 or more. However, when the number of young camels is less than 25, Imam Abu Yusuf has three different narrations, leading to practical variability. Understanding this ikhtilaf is crucial for a mufti.

Guided Path
1
Understand the adult camel zakat schedule
Recall the standard zakat brackets for adult camels: 25-35 camels: one bint makhad (1-year-old); 36-45: one bint labun (2-year-old); 46-60: one hikkah (3-year-old); 61-75: one jadha'ah (4-year-old); 76-90: two bint labun; and so on up to 196+: four hikkah. These thresholds are fixed in the Shariah.
The specific age categories are important for the analogy.
2
Apply the qiyas to young camels (25 or more)
According to Sahib al-Hidayah, for a herd of 25 or more young camels (under one year), the zakat obligation is exactly the same as for adult camels, except that the animal given is a young camel of the same age as the herd. For example, 25 young camels require one young camel; 36 young camels also require one young camel (since 36 is between 25 and 75, only one is due); 76 young camels require two young camels; and so on.
The threshold where the number increases (e.g., 76) is taken from the adult schedule.
3
Examine the ruling for fewer than 25 young camels
For a herd of less than 25 young camels, the main Hanafi position (via qiyas) is that no zakat is due, because the nisab has not been reached. However, Imam Abu Yusuf has three narrations that provide alternatives.
This ikhtilaf is the focus of the later steps.
4
Identify the three narrations of Imam Abu Yusuf
First narration: no zakat is due on fewer than 25 young camels. Second narration: a fractional system is used – for every 5 young camels, one-fifth of a young camel is due (so 5 young: 0.2 young; 10 young: 0.4 young; 15 young: 0.6 young; 20 young: 0.8 young; 25 young: 1 full young). Third narration: compare one-fifth of the value of a young camel with the value of an average goat; the lesser of the two is due. For multiples, scale accordingly (e.g., for 10 young, compare two-fifths value of a young camel with the value of two goats).
The third narration introduces a value-based calculation.
5
Evaluate the practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf)
The three narrations produce different obligations. For example, for 15 young camels: narration 1 gives 0; narration 2 gives three-fifths of a young camel (value-based); narration 3 gives the lesser of three-fifths of a young camel's value or the value of three goats. The mufta bihi is not specified in this text, so a mufti may choose based on contextual need.
This flexibility is characteristic of later Hanafi practice where multiple valid views exist.

پچھیں بچوں کے اندر ایک بچہ کا واجب ہونا یہ تو ٹھیک ہے یعنی برے اونٹوں میں چھتیں پر ایک بنت لبون اور چھیالیس پر ایک حقہ تھا۔ پس بچوں کی صورت میں چھتیں اور چھیالیس پر کیا واجب ہوگا۔ اس کے جواب میں صاحب ہدایہ نے فرمایا کہ پچھیں بچوں سے زائد میں کچھ واجب نہ ہوگا یہاں تک کہ بچوں کی تعداد اس مقدار کو پہنچ جائے کہ اگر یہ بڑے اونٹ ہوتے تو اس میں شئی واجب دو ہوتی مثلاً چھپتر اونٹوں میں دو بنت لبون واجب ہوتی ہیں تو چھہتر بچوں میں دو بچے واجب ہوں گے پھر چھہتر سے زائد میں کچھ واجب نہ ہوگا۔ یہاں تک کہ بچوں کی تعداد اس مقدار کو پہنچ جائے کہ اگر یہ بڑے اونٹ ہوتے تو ان میں تین واجب ہوتے مثلا ایک سو پینتالیس اونٹوں میں تین حقہ واجب ہوتے ہیں۔ تو ایک سو پینتالیس بچوں میں تین بچے واجب ہوں گے۔ اسی طرح ایک سو چھیانوے اونٹوں میں چار حصے واجب ہیں لہذا ایک سو چھیانوے بچوں میں چار بچے واجب ہوں گے، علی ہذا القیاس اور اونٹ کے پچیس سے کم بچوں میں امام ابو یوسف کی ایک روایت کے مطابق کچھ واجب نہ ہوگا۔ اور دوسری روایت یہ ہے کہ پانچ بچوں میں ایک بچہ کا پانچواں حصہ واجب ہوگا ۔ دس میں دو پانچویں اور پندرہ میں تین پانچویں اور میں میں چار پانچویں اور پچھپیس میں پورا ایک بچہ واجب ہوگا اور امام ابو یوسف سے تیسری روایت یہ ہے کہ پانچ فصلان (اونٹ کے بچوں ) کی صورت میں ایک فصیل (اونٹ کا بچہ ) کی قیمت کے پانچویں حصہ کو اور ایک اوسط درجہ کی بکری کی قیمت کو دیکھیں پس جو دونوں میں سے کم ہو وہ واجب ہے یعنی اگر فصیل کی قیمت کا پانچواں حصہ کم ہے اور بکری کی قیمت زائد ہے تو فصیل کی قیمت کا پانچواں حصہ واجب ہوگا۔ اور اگر بر عکس ہے تو بکری واجب ہوگی۔ اور اونٹ کے دس بچوں کی صورت میں اوسط درجہ کی دو بکریوں کی قیمت اور فصیل کی قیمت کے دو پانچویں حصوں کی مقدار کو دیکھیں جو کم ہو وہ واجب ہے اسی پر پندرہ اور میں فصلان کی صورتوں کو قیاس کیا جائے مثلاً پندرہ فصلان میں اوسط درجہ کی تین بکریوں کی قیمت اور فصیل کی قیمت کے تین پانچویں حصوں کی مقدار کو دیکھیں جو کم ہو وہ واجب ہے۔ واللہ اعلم
It is correct that one young camel is wajib for twenty-five young camels. For adult camels, on thirty-six there is one bint labun and on forty-six one hikkah. So for young camels, what is wajib for thirty-six and forty-six? Sahib al-Hidayah responded: From twenty-five young camels onward, nothing extra is wajib until the number of young camels reaches the amount where two animals would be wajib if they were adult. For example, for seventy-six adult camels, two bint labun are wajib, so for seventy-six young camels, two young camels are wajib. Then from seventy-six onward nothing is wajib until the number reaches two hundred and forty-five [etc.]. For less than twenty-five young camels, according to one narration of Imam Abu Yusuf, nothing is wajib. The second narration: for five young camels, one-fifth of a young camel is wajib; for ten, two-fifths; for fifteen, three-fifths; for twenty, four-fifths; for twenty-five, one full young camel. The third narration from Imam Abu Yusuf: look at one-fifth of the value of a young camel and the value of an average goat; whichever is less is wajib. For ten young camels, look at the value of two average goats and two-fifths of a young camel's value; whichever is less is wajib. And similarly for fifteen and twenty. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 67

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding zakat on young camels. The main ruling, stated by Sahib al-Hidayah, is that zakat on young camels is calculated by analogy to adult camel thresholds. For a herd of young camels numbering between 25 and 75, one young camel is wajib. Beyond that, the number increases in the same increments as adult camels (e.g., 76 young camels require two young camels). For less than 25 young camels, Imam Abu Yusuf has three different narrations: (1) no zakat, (2) fractional shares based on a fifth system, and (3) a comparison between the fractional value of a young camel and the value of goats, with the lesser being wajib. The text does not specify which is the relied-upon position, concluding with 'Wallahu A'lam'.

Key Terms
بچہ (bacha): A young camel, specifically a foal (fashil), less than one year old.
فصیل (fasil): Synonym for بچہ, a young camel.
بنت لبون (bint labun): A female camel that has completed two years and entered its third year; a category in zakat.
حقہ (hikkah): A female camel that has completed three years and entered its fourth year; another zakat category.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the main ruling (qiyas) presented in the passage, if a person owns 60 young camels, how many young camels are wajib as zakat?
A) One young camel
B) Two young camels
C) Three young camels
D) Nothing

Key Takeaway
Zakat on young camels is obligatory at 25 by qiyas; below 25, the obligation varies according to three intra-Hanafi views.

Zakat — Almsgiving

Zakat Substitution When the Wajib Animal is Unavailable
Ruling on substitute animals with compensation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on substituting animals in zakat when the exact wajib is absent, and distinguish the collector's option in the higher-animal scenario from the lower-animal scenario.

Core Idea
When the exact zakat animal is absent, the collector may take a higher or lower animal with compensation—but who has the option depends on whether it is a 'purchase' or 'payment by value'.

This passage from al-Hidayah addresses a practical problem: the owner may not have the exact age or quality of animal required for zakat. The Hanafi school permits taking a substitute with monetary adjustment, based on the principle that value can fulfill zakat. However, the text draws an important distinction between two methods—taking a higher animal (considered a partial purchase) and taking a lower animal (considered payment by value)—which determines whether the collector can be compelled.

Guided Path
1
Identify the problem and the two solutions
The passage begins with the scenario: the wajib animal (musinn) is unavailable. Two options are given: take a higher-quality animal and return the excess value, or take a lower-quality animal and demand the difference in value. This is the basic ruling.
The key is that compensation must accompany the substitution.
2
Trace the basis of the ruling
The text states that this ruling is built on the permissibility of taking value (qeemah) in zakat in the Hanafi school. The proof is the hadith of Mu'adh: 'Iyyaka wa kara'ima amwalihim' (Beware of taking the choicest of their wealth), which implies taking average quality. The Hanafi school uses istihsan to allow value substitution.
The hadith is the primary dalil for the average standard, while permissibility of value is via istihsan.
3
Distinguish the two scenarios
The text clarifies a key difference: in the first scenario (taking higher and returning excess), the transaction involves a purchase element (shira'), so the collector has the option to refuse and demand the exact wajib or its cash value. In the second scenario (taking lower and taking excess), it is a pure payment by value (i'ta' bil qeemah), so the collector is compelled to accept.
This distinction is based on whether the collector is buying a share (cannot be forced) or simply receiving the zakat in a different form.
4
Identify the intra-Hanafi difference
The passage references Quduri's text, which implies the collector has the option in both scenarios. Sahib al-Hidayah clarifies that the second scenario is different because it involves no sale. The relied-upon view (mufta bihi) follows al-Hidayah: in the second scenario, the owner has the option, and the collector must comply.
The justification is that the option was legislated for the convenience of the obligated (owner), not the collector.
5
Contrast with the Shafi'i position
The passage notes that the Shafi'i school does not allow taking value in zakat at all; they require the exact animal in kind. This leads to a practical difference: in Hanafi jurisdictions, zakat can be paid in cash or substitute animals; in Shafi'i areas, only the specified type/age is accepted.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf based on different usul principles.

زکوۃ میں جو جانور دینا لازم ہوا اگر وہ مالک کے پاس نہ ہو تو کس طرح زکوۃ ادا کرے
قَالَ وَمَنْ وَجَبَ عَلَيْهِ مُسِنُّ فَلَمْ يُوْجَدْ أَخَذَ الْمُصَدِّقُ أَعْلَى مِنْهَا وَرَدَّ الْفَضْلَ أوْ اَخَذَ دُونَهَا وَأَخَذَ الْفَضْلَ وَهذَا يَبْتَنِى عَلَى أَنَّ أَخَذُ الْقِيْمَةٍ فِى بَابِ الزَّكوةِ جَائِزَ عِنْدَنَا عَلَى مَانَذَكُرُهُ إِن شَاءَ اللهُ إِلَّا أَنَّ فِي الْوَجهِ الْأَوَّلِ لَهُ أَنْ لا يَأخُذُو يُطَالِبُهُ بِعَيْنِ الْوَاجِبِ أَوْ بِقِيْمَتِهِ لِأَنَّهُ شِرَاءُ وَ فِى الْوَجْهِ الثَّانِي يُجْبَرُ لأَنَّهُ لَا بَيْعٌ فِيهِ بَلْ هُوَ اعطاء بِالْقِيْمَةِ
ترجمہ مصنف نے کہا ہے کہ اور جس شخص پر مسن ( ذات سن ) واجب ہوا تو مصدق اس سے اعلیٰ کو لے کر زیادتی کو پھیر دے۔ یا ادنی کو لے کر اور زیادتی کو لے ۔ اور یہ اس پر مبنی ہے کہ باب زکوۃ میں قیمت لینا ہمارے نزدیک جائز ہے۔ ہم اس کو ان شاء اللہ ذکر کریں گے۔ مگر پہلی صورت میں مصدق کو اختیار ہے کہ وہ اعلیٰ جانور کو نہ لے۔ اور مالک سے عین واجب کا مطالبہ کرے یا اس کی قیمت کا کیونکہ یہ تو خرید کرتا ہے اور دوسری صورت میں مصدق کو مجبور کیا جائے گا۔ کیوں کہ اس میں مبیع نہیں ہے بلکہ قیمت کے ذریعہ زکوۃ دینا ہے۔ تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ زکوۃ میں اوسط درجہ کا جانور واجب ہوتا ہے نہ بہت گھٹیا اور نہ بہت بڑھیا۔ چنانچہ اگر کسی پر بنت لبون واجب ہوا تو عامل اور مصدق ( زکوۃ وصول کرنے والا ) نہ تو اعلیٰ درجہ کا بنت لبون لے اور نہ ادنیٰ درجہ کا لے۔ بلکہ ان دونوں کے درمیان کا وصول کر لے ۔ کیونکہ رسول اکرم صلى الله عليه وسلم نے حضرت معاذ رضی اللہ عنہ کو جب یمن کا حکم بنا کر بھیجا تو فرمایا تھا۔ ايَّاكَ وَ كَرَائِمَ أَمْوَالِهِمْ یعنی زَكرة میں عمدہ مال لینے سے بچتے رہنا۔ (شرح نقایہ ) اور اس لئے کہ اوسط درجہ کا لینے میں رب المال اور فقراء دونوں کو رعایت ہے کیونکہ اعلیٰ درجہ کا لینے میں رب المال کا ضرر اور نقصان ہے۔ اور ادنیٰ لینے میں فقراء کا نقصان ہے۔
اب سوال یہ ہے کہ رب المال پر جو جانو ر واجب ہوا ہے۔ اگر وہ موجود نہ ہو تو کیا کرے۔ مثلاً بنت لبون واجب ہو اور بنت لبون اس کے پاس نہیں ہے۔ بلکہ حقہ موجود ہے۔ یا حقہ واجب ہو مگر وہ موجود نہیں بلکہ بنت لبون موجود ہے یا وصف کے اعتبار اوسط درجہ کا جانور موجود نہیں ہے بلکہ اعلیٰ درجہ کا موجود ہے یا ادنیٰ درجہ کا موجود ہے تو ان صورتوں میں کونسا جانور واجب ہوگا۔ صاحب قدوری نے فرمایا کہ عامل ( زکوۃ وصول کر نیوالا) اعلیٰ درجہ کا جانور لے کر زائد قیمت واپس کر دے مثلاً اوسط درجہ کے بنت لبون کی قیمت ایک ہزار روپے ہے ۔ اور اعلیٰ درجہ کا بنت لبون جورب المال کے پاس ہے اس کی قیمت پندرہ سو روپیہ ہے تو عامل اعلیٰ درجہ کا بنت لبون لے کر پانچ سورو پسید رب المال کو دیدے۔ یا مثلاً کسی پر بنت لبون واجب ہوا ہے۔ لیکن اس کے پاس بنت لبون تو موجود نہیں البتہ حقہ موجود ہے تو عامل کو چاہئے کہ وہ حقہ لے کر بنت لبون سے زائد قیمت کو واپس کر دے مثلاً بنت لبون کی قیمت ایک ہزار روپیہ ہے اور حقہ کی قیمت پندرہ سو روپیہ ہے تو عامل حقہ لے لے اور پانچ سو روپیہ رب المال کو دیدے۔ یا عامل ادنی درجہ کا جانور لے کر زیادتی کو لے لے مثلاً اوسط درجہ کا بنت لبون جورب المال پر واجب ہے اس کی قیمت ایک ہزار روپیہ ہے اور ادنی بنت لبون کی قیمت آٹھ سو روپیہ ہے تو عامل ادنی درجہ کا بنت لبون لے لئے اور دوسوزائد روپیہ لے لے۔ یا مثلا کسی پر حقہ واجب ہوا ہے لیکن اس کے پاس حقہ تو موجود نہیں البتہ بنت لبون موجود ہے اور بنت لبون کی قیمت ایک ہزار روپیہ ہے اور حقہ کی قیمت پندرہ سو روپیہ ہے تو عامل بنت لبون لے لے اور مزید پانچسو روپیہ لے لے۔ صاحب ہدایہ کہتے ہیں کہ متن کا یہ مسئلہ اس بناء پر ہے کہ ہمارے نزدیک باب زکوۃ میں قیمت لینا جائز ہے اگر چہ امام شافعی کے نزدیک جائز نہیں ہے ہم اس کو ان شاء اللہ آئندہ ذکر کریں گے۔
قدوری کی مذکورہ عبارت سے ظاہر ہوتا ہے کہ اس بارے میں مصدق اور عامل کو اختیار ہے کہ وہ اعلیٰ لے کر زیادتی کو واپس کر دے یا ادنی لے کر زیادتی کو لے لے۔ لیکن صحیح یہ ہے کہ اختیار اس کو ہے جس پر زکوۃ واجب ہے کیونکہ اختیار اس شخص کی سہولت کے لئے مشروع کیا گیا ہے۔ جس پر ز کوۃ واجب ہوئی ہے۔ اور سہولت اس کا اختیار دینے سے متحقق ہو گی۔ اس لئے اعلیٰ یا ادنی مذکورہ تفصیل کے ساتھ دینے کا اختیار اسی کو ہوگا جس پر زکوۃ واجب ہوئی ہے ۔ صاحب ہدایہ کی تقریر ان دونوں اقوال سے مختلف ہے کیونکہ موصوف مرحوم نے فرمایا ہے کہ پہلی صورت میں جبکہ اعلی جانور لے کر زیادتی واپس کرنی پڑتی ہے تو مصدق کو اختیار ہے کہ وہ اعلیٰ کو نہ لے۔ بلکہ مالک سے عین واجب یعنی اوسط درجہ کے جانور کا مطالبہ کرے۔ یا مالک اوسط درجہ کے جانور کی قیمت دیدے۔ اس کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ مصدق اگر اعلی جانور لے کر زیادتی واپس کرے گا تو گویا مصدق نے اس جانور کے ایک حصہ کو خرید لیا ہے اور خریدنے کے لئے کسی پر جبر نہیں ہو سکتا۔ اس لئے اس صورت میں مصدق کو اختیار ہوگا کہ وہ اعلیٰ جانور لے کر زیادتی واپس کر دے یا مالک سے اوسط درجہ کے جانور کا مطالبہ کرے۔ پس مالک اوسط درجہ کا جانور دے یا اس کی قیمت دیدے اور دوسری صورت میں ( جبکہ مصدق ادنی لے کر زیادتی لے گا ) مالک کو اختیار ہے کہ وہ ادنیٰ درجہ کا جانور دیدے اور زائد قیمت دیدے اور مصدق پر جبر کیا جائے گا کہ وہ ادنی درجہ کا جانور لے اور زائد قیمیتے ہیں۔ اس کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ مصدق کا ادنی کو لے کر زائد قیمت کو لینا یہ مصدق کی طرف سے کوئی بیچ نہیں ہے بلکہ مالک مال نے بذریعہ قیمت زکوۃ ادا کی ہے اور قیمت ادا کرنے کی
Zakat: When the animal that is obligatory to give is not possessed by the owner, how should zakat be discharged? He (the author) said: And whoever is obligated to give a musinn (adult camel) and it is not found, the collector takes a higher one and returns the excess, or takes a lower one and takes the excess. And this is based on the fact that taking value in the chapter of zakat is permissible in our school, as we will mention if Allah wills, except that in the first scenario he has the option not to take and to demand from him the exact wajib or its value, because it is a purchase; in the second scenario he is compelled, because there is no sale in it, rather it is giving by value. Translation: The author said: And the person upon whom a musinn (aged camel) is obligatory, if it is not present, the collector takes a higher one and returns the excess, or takes a lower one and takes the excess. And this is based on the fact that taking value in the chapter of zakat is permissible in our school; we will mention it if Allah wills. But in the first scenario, the collector has the option not to take the higher animal and to demand from the owner the exact wajib or its value, because this is a purchase; in the second scenario the collector will be compelled, because there is no sale in it, rather it is giving zakat by value. Explanation: The issue is that in zakat, an average animal is wajib, neither too poor nor too good. So if bint labun is wajib, the collector takes neither the best nor the worst, but the average. Because the Prophet (s) said to Mu'adh when sending him to Yemen: 'Beware of taking the choicest of their wealth' meaning in zakat. And because taking the average considers both the owner and the poor: taking the best harms the owner, taking the worst harms the poor. Now the question: If the exact animal wajib is not present, what to do? For example, bint labun is wajib but not present, only hikkah is present; or hikkah is wajib but not present, only bint labun is present; or the average quality is not present, but a better or worse quality is present. What animal should be taken? Sahib al-Quduri said: The collector takes the better animal and returns the excess value, or takes the worse animal and takes the excess. For example, average bint labun value 1000, better bint labun 1500, collect takes the better and returns 500. Or hikkah is wajib but absent, bint labun present, value of bint labun 1000, hikkah 1500, collector takes bint labun and takes 500 more. Sahib al-Hidayah says that the matn's ruling is based on the permissibility of taking value in zakat in our school, though Imam Shafi'i does not allow it; we will mention that later. From Quduri's text it seems the collector has the option, but the correct view is that the option belongs to the owner, because the option was legislated for the convenience of the one obligated. Sahib al-Hidayah's wording differs: in the first scenario (taking higher and returning difference), the collector has the option not to take and to demand the exact wajib or its value; in the second scenario (taking lower and taking difference), the collector is compelled to accept, and the owner may give the lower and pay the difference. The reason: in the first, the collector is effectively buying a part, so he cannot be forced; in the second, it is not a sale but payment by value.
Source pages p. 67

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof and intra-Hanafi clarification regarding zakat collection when the exact wajib animal is unavailable. The matn (from Quduri/Hidayah) states that the collector may take a higher animal and return the excess, or take a lower animal and take the excess. This is based on the Hanafi principle that taking value in zakat is permissible. The commentary explains that the average animal is wajib, citing the hadith of Mu'adh. Two scenarios are distinguished: (1) if the collector takes a higher animal, it is considered a purchase, so the collector cannot be compelled; he has the option to instead demand the exact wajib or its value. (2) If the collector takes a lower animal, it is not a sale but a payment by value, so the collector is compelled to accept. The owner has the option to give the lower and pay the difference. The commentary also notes that Quduri's formulation implies the collector has the option, but the correct (sahih) view according to Sahib al-Hidayah gives the option to the owner in the second scenario.

Key Terms
مصدق (musaddiq): The appointed zakat collector or official.
مسن (musinn): An adult camel, here used generically for any age-category of zakat animal.
قیمت (qeemah): Value or cash equivalent of the animal.
شراء (shira'): Purchase. In the text, when the collector takes a higher animal and returns the excess, that portion is considered a purchase.
إعطاء بالقيمة (i'ta' bil qeemah): Giving by value, i.e., paying the monetary equivalent of the wajib animal.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the Hanafi school, when the collector takes a higher-quality animal than the wajib, why does the collector have the option to refuse and demand the exact wajib or its value?
A) Because the hadith of Mu'adh forbids taking the best animal.
B) Because taking a higher animal is considered a purchase, and purchase cannot be forced.
C) Because the owner always has the right to give the exact wajib.
D) Because the collector prefers not to handle compensation.

Key Takeaway
When the wajib zakat animal is absent, the Hanafi school permits substitution with compensation, but the collector's compulsion depends on whether the transaction is a purchase (higher animal) or payment by value (lower animal).

Who Chooses When Zakat Animals Are Substituted?
Intra-Hanafi dispute on substitution choice in zakat.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the three Hanafi positions on who holds the choice when substituting zakat animals and identify the mufta bihi view.

Core Idea
The choice to substitute belongs either to the collector or the owner, depending on whether a higher or lower grade is taken.

When the exact zakat animal is unavailable, a substitute of higher or lower grade may be given. But who decides? This passage from Ashraf ul-Hidayah examines an intra-Hanafi dispute between Quduri, the 'correct view', and Sahib al-Hidayah. We will walk through each position and see how the final ruling balances the rights of both the collector and the owner.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal problem
The wajib animal (e.g., bint labun) is not present; the owner has a higher or lower grade. What happens? Three Hanafi opinions exist.
2
State al-Quduri's position
The collector (āmil) has the choice to take a higher grade and return surplus, or take lower and collect the deficit.
This treats the collector as the primary decision-maker.
3
State the 'correct view'
The choice belongs to the owner because the concession was legislated for his ease.
This is presented as the more widely held view before Hidayah.
4
Analyse Sahib al-Hidayah's differentiation
When taking higher, the collector effectively buys part of the animal, so he cannot be forced; thus collector has choice. When taking lower, the owner pays value, which is permissible, so owner has choice and collector must accept.
This is the most nuanced and relied-upon position.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The Hidayah position is the operative ruling for fatwa because it accounts for the nature of the transaction (sale vs. value payment).
This also aligns with the Hanafi permissibility of paying value (qīmah) in zakat.

گا کہ وہ ادنی درجہ کا جانور لے اور زائد قیمت لے۔ اس کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ مصدق کا ادنی کو لے کر زائد قیمت کو لینا یہ مصدق کی طرف سے کوئی بیع نہیں ہے بلکہ مالک نے بذریعہ قیمت زکوۃ ادا کی ہے اور قیمت ادا کرنے کی صورت میں مصدق کو اس کے لینے پر مجبور کیا جا سکتا ہے۔ عنایہ۔
Avoid taking the best property. (Sharh Niqaya) And because taking the middle-grade considers both the owner and the poor: taking the highest harms the owner, taking the lowest harms the poor. Now the question: what if the animal wajib upon the owner is not present? For example, bint labun is wajib but he does not have it; rather he has hiqqah. Or hiqqah is wajib but he does not have it; rather he has bint labun. Or the middle-grade animal is not present but a higher or lower grade is. What animal becomes wajib? Sahib Quduri said: the collector (amil) should take the higher grade and return the excess value. For example, the middle-grade bint labun costs 1000 rupees, the higher-grade bint labun with the owner costs 1500; the collector takes the higher and gives back 500 rupees. Or if bint labun is wajib but he has hiqqah, the collector takes hiqqah and returns the excess. Or the collector may take a lower grade animal and take the extra value. Sahib Hidayah says this ruling is based on our view that taking value in zakat is permissible, unlike Imam Shafi'i, and we will mention that later. From Quduri's statement it appears that the musaddiq/amil has the choice to take higher and return excess or take lower and take excess. But the correct view is that the choice belongs to the one upon whom zakat is wajib, because the choice was legislated for his convenience. So the choice to give higher or lower with the described details belongs to the zakat payer. The statement of Sahib Hidayah differs from both these views: He said in the first case (taking higher and returning excess) the musaddiq has the option not to take higher but to demand the exact wajib (middle-grade) from the owner, or the owner may give its value. The reason is that if the musaddiq takes higher and returns excess, he has purchased part of the animal, and no one can be forced to buy. So the musaddiq may either take higher and return excess or demand the middle-grade animal or its value. In the second case (when the musaddiq takes lower and takes extra), the owner has the option to give a lower-grade animal and pay the extra amount, and the musaddiq will be compelled to accept it. The reason is that taking lower and taking extra is not a sale by the musaddiq; rather the owner has paid zakat by value, and in the case of paying value, the musaddiq is compelled to accept it. (Inayah)
Source pages p. 68

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf ul-Hidayah addresses a practical issue in zakat collection: what happens when the exact type of animal required (the wajib) is not available? The text begins by recommending the middle-grade property for zakat to balance the interests of the owner and the poor. Then it poses the question of substitution. The early Hanafi authority, Imam al-Quduri, stated that the collector (amil or musaddiq) has the choice to take a higher-grade animal and return the surplus value, or take a lower-grade animal and collect the deficit. This implies that the collector is the active decision-maker. However, the correct position according to later Hanafis is that the choice belongs to the zakat payer (rabb al-mal), because the ruling was designed for his ease. Then the text presents a third view from Sahib al-Hidayah (Marghinani), which makes a distinction between two scenarios: (1) when the collector takes a higher-grade animal, he is effectively purchasing part of it, so he cannot be forced; thus the collector has the option to either take the higher and return surplus, or demand the exact wajib or its value. (2) When the collector takes a lower-grade animal, the owner is effectively paying the difference as value, and since paying value is permissible, the collector must accept it. This is a nuanced ruling that balances the rights of both parties. The passage is a typical Hanafi exposition that shows the evolution of the madhhab from Quduri to Marghinani.

Key Terms
مصدق (musaddiq): The official collector of zakat appointed by the state.
عامل (āmil): Synonym for musaddiq; the collector of zakat.
رب المال (rabb al-māl): The owner of the wealth upon whom zakat is obligatory.
قیمت (qīmat): Monetary value or price; used here as paying the value instead of the specific item.
اختیار (ikhtiyār): Choice or option; the right to decide between alternatives.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Sahib al-Hidayah, if a zakat payer has a higher-grade animal than what is wajib, who has the choice to decide whether to give it and receive the surplus?
A) The collector has the choice.
B) The owner has the choice.
C) The poor recipients have the choice.
D) Both have equal choice.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school resolves the substitution choice in zakat by distinguishing whether the substitute is higher (collector chooses) or lower (owner chooses), based on the nature of the transaction.

Inter-Madhhab Dispute: Fixed vs Market-Based Zakat Animal Compensation
Hanafi refutation of Shafi'i view that difference between animal ages is fixed at two sheep or twenty dirhams.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi and Shafi'i positions on the compensation for substituting zakat camel ages and evaluate the Hanafi response using the practice of Ali (RA).

Core Idea
Compensation for substituting zakat animals is not fixed but based on market value – a ruling shaped by circumstance, not a fixed legal quantity.

This passage addresses a classic inter-madhhab dispute: when a zakat collector must accept a different-aged camel, what compensation is owed? Both Hanafis and Shafi'is agree that compensation is required, but they differ on whether the amount is fixed by the Prophet's hadith or determined by current market prices. The Hanafi position, relying on the practice of Caliph Ali (RA), argues that the hadith reflects the market of that time, not a permanent legal prescription.

Guided Path
1
Identify the common ground and the dispute
Both schools agree that when the exact wajib animal is unavailable, another age can be substituted with compensation. The dispute is whether the compensation is fixed (Shafi'i) or variable (Hanafi).
2
Examine the Shafi'i proof
Imam al-Shafi'i cites a hadith where the Prophet specified two sheep or twenty dirhams as compensation. This seems to fix the amount definitively.
Hadith: 'Whosoever's camels necessitate bint labun... he gives back two sheep or twenty dirhams.'
3
Analyse the Hanafi response
Hanafis reinterpret the hadith as descriptive of the market rate at the Prophet's time, not a binding legal determination (taqdir shar'i). They argue that the Prophet's statement was situational.
The Hanafi school does not reject the hadith but contextualizes it.
4
Consider the proof from Ali (RA)
Caliph Ali, as a zakat collector, used one sheep or ten dirhams as compensation. Since he could not have opposed the Prophet or been ignorant of the hadith, his practice shows variability.
Ali's action demonstrates that the amount is not fixed but depends on market conditions.
5
Derive the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: Shafi'is always require two sheep or twenty dirhams; Hanafis require the actual market value difference, which fluctuates.
This impacts zakat calculation in different times and places.

Source Text

روپے کی قیمت کا ہے۔ اور حقہ پندرہ سو روپیہ کی قیمت کا۔ تو مصدق حقہ لے کر پانچ سوروپیہ رب المال کو دے گا۔ یا مصدق بنت مخاض لے کر زیادتی کو لے لے۔ مثلاً بنت لبون کی قیمت ایک ہزار روپے ہے اور بنت مخاض کی بکریاں یا بیس درہم لے۔ امام شافعی نے اس پر حدیث سے استدلال کیا ہے۔ حدیث یہ ہے اِنَّ رَسُولَ اللهِ صَلَّى الله عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّم قَالَ وَمَنْ وَجَبَ فِى ابله ابْنَةُ لَيُون فَلَمْ يَجِدِ الْمُصَدِّقُ إِلَّاحِقَةً اَخَذَهَا وَرَدَّ شَاتَيْنِ أَوْ عِشْرِينَ دِرْهَما مِمَّا يَتَيَسَّرُ عَلَيْهِ وَلَمْ يُوجَد إلا ابنة مخاضٍ اَخَذَهَا، وَاَخَذَ شَاتَين أو عِشْرِينَ دِرْهَما مِمَّا يَتَيَسَّر عَلَيْهِ یعنی رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا کہ جس کے اونٹوں میں بنت لبون واجب ہوا لیکن مصدق نے بنت لبون نہیں پایا مگر مالک کے پاس حقہ ہے تو مصدق حقہ لے لے۔ اور مالک کو دو بکریاں یا بیس درہم دیدے جو اس پر آسان ہو۔ اور اگر مالک کے پاس صرف بنت مخاض ہے تو مصدق بنت مخاض لے لے۔ اور دو بکریاں یا بیس درہم لے جو اس پر آسان ہو ۔ ( کفایہ عنایہ ) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ دو عمروں کے جانوروں کے درمیان تفاوت کی مقدار متعین ہے۔ اور وہ مقدار دو بکریاں یا بیس درہم ہیں ہماری طرف سے جواب یہ ہے کہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے یہ اس لئے فرمایا کہ آپ صلى الله عليه وسلم کے زمانہ میں دو عمروں کے جانوروں کے درمیان تفاوت کی یہی مقدار تھی یہ کوئی شرعی تقدیر اور تعین نہیں ہے اور دلیل یہ ہے کہ حضرت علی رضی اللہ تعالیٰ عنہ نے دو عمروں کے جانوروں کے درمیان ایک بکری یا دس درہم کے ساتھ تفاوت کو مقدر کیا ہے حالانکہ حضرت علی رضی اللہ تعالٰی عنہ رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم کے مصدق اور عامل تھے پس یہ بھی نہیں کہا جا سکتا کہ حضرت علی پر حدیث رسول مخفی ہوگی اور یہ بھی گمان نہیں کیا جا سکتا کہ حضرت علی رضی اللہ تعالٰی عنہ نے رسول اللہ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم کی مخالفت کی ہوگی پس جب یہ دونوں باتیں نہیں ہیں تو حضرت علی رضی اللہ عنہ کی روایت کو اس پر محمول کیا جائے گا۔ کہ حضرت علی رضی اللہ تعالی عنہ کے زمانہ میں تفاوت کی یہی مقدار تھی ۔ پس ثابت ہو گیا کہ دو عمروں کے جانوروں کے درمیان تفاوت کی کوئی مقدار متعین نہیں ہے۔ بلکہ وہ زمان و مکان کے لحاظ سے گھٹتی بڑھتی رہتی ہے۔ (کفایہ )
Benefits: According to our madhhab it is mentioned that if bint labun is wajib upon someone but he does not have bint labun; rather he has hiqqah and bint makhad, the musaddiq should take hiqqah and return the excess. For example, bint labun is worth 1000 rupees, hiqqah is worth 1500, so the musaddiq takes hiqqah and gives 500 to the owner. Or the musaddiq takes bint makhad and takes the excess (e.g., bint labun 1000, bint makhad 800, so takes bint makhad and 200). Note that in our view the difference in value between hiqqah, bint labun, and bint makhad is not fixed (muqaddar); rather it depends on market price which fluctuates. However, according to Imam Shafi'i, the difference between animals of two ages is fixed: it is two sheep or twenty dirhams. Imam Shafi'i argues from a hadith: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'Whosoever's camels necessitate bint labun and the musaddiq does not find it but finds hiqqah, he takes hiqqah and gives back two sheep or twenty dirhams, whichever is easier. And if only bint makhad is found, he takes it and takes two sheep or twenty dirhams.' This hadith shows the difference is fixed. Our response: The Prophet said that because in his time that was the difference; it is not a fixed legal determination. The proof is that Ali (may Allah be pleased with him) fixed the difference at one sheep or ten dirhams, yet he was the Prophet's musaddiq and amil. It cannot be said that Ali was unaware of the hadith or that he opposed the Prophet. Therefore, his practice is interpreted as being based on the market rate of his time. Hence, it is established that the difference is not fixed but varies with time and place. (Kifayah)
Source pages p. 69

Commentary
This passage continues the discussion of substituting zakat animals. It provides specific examples of the Hanafi methodology. The core issue is the inter-madhhab dispute with Imam al-Shafi'i. Both schools agree that when the exact wajib animal is unavailable, another age can be substituted with compensation. However, Shafi'i holds that the compensation amount is fixed by the Prophet's hadith at two sheep or twenty dirhams. The Hanafi response is nuanced: they do not reject the hadith but interpret it as time-specific. They argue that the difference in value between animal ages is not a fixed legal quantity but depends on market conditions. Their proof is the practice of Caliph Ali (RA), who as a zakat collector used one sheep or ten dirhams as compensation—a different amount. Since Ali would not have opposed the Prophet or been ignorant of the hadith, his action shows that the compensation amount is not fixed but was based on prevailing prices. Thus, the Hanafi school holds that the compensation is based on current market value, not a fixed number of sheep or dirhams. This reflects the Hanafi principle of considering changing circumstances ('urf and zaman) in legal rulings.

Key Terms
بنت لبون (bint labūn): A female camel in its second year (after one year).
حقہ (hiqqah): A female camel in its third year (after two years).
بنت مخاض (bint makhāḍ): A female camel in its first year (after birth).
تفاوت مقدر (tafāwut muqaddar): A fixed or predetermined difference in value or quantity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Hanafi school's position on the compensation amount when a different-aged zakat animal is substituted?
A) It is fixed at two sheep or twenty dirhams.
B) It is fixed at one sheep or ten dirhams.
C) It is not fixed; it varies according to market value.
D) Compensation is not required at all.

Key Takeaway
The compensation for substituting zakat animals is not fixed but determined by market values, as proven by the practice of Ali (RA) and the contextual interpretation of the Prophet's hadith.

Permissibility of Paying Value (Qimah) in Zakat
Ruling with proof: Hanafi permissibility of qimah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on paying value in zakat and explain the proof based on purpose (maqsad).

Core Idea
Paying cash in zakat fulfills the purpose of sustenance, so it is valid.

In this lesson, we examine a distinctive Hanafi ruling: that it is permissible to pay the monetary value (qimah) instead of the specific item in zakat and other obligations. The Shafi'i school restricts giving to the specified items, but the Hanafi school relies on the underlying objective of delivering sustenance to the poor. We will explore the proof from purpose (maqsad) and see how this ruling applies in practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its scope
Read the first part of the passage: paying value is permissible in zakat and also in expiations, sadaqat al-fitr, ushr, and nadhr.
Note the list of obligations where qimah is allowed.
2
Recognize the opposing view
The text mentions al-Shafi'i's position: he does not allow paying value, insisting on the specified item (manṣūṣ).
This is a clear inter-madhhab difference.
3
Extract the Hanafi proof
The Hanafi proof is given: 'The command to give to the poor is to deliver the promised sustenance.' Paying value achieves this objective.
This proof is based on maqasid (objectives) and istihsan.
4
Apply the reasoning
Understand that the ruling flows from the purpose, not the literal text alone. If the goal of zakat is to suffice the poor, then value (cash) often does that better.
This is a key difference in usul between Hanafi and Shafi'i.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قيمت سے زکوۃ ادا کرنے کا حکم
وَيَجُوزُ دَفْعُ الْقِيْمَةِ فِي الزَّكوة عِندَنَا وَ كَذَا فِى الْكَفَّارَاتِ وَصَدَقَةِ الْفِطْرِ وَالْعُشْرِ وَالنَّدْرِ وَقَالَ الشَّافِعى لا يَجُوزُ الْبَاعًا لِلْمَنْصُوصِ كَمَا فِي الْهَدَايَا وَ الصَّحَايَا وَلَنَا أَنَّ الْأمْرَ بِالْآدَاءِ إِلَى الْفَقِير إيصال لِلرِّزْقِ الْمَوْعُودِ
Ruling on paying value in zakat: It is permissible to pay the value (qimah) in zakat according to us, and similarly in expiations, sadaqat al-fitr, ushr, and nadhr. Al-Shafi'i said: It is not permissible [?] for the specified item, as in gifts and sacrifices. Our proof is that the command to give to the poor is to deliver the promised sustenance.
Source pages p. 69

Commentary
This is a foundational ruling in the Hanafi school: it is permissible to give the monetary value (qimah) of the required item in zakat, rather than the specific commodity. This extends to other obligations such as kaffarah (expiation for broken oaths, etc.), sadaqat al-fitr, ushr (agricultural tithe), and nadhr (vowed charities). The Shafi'i school opposes this, arguing that the texts specify particular items, and thus only those items may be given. The Hanafi proof is based on the objective of zakat: the command to provide for the poor is ultimately about delivering sustenance; paying value achieves this objective just as well, and sometimes better. The Arabic phrase 'إيصال للرزق الموعود' indicates that the purpose is to deliver the promised provision to the needy, and value fulfills that. This ruling is a clear example of Hanafi reliance on maqasid (objectives) and istihsan (juristic preference) over literal textual restriction.

Key Terms
قیمت (qīmat): Monetary value or price; paying the cash equivalent of the required item.
دفع القيمة (daf' al-qīmah): Paying the value instead of the commodity itself.
منصوص (manṣūṣ): The item explicitly specified in the primary texts (Quran or Sunnah) for a particular obligation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, in which of the following is paying value (qimah) permissible?
A) Zakat only
B) Zakat, kaffarah, sadaqat al-fitr, ushr, and nadhr
C) Only sadaqat al-fitr and zakat
D) None; it is not permissible in any obligation

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits paying the monetary value in zakat and other obligations based on the objective of delivering sustenance, using maqasid and istihsan over literal textual restriction.

Compensation with Different-Aged Animal in Zakat: Fixed or Flexible?
Hanafi-Shafi'i dispute on fixed vs flexible compensation for age difference

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school holds that compensation for age difference in zakat is based on market value and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument.

Core Idea
The Prophet's fixed compensation in hadith reflects his era's market, not a timeless Shariah rule.

When the exact age of animal for zakat is unavailable and a different-aged animal is taken, should the compensation be a fixed amount or vary with market prices? This dispute between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools turns on how we interpret a key hadith and the practice of Imam Ali. This lesson walks you through the arguments so you can understand the Hanafi reliance on market-based justice.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify exactly what the Hanafi school holds: the compensation is not fixed; it is the market price difference between the two animals at the time of collection.
The passage gives an example: if bint labun (one-year-old) is worth 1000 and haqqah (three-year-old) is 1500, the collector gives 500 to the owner.
2
Identify the Shafi'i position and its proof
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that the compensation is fixed at two sheep or twenty dirhams. He cites a hadith of the Prophet (peace be upon him) that explicitly mentions these numbers.
The hadith is quoted in the passage: 'Whoever owes bint labun... the collector takes haqqah and returns two sheep or twenty dirhams.'
3
Follow the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response argues that the Prophet's statement was descriptive of the market value of his time, not a prescriptive fixed amount. The proof is the practice of Imam Ali, who as a collector set the difference at one sheep or ten dirhams.
Imam Ali was a knowledgeable collector and would not contradict the Prophet; his different rate shows that the amount can change.
4
Analyze the Hanafi rebuttal
The Hanafis argue that if the hadith were a fixed Shariah ruling, Imam Ali would have adhered to it. Since he did not, the hadith is interpreted as contextual. Thus the amount is not fixed.
This rebuttal uses istihsan (juristic preference) and the principle that rulings may vary with time and place.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: Hanafis calculate compensation based on current market prices; Shafi'is always use two sheep or twenty dirhams.
This affects fairness: a fixed amount may overcompensate or undercompensate in different markets.

مصدق حقہ لے کر زیادتی کو واپس کرے۔ مثلاً بنت لبون ایک ہزار روپے کی قیمت کا ہے۔ اور حقہ پندرہ سو روپیہ کی قیمت کا۔ تو مصدق حقہ لے کر پانچ سوروپیہ رب المال کو دے گا۔ یا مصدق بنت مخاض لے کر زیادتی کو لے لے۔ مثلاً بنت لبون کی قیمت ایک ہزار روپے ہے اور بنت مخاض کی آٹھ سو روپیہ ہے تو مصدق ایک بنت مخاض لے لے۔ اور دوسو روپیہ لے لے۔ یہ خیال رہے کہ ہمارے نزدیک حقہ اور بنت لبون اور بنت مخاض کے درمیان قیمت کا جو تفاوت ہے وہ مقدر نہیں ہے۔ یعنی اس کی مالیت کی مقدار متعین نہیں ہے۔ بلکہ اس کا دارو مدار بازار کی قیمت پر ہے جو گھٹتی بڑھتی رہتی ہے۔ البتہ امام شافعی کے نزدیک دو عمر کے جانوں کے درمیان تفاوت کی مقدار متعین ہے۔ اور وہ مقدار تفاوت دو بکریاں یا نہیں درہم ہیں یعنی امام شافعی کے نزدیک اگر کسی پر بنت لبون واجب ہوا ۔ مگر اس کے پاس بنت لبون نہیں ہے بلکہ حقہ اور بنت مخاض ہے تو مصدق حقہ لے کر دو بکریاں یا نہیں درہم رب المال کو دیدے۔ اور یا بنت مخاض لے اور دو بکریاں یا نہیں درہم لے۔ امام شافعی نے اس پر حدیث سے استدلال کیا ہے۔ حدیث یہ ہے اِنَّ رَسُولَ اللهِ صَلَّى الله عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّم قَالَ وَمَنْ وَجَبَ فِى ابله ابْنَةُ لَيُون فَلَمْ يَجِدِ الْمُصَدِّقُ إِلَّاحِقَةً اَخَذَهَا وَرَدَّشَاتَيْنِ أَوْ عِشْرِينَ دِرْهَما مِمَّا ف يَتَيَسَّرُ عَلَيْهِ وَلَمْ يُوجَد إلا ابنة مخاضِ اَخَذَهَا، وَاَخَذَ شَاتَين أو عِشْرِينَ دِرْهَما مِمَّايَتَيَسَّر عَلَيْهِ یعنی رسول الله صلے اللہ علیہ وسلم نے فرمایا کہ جس کے اونٹوں میں بنت لبون واجب ہوا لیکن مصدق نے بنت لبون نہیں پایا مگر مالک کے پاس حقہ ہے تو مصدق حقہ لے لے۔ اور مالک کو دو بکریاں یا نہیں درہم دیدے جو اس پر آسان ہو۔ اور اگر مالک کے پاس صرف بنت مخاض ہے تو مصدق بنت مخاض لے لے۔ اور دو بکریاں یا نہیں درہم کے جو اس پر آسان ہو ۔ ( کفایہ عنایہ ) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ دو عمروں کے جانوروں کے درمیان تفاوت کی مقدار متعین ہے۔ اور وہ مقدار دو بکریاں یا بیس درہم ہیں ہماری طرف سے جواب یہ ہے کہ حضور صلے اللہ علیہ وسلم نے یہ اس لئے فرمایا کہ آپ صلى الله عليه وسلم کے زمانہ میں دو عمروں کے جانوروں کے درمیان تفاوت کی یہی مقدار تھی یہ کوئی شرعی تقدیر اور تعین نہیں ہے اور دلیل یہ ہے کہ حضرت علی رضی اللہ تعالیٰ عنہ نے دو عمروں کے جانوروں کے درمیان ایک بکری یا دس درہم کے ساتھ تفاوت کو مقدر کیا ہے حالانکہ حضرت علی رضی اللہ تعالٰی عنہ رسول اللہ صلے اللہ علیہ وسلم کے مصدق اور عامل تھے پس یہ بھی نہیں کہا جا سکتا کہ حضرت علی پر حدیث رسول مخفی ہوگی اور یہ بھی گمان نہیں کیا جا سکتا کہ حضرت علی رضی اللہ تعالٰی عنہ نے رسول اللہ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم کی مخالفت کی ہوگی پس جب یہ دونوں باتیں نہیں ہیں تو حضرت علی رضی اللہ عنہ کی روایت کو اس پر محمول کیا جائے گا۔ کہ حضرت علی رضی اللہ تعالی عنہ کے زمانہ میں تفاوت کی یہی مقدار تھی ۔ پس ثابت ہو گیا کہ دو عمروں کے جانوروں کے درمیان تفاوت کی کوئی مقدار متعین نہیں ہے۔ بلکہ وہ زمان و مکان کے لحاظ سے گھٹتی بڑھتی رہتی ہے۔ (کفایہ )
In this situation, the collector can be compelled to take it. Benefits: According to our madhhab, it is mentioned that if bint labun is obligatory but one does not have it, but has haqqah and bint makhad, the collector takes haqqah and returns the excess. For example, bint labun is worth 1000 rupees and haqqah is 1500 rupees, so the collector takes haqqah and gives 500 rupees to the owner. Or the collector takes bint makhad and takes the excess. For example, bint labun is worth 1000 rupees and bint makhad is 800 rupees, so the collector takes bint makhad and takes 200 rupees. Note that according to us, the difference in value between haqqah, bint labun, and bint makhad is not fixed. That is, its amount is not predetermined. Rather, it depends on the market price, which fluctuates. However, according to Imam Shafi'i, the difference between two ages of animals is fixed, and that fixed amount is two sheep or twenty dirhams. That is, according to Imam Shafi'i, if bint labun is obligatory on someone but he does not have it, but has haqqah and bint makhad, then the collector takes haqqah and gives two sheep or twenty dirhams to the owner, or takes bint makhad and takes two sheep or twenty dirhams. Imam Shafi'i adduced a hadith for this. The hadith is: 'Indeed the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, said: Whoever owes bint labun on his camels and the collector does not find except haqqah, he takes it and returns two sheep or twenty dirhams of what is easy for him, and if bint makhad is not found, he takes it and takes two sheep or twenty dirhams of what is easy for him.' That is, the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, said: For whom bint labun is obligatory on his camels, but the collector does not find bint labun but the owner has haqqah, then the collector takes haqqah and gives the owner two sheep or twenty dirhams, whichever is easy for him. And if the owner has only bint makhad, then the collector takes bint makhad and gives two sheep or twenty dirhams, whichever is easy for him. (Kifayah 'Inayah) From this hadith, it is learned that the difference between animals of two ages is fixed, and that amount is two sheep or twenty dirhams. Our response is that the Prophet, peace be upon him, said this because in his time the difference between animals of two ages was this amount. This is not a Shariah-set fixed amount. The proof is that Ali, may Allah be pleased with him, set the difference between animals of two ages as one sheep or ten dirhams, even though Ali, may Allah be pleased with him, was the collector and agent of the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him. So it cannot be said that Ali was unaware of the Prophet's hadith, nor can it be thought that Ali opposed the Messenger of Allah. Since both these possibilities are not there, Ali's narration is interpreted to mean that in his time the difference was that amount. Thus it is established that the difference between animals of two ages has no fixed amount; rather, it increases and decreases according to time and place. (Kifayah)
Source pages p. 69

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute (Hanafi vs Shafi'i) regarding the compensation when the exact wajib animal for zakat is unavailable and a different-aged animal is taken instead. The author begins by explaining the Hanafi position: if bint labun (a one-year-old camel) is obligatory but not available, and the owner has either haqqah (a three-year-old) or bint makhad (a two-year-old), the collector can take the available animal and either pay or receive the price difference based on the market value. The difference in value is not fixed; it depends on current market prices. In contrast, Imam Shafi'i holds that the compensation is fixed at two sheep or twenty dirhams, based on a hadith of the Prophet (peace be upon him). The Hanafi response uses the practice of Imam Ali (may Allah be pleased with him), who as a collector set the difference at one sheep or ten dirhams. Since Ali was fully aware of the Prophet's practice and would not contradict it, this shows that the amount was not a fixed Shariah rule but varied by time and place. Therefore, the Hanafi school follows the principle that compensation is determined by market value, not a fixed number.

Key Terms
مصدق (muṣaddiq): The official collector of zakat appointed by the state.
بنت لبون (bint labūn): A female camel in its second year (one year old).
حقہ (ḥaqqah): A female camel in its fourth year (three years old).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a person owes bint labun but only has haqqah, what should the zakat collector do?
A) Take the haqqah and give two sheep or twenty dirhams compensation.
B) Take the haqqah and pay/collect the market price difference.
C) Leave the zakat unpaid until bint labun is available.
D) Take the haqqah without any compensation.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school prioritizes market-based compensation in zakat over a fixed textual amount, based on the contextual interpretation of hadith and the practice of Imam Ali.

Permissibility of Paying Value (Qimah) in Zakat
Hanafi-Shafi'i dispute on paying cash value instead of specified animal

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi and Shafi'i positions on paying qimah in zakat and apply the Hanafi proof based on the rational objective of the obligation.

Core Idea
In zakat, the goal is to fulfill the need of the poor; paying cash value achieves that goal, making it permissible in the Hanafi school.

This passage presents a classic inter-madhhab dispute between the Hanafis and Shafi'is regarding whether one may pay the cash value (qimah) instead of the specified animal in zakat. The Hanafi school permits it based on the rational purpose of zakat, while the Shafi'i school insists on the specified animal, analogizing to hadaya (sacrificial animals). Understanding this dispute clarifies how each school approaches textual commands and underlying rationales.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
The Hanafi ruling is that paying the cash value (qimah) is permissible in zakat, kaffarat, sadaqat al-fitr, 'ushr, and nadhr. The specified animal is not an end in itself; the goal is to provide for the poor.
This applies even if the animal is available.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that it is not permissible to pay the value; one must give the specified animal (manṣūṣ) as mentioned in the texts.
The Shafi'i proof is based on textual adherence, comparing to hadaya where value is not allowed by consensus.
3
Analyze the opponent's proof
The Shafi'i school argues that the texts specify particular animals (bint makhad, goat, etc.), so departing from them by giving value is a violation, just as in hadaya.
The parallel with hadaya is central to the Shafi'i argument.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafi school responds that the purpose of zakat is rationally understood (ma'qul) – to remove the need of the poor. The specific animal is a means, not an end. Therefore, giving value achieves the same objective. This is unlike hadaya, where the act of bloodshed is a non-rational devotional act that cannot be replaced.
The distinction between rational and non-rational 'illa is key.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: Hanafis may pay zakat in cash, making it easier; Shafi'is must give the specified animal unless it is unavailable.
The mufta bihi for fatwa is the Hanafi position.
