Ruling on paying the value (qimah) in zakat: And it is permissible to give the value in zakat according to us, and similarly in kaffarat, sadaqat al-fitr, 'ushr, and nadhr. And al-Shafi'i said: It is not permissible to pay the value as a departure from the specified (manṣūṣ), like in hadaya (sacrificial animals) and dhabaih (slaughtered victims). And our proof is that the command to give to the poor is a delivery of the promised provision, so it nullifies the restriction of the sheep, so it becomes like jizyah, unlike hadaya because the act of worship in them is the shedding of blood, which is not rationally understood, and the aspect of worship in the disputed matter is removing the need of the needy, which is rationally understood. Translation: And according to us, giving the value in zakat is permissible. And similarly in kaffarat, sadaqat al-fitr, 'ushr, and nadhr (giving the value is permissible). Imam al-Shafi'i said that it is not permissible to follow the specified (manṣūṣ), as in hadaya and qurbani animals. And our proof is that the command to give to the poor (which the Shariah has given) is to deliver the promised provision, so it nullifies the restriction of the sheep, so it becomes like jizyah, unlike hadaya animals because in hadaya and qurbani animals, the shedding of blood is an act of worship, which is not rational, and in the disputed matter, the aspect of worship is removing the need of the needy, which is rational. Explanation: Previously, the details of zakat on animals were mentioned, that in some cases a goat is obligatory, in some bint makhad, and in some tarbi'ah. Now the question is: if the owner wants to give the value instead of the animal that is obligatory in zakat, is it permissible? Responding to this, Sahib al-Quduri said that according to us, giving the value in zakat is permissible. Similarly, in financial kaffarat, giving the value is permissible. For example, in kaffarat al-yamin (oath expiation), if someone gives cash instead of feeding ten poor or clothing them, it is permissible. Similarly, in sadaqat al-fitr, instead of wheat or barley, giving their value is permissible. And similarly, in 'ushr and nadhr, giving the value is permissible. That is, if a tenth of the land's produce is obligatory, and he sells it and gives the tenth as value, it is permissible. Similarly, if someone vowed to give a gold coin in charity and then gave an equivalent amount of dirhams in charity, it is permissible. Keep in mind that the value is considered according to the day of payment and the city where the wealth is, and if in a forest, then give the value of such animals in the nearest populated area. Imam al-Shafi'i said that in zakat etc., it is not permissible to pay the value of the animal that is wajib; rather, one must give the same animal mentioned in the hadith. Imam al-Shafi'i's proof is that this is following the manṣūṣ, i.e., the specified are bint makhad, goat, tarbi'ah, etc., so following them is wajib, and giving value is not permissible, just as in hadaya and qurbani, by consensus, giving value is not permissible. So similarly, in zakat, giving value will not be permissible. Our proof is that Allah's command to give zakat to the poor is to fulfill the promise that Allah has made to provide sustenance to all creatures, as in the verse: 'And there is no creature on earth but that upon Allah is its provision' (Hud 11:6). The conclusion is that Allah has promised to provide sustenance to all creation. So He provides sustenance to some by creating means of livelihood (trade, agriculture, craft, employment), and for others (the poor and needy) He did not create means, so He ordered the wealthy to give one-fortieth of their wealth to these poor. As the hadith says: 'Take from their wealthy and return to their poor.'
Source pages p. 70

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute (Hanafi vs Shafi'i) on whether paying the cash value (qimah) instead of the specified animal in zakat is permissible. The author first states the Hanafi ruling that paying the value is permissible not only in zakat but also in kaffarat, sadaqat al-fitr, 'ushr, and nadhr. The Shafi'i position is that it is not permissible because one must follow the specified animal (manṣūṣ) as in hadaya and qurbani. The Hanafi proof is that the purpose of zakat is to provide for the poor, which is a rational objective ('illa ma'qula). Therefore, the specific animal is not the goal; the goal is fulfilling the need. Hence, paying the value achieves the same purpose. This is unlike hadaya, where the act of shedding blood is a ritual worship that cannot be replaced by value. The passage then elaborates with examples from the Hanafi school, including kaffarat al-yamin, sadaqat al-fitr, 'ushr, and nadhr. It also notes that the value is determined by the market of the day and place. The Shafi'i proof is that since the texts specify certain animals, one must adhere to them, similar to the consensus on hadaya. The Hanafi response emphasizes that the underlying reason for zakat is the need of the poor, which is rationally understood, so value can substitute. The passage concludes by citing the Quranic verse and hadith about Allah's guarantee of provision.

Key Terms
قیمت (qīmah): The cash value or price equivalent of the obligatory item.
منصوص (manṣūṣ): The specified item mentioned in the text (e.g., bint makhad, goat).
ہدی (hadaya): Sacrificial animals brought to the Haram (for Hajj/Qurbani).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Zakat — Almsgiving

Paying Value in Zakat: Hanafi Permissibility and Shafi'i Objection
Hanafi ruling on paying value in zakat with proof and response to Shafi'i

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on paying monetary value instead of the specified animal in zakat and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument using the distinction between ta'abbudi and ma'qul purposes.

Core Idea
In zakat, the purpose is rationally understood—relieving need—so value can substitute for the specified animal.

This lesson examines a classic inter-madhhab dispute: may a person pay the monetary value of the required animal (e.g., a goat) in zakat, or must the animal itself be given? The Hanafi school holds that paying value is permissible and fulfills the obligation, while the Shafi'i school insists on the specific animal. The key lies in understanding the nature of the worship—whether its purpose is rationally understood (ma'qul) or purely devotional (ta'abbudi).

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Start by clearly stating the Hanafi ruling: paying value in zakat is permissible (ja'iz) and discharges the obligation. The obligation is to deliver sustenance to the poor, which value accomplishes.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
The opposing school is the Shafi'i madhhab, which holds that paying value is not permissible; the specific animal must be given. Their evidence is based on following the specified animals (mansus) as in hadaya and udhiyah.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
The Shafi'is analogize zakat to hadaya (sacrificial animals), where the act of worship is the shedding of blood (a non-rational act). They argue that just as value cannot replace the animal in hadaya, it cannot in zakat.
This is a qiyas argument: zakat is like hadaya in being a financial worship.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafis distinguish the two: the purpose in zakat is rationally understood—filling the need of the poor—while the purpose in hadaya is the bloodshed itself, which is not rationally understood. Therefore, the analogy fails. Additionally, they cite the verse from Surah Hud (11:6) about sustenance and analogize to jizyah where value is accepted.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence is clear: Hanafis allow paying value for zakat, kaffarah, sadaqat al-fitr, ushr, and nadhr; Shafi'is require the specific animal. This difference affects how Muslims fulfill these obligations in practice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَلَنَا أَنَّ الْوَاجِبَ إِيصَالُ الرِّزْقِ إِلَى الْفَقِيرِ وَالْقِيمَةُ تُوصِلُهُ إِلَيْهِ فَيَكُونُ إِبْطَالًا لِقَيْدِ الشَّاةِ فَصَارَ كَالْجِزْيَةِ بِخِلَافِ الْهَدَايَا لِأَنَّ الْقُرْبَةَ فِيهَا إِرَاقَةُ الدَّمِ وَهُوَ لَا يُعْقَلُ وَوَجْهُ الْقُرْبَةِ فِي الْمُتَنَازَعِ فِيهِ سَدُّ خَلَّةِ الْمُحْتَاجِ وَهُوَ مَعْقُولٌ
Our evidence: The obligation is to deliver sustenance to the poor, and the value delivers it to him, so it becomes an annulment of the restriction of the goat, thus it is like jizyah, unlike hadaya, because the act of worship in them is the shedding of blood, which is not rationally understood, while the aspect of worship in the disputed matter is filling the need of the needy, which is rationally understood.
Source pages p. 70

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute between Hanafis and Shafi'is regarding the permissibility of paying the monetary value instead of the specific animal (e.g., goat, camel) in zakat and similar obligatory payments. The Hanafi position is that paying value is permissible. The author presents the Hanafi proof: the underlying purpose of zakat is to deliver sustenance to the poor; value accomplishes this just as well, thus the restriction to a specific animal is meaningless. This is analogized to jizyah, where value is accepted. The Hanafi response to the Shafi'i analogy to hadaya (sacrificial animals) is that the worship in hadaya is the bloodshed itself, which is non-rational (ta'abbudi), whereas in zakat the worship is rationally understood as fulfilling need. Therefore, value can substitute for the animal in zakat but not in hadaya.

Key Terms
قيمة (qīmah): Monetary value of the specified animal or item at the time and place of payment.
الهدايا (al-hadāyā): Sacrificial animals offered in the Haram (Hadi) and sacrificial animals for 'Eid (Udhiyah).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Not permissible under any circumstances.
B) Permissible and fulfills the obligation.
C) Permissible only for zakat, not for kaffarah.
D) Permissible only if the poor agrees.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, paying value in zakat is permissible because the purpose is rationally understood as relieving need, unlike non-rational acts like hadaya.

Zakat Exemption for Work, Pack, and Fed Animals
Hanafi ruling with inter-madhhab dispute and proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi rationale for exempting work, pack, and fed animals from zakat and contrast it with the Maliki position.

Core Idea
Zakat is on growing wealth; work and fed animals do not grow.

This passage addresses a classic inter-madhhab dispute: which animals are subject to zakat? The Hanafi school exempts certain categories based on a specific hadith and the principle that zakat applies only to growing (nami) wealth. We will examine the proof, the opposing view of Imam Malik, and the practical consequence of this difference.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Hanafi ruling
State clearly which animals are exempt from zakat according to the Hanafi school: work animals ('awāmil), pack animals (ḥawāmil), and animals fed at home ('alūfah).
These are categories where the animal is used for service or incurring expenses, not for growth.
2
Analyze the Hanafi proof
Look at the specific hadith cited: 'There is no zakat on pack animals, work animals, nor on the plowing ox.' Also note the rational argument: zakat's legal cause (illah) is growth (nama'), which is absent here.
The hadith is narrated by Ibn Majah and others; its chain is acceptable for Hanafi usul.
3
Consider the Maliki objection
Imam Malik relies on general texts (zawahir an-nusus) like 'Take from their wealth sadaqah' (Quran 9:103) and the hadith 'In every forty goats a goat is due.' According to him, all grazing cattle are zakatable unless excluded.
Malik's position is that the general command includes all cattle; no exception is made without clear proof.
4
Evaluate the Hanafi response
The Hanafi school responds that the specific hadith specifies (takhsis) the general texts. Moreover, the rational illah of growth is missing in these categories: work animals are used for labor, pack animals for transport, and fed animals incur expenses that consume any potential growth.
Thus, the general texts are not absolutely general; they are qualified by the specific evidence.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: a Hanafi mufti will not levy zakat on a farmer's plowing oxen or a tradesman's pack camels, whereas a Maliki mufti would require zakat on such animals if they are grazing (sa'imah) for most of the year.
The dispute is legitimate (mukhtalaf fih), and each school has its evidence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَلَيْسَ فِي الْعَوَامِل وَالْحَوَامِلَ وَالْعَلُوْفَةِ صَدَقَةٌ خِلافًا لِمَالِك لَهُ ظَوَاهِرُ التَّصْوص وَلَنَا قَوْلُهُ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ لَيْسَ فِي الْحَوَامِلِ وَالْعَوَامِلِ وَلَا فِى الْبَقَرَةِ الْمُثِيرَةِ صَدَقَةٌ وَلَأنَّ السَّبَبَ هُوَ الْمَالُ النَّامِيُّ وَ دَلِيلُ الإِسامَةُ وَالإعْدَادُ لِلتِّجَارَةِ وَلَمْ يَوْجَدَ وَلانَّ فِي الْعُلُوْفَةِ تَتَرَاكُمُ الْمُؤنَةِ فَيَنْعَدِمُ اليَمَاءُ مَعْنَى ثُمَّ السَّائِمَةُ هِيَ الَّتِي تَكْتَفِي بِالرَّعْي فِي اَكْثَر الْحَوْل حَتَّى لَوْ اعْلَفَهَا نِصْفَ الْحَوْلِ اوْ اَكْثَرَ كَانَتْ عَلُوفَةً لأن القَلِيل تابع للاكثر
And there is no zakat on work animals, pack animals, and animals fed at home, contrary to Malik; he has apparent texts. Our evidence is his statement (peace be upon him): 'There is no zakat on pack animals, work animals, nor on the plowing ox.' And because the cause is growing wealth, and evidence of growth is grazing or preparation for trade, and that is not found; and because in animals fed at home the expenses accumulate, so the meaning of growth is absent. Then, the sa'imah (grazing animal) is that which suffices with grazing most of the year, such that if one feeds it half the year or more, it is 'alufah (fed at home), because the little follows the majority.
Source pages p. 71

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute between Hanafis and Malikis regarding zakat on certain types of cattle. The Hanafi ruling, agreed upon by the Shafi'is, is that no zakat is due on 'awamil (work animals used for labor), hawamil (pack animals used for carrying loads), and 'alufah (animals that are fed at home for most or half the year). The author presents the Hanafi proof: a specific hadith of the Prophet (peace be upon him) exempts such animals. Additionally, the rationale (ta'lil) is that zakat is only on growing (nami) wealth; growth in livestock is evidenced by free grazing (sa'imah) or being prepared for trade. Work and pack animals are used for service, not growth, and fed animals incur constant feeding costs, negating growth. The text then defines sa'imah as animals that rely on grazing for most of the year; if fed for half or more, they become 'alufah and are exempt. Imam Malik's position is based on general texts like 'Take from their wealth...' which he considers inclusive of all animals.

Key Terms
العوامل (al-'awāmil): Animals used for work, such as plowing oxen or transport.
الحوامل (al-ḥawāmil): Animals used for carrying loads (pack animals).
العلوفة (al-'ulūfah): Animals that are fed at home (not grazing freely) for half the year or more.
السائمة (al-sā'imah): Animals that graze freely for most of the year, the type subject to zakat.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) General qiyas on horses
B) A specific hadith negating zakat on certain animals
C) Consensus of the Companions
D) The principle of istihsan

Key Takeaway
Work, pack, and fed animals are exempt from zakat in the Hanafi school because they lack the essential condition of growth (nama').

Paying Zakat Value: Ruling and Refutation of Shafi'i Qiyas
Ruling with proof and refutation of opposing qiyas

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on paying zakat value, cite the Quranic proof, and explain why analogizing zakat to Hadi/Udhiya is invalid.

Core Idea
Paying cash value fulfills zakat because its purpose is meeting needs, not specific livestock.

This lesson unpacks the Hanafi position that giving the cash equivalent of livestock in zakat is valid. We begin with the Quranic basis—zakat is for the poor's needs—and then examine why the Shafi'i analogy to sacrificial animals (Hadi/Udhiya) fails. Understanding this illustrates how the Hanafi school prioritizes the maqsad (purpose) of the law over literal form.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Hanafi ruling
Read the passage to find the explicit ruling: paying the value (qimat) instead of the animal itself is permissible (ja'iz). Note that the three Hanafi imams agree.
The ruling applies to all zakat livestock.
2
Extract the Quranic proof
Locate the Quranic verses cited: 'The alms are only for the poor…' (At-Tawbah 9:60) and 'And give the zakat…' (Al-Hajj 22:41). The author argues these show the goal is delivering sustenance to the poor, which is not limited to animals.
The dalala (indication) is zanni: the verses imply flexibility.
3
Understand the maqsad of zakat
The passage states that zakat aims to meet the needs of the poor (fugarah). Needs vary and can be met with cash, so restricting to animals is bāṭil (invalid).
This is a teleological (maqsad-based) argument.
4
Analyze the Shafi'i qiyas and its refutation
Imam al-Shafi'i analogizes zakat to Hadi/Udhiya, requiring the animal itself. The Hanafi response: the 'illa in Hadi/Udhiya is the act of slaughter (non-rational worship), whereas zakat's 'illa is removing need (rational). Therefore, qiyas is invalid.
The passage calls slaughter 'non-rational' (ghayr ma'qul) and need-removal 'rational' (ma'qul).
5
Apply the ruling to modern practice
Conclude that giving the market value of livestock is permitted and widely practiced in the Hanafi school. This aligns with the maqsad of zakat in cash economies.
This fatwa position (mufta bihi) is the dominant view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الزكوة إِنَّمَا الصَّدَقتُ لِلْفُقَرَاءِ وَالْمَسَكِين .... آلاية (التوب (۲۰) اور باری تعالیٰ کا قول "وآتوا الزكوة (الج ۴۱) ہے پس ثابت ہو گیا کہ زکوۃ کا مقصد فقراء تک ان کا رزق موعود ( وعدہ کیا گیا ) پہنچانا ہے اور رزق بکری گائے اونٹ وغیرہ جانوروں کے اندر منحصر نہیں ہے بلکہ انسان کی بہت سی حاجتیں اور ضرورتیں ہیں جن کو ان جانوروں سے پورا نہیں کیا جاسکتا اس لئے بکری کی قید لگانا باطل ہے یعنی خاص طور پر بکری وغیرہ دینے کی قید نہیں ہے۔ بلکہ اگر اس کی قیمت دیدی گئی تو بھی جائز ہے جیسے جزیہ میں قیمت کا ادا کرنا جائز ہے۔ بخلاف الھدایا سے امام شافعی کے قیاس کا جواب ہے۔ جواب کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ زکوۃ کو ہدی اور قربانی کے جانور پر قیاس کرنا درست نہیں ہے کیونکہ ہدی اور قربانی کے جانور کو قربان کرنا اور ذبح کرنا قربت اور عبادت ہے حتی کہ ذبح کرنے کے بعد اور اس کو صدقہ کرنے سے پہلے اگر جانور ضائع ہو گیا تو اس پر کچھ لازم نہیں ہے اس لئے کہ ذبح کرنے سے عبادت ادا ہوگئی ہے اور یہ ذبح کرنا یعنی خون بہانا غیر معقول اور خلاف قیاس ہے اس کے غیر معقول ہونے کو ایک اردو شاعر نے بھی بیان کیا ہے۔
یہ عجیب ماجرا ہے کہ بروز عید قربان وہی قتل بھی کرے وہی لے ثواب الٹا۔ اور زکوۃ جس میں گفتگو ہے اس میں قربت اور عبادت محتاج کی احتیاج کو دور کرنا ہے اور یہ بات معقول اور عین قیاس کے مطابق ہے کہ محتاج کی احتیاج کو دور کرنا عبادت ہے پس امر معقول کو امر غیر معقول پر قیاس کرنا کس طرح درست ہو گا۔
The Book of Zakat: 'The alms are only for the poor and the needy...' verse (at-Tawbah 60) and Allah's saying 'And give the zakat' (al-Hajj 41). So it is established that the purpose of zakat is to deliver to the poor their promised sustenance, and sustenance is not confined to goats, cows, camels, etc. Rather, humans have many needs that cannot be fulfilled by these animals. Therefore, restricting to a goat is invalid—meaning there is no condition specifically to give a goat, etc. Rather, if its value is given, it is also permissible, just as giving value in jizyah is permissible. Contrary to the Hadiya (sacrificial animal), this is the answer to Imam Shafi'i's analogy. The gist of the answer is that analogizing zakat to the animal of Hadi and Udhiya is incorrect because sacrificing and slaughtering the Hadi and Udhiya animal is an act of worship and nearness—to the extent that if the animal is lost after slaughter but before being given in charity, nothing is due, because the worship is fulfilled by slaughter, and this slaughter (shedding blood) is irrational and contrary to analogy. An Urdu poet has also expressed its irrationality: 'What a strange affair that on the day of Eid sacrifice, he both kills and takes reward in reverse.' Whereas zakat, which is under discussion, its act of worship and nearness is to remove the need of the needy, and this is rational and perfectly analogical—that removing the need of the needy is worship. So how can it be correct to analogize a rational matter to an irrational one?
Source pages p. 71

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling with proof regarding the permissibility of giving the cash value of the animal in zakat instead of the animal itself. The author establishes the ruling from the Quranic verses that zakat is for fulfilling the needs of the poor, which are not limited to livestock. Then it refutes Imam al-Shafi'i's analogy (qiyas) with the Hadi and Udhiya animals, showing that the 'illa (effective cause) in those is the act of slaughter (which is non-rational worship), whereas in zakat it is removing need (which is rational and serves the maqsad). Therefore, giving value is valid. The author also supports the ruling with the analogy of jizya, where paying value is accepted.

Key Terms
زکوۃ (zakāt): Obligatory alms, one of the pillars of Islam, due on specific wealth.
قیاس (qiyās): Analogical reasoning used to derive rulings for new cases from existing ones.
قیمت (qīmat): Monetary value or cash equivalent of an item.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

C) Because the Quran explicitly commands giving cash.
D) Because the Sahibayn disagreed with Abu Hanifa on this point.

Key Takeaway
Paying the cash value of zakat livestock is permissible because the maqsad of zakat is meeting the needs of the poor, which cash can fulfill, and the analogy to sacrificial animals fails due to a difference in the effective cause.

Zakat Exemption for Work, Pack, and Stall-Fed Animals
Presenting the Hanafi ruling and proofs against Imam Malik

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on zakat for 'awamil, hawamil, and 'alufa, and explain the three proofs supporting the exemption.

Core Idea
Zakat is only due on growing wealth; work, pack, and stall-fed animals lack the condition of growth.

In this lesson, we examine the Hanafi position that no zakat is due on animals used for work, transport, or stall-feeding. This ruling is based on specific hadiths and the legal cause (sabab) of zakat. We will explore the three proofs and the definition of sa'imah and 'alufa, which determines zakatability.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi ruling
Identify the three categories of animals: 'awamil (work animals), hawamil (pack animals), and 'alufa (stall-fed animals). According to the Hanafi school, no zakat is due on any of these.
This is contrary to Imam Malik who holds zakat is obligatory on all livestock.
2
Examine the first proof: specific hadith
The Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'There is no zakat on pack animals, work animals, nor on the ox that plows.' This hadith explicitly exempts these categories.
This hadith is a khabar wahid but its meaning is clear (qati' al-dalalah).
3
Examine the second proof: absence of the cause (sabab)
Zakat is only due on wealth that grows (mal nam). Growth in livestock is evidenced by free grazing (sa'imah) or preparation for trade. Work and pack animals are not free-grazing nor trade goods, so growth is absent.
The Hanafi school emphasizes the illah of growth for zakat on livestock.
4
Examine the third proof: continuous expenses negate growth
Stall-fed animals ('alufa) require continuous feeding expenses, which eliminates the meaning of growth. Therefore, zakat is not due.
This is a rational proof (ma'qul) based on the purpose of zakat.
5
Define sa'imah and 'alufa
Sa'imah is an animal that grazes freely for most of the year. If it is fed for half the year or more, it becomes 'alufa. The lesser part follows the greater; thus, feeding for most of the year makes it 'alufa.
This definition is crucial for determining zakat liability.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

سے کوئی بات نہیں پائی گئی ہے۔ اس لئے زکوۃ واجب ہونے کا سب منفی ہو گیا اور جب سبب منفی ہو گیا تو ز کو بھی منعی ہو جائے گی ۔ تیسری دلیل یہ ہے کہ علوفہ ( جن جانوروں کو باندھ کر کھلایا جاتا ہے) میں پیہم خرچہ کا بار پڑتا ہے یعنی ان کو چارہ دینا پڑتا ہے تو معنی علوفہ کے اندر نمو معدوم ہو گیا اور نمو جب معدوم ہو گیا تو زکوۃ واجب ہونے کا سبب نہ پایا گیا اور جب سبب ز کو نہیں پایا گیا تو زکوۃ بھی واجب نہ ہوگی۔ سوال: اس جگہ ایک سوال ہے وہ یہ کہ امام مالک نے اپنی دلیل میں اطلاق کتاب "خُذْ مِنْ اَمْوَالِهِمْ " کو پیش فرمایا ہے لیکن آپ نے خبر واحد لَيْسَ فِي الْحَوَامِل صَدَقَةٌ .. الحدیث سے اس کے اطلاق نہیں ہے۔ چنانچہ آپ دیکھئے کہ یہ آیت حولان حول کی قید سے بھی مطلق ہے حالانکہ زکوة حولان حول کے بعد ہی واجب ہوتی ہے پس معلوم ہوا کہ یہ آیت وجوب اخذ کو بیان کرنے کے لئے ہے۔ یعنی آیت میں فقط " زکوۃ" وصول کرنے کے وجوب کو بیان کیا گیا ہے اس کے علاوہ تمام چیزوں میں مجمل ہے۔ اور مجمل کی تفسیر حدیث سے کی جاتی ہے پس حدیث لَيْسَ فِي الْحَوَامِلِ... الحديث آيت خُذْ مِنُ اَمْوَالِهِمْ صَدَقَةً (التوبہ (۱۰۳) مؤخر مانا ہے اور مطلق کو مقدم اور مؤخر مقدم کے لئے ناسخ ہوتا ہے بس احادیث مطلقه حديث مقيده لَيْسَ فِي الْحَوَامِل الحدیث کی وجہ سے منسوخ ہو گئیں ہیں۔
سائمہ و علوفہ کی تعریف صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ سائمہ وہ جانور ہوتا ہے جو سال کے اکثر حصہ میں چرنے پر اکتفاء کرے۔ چنانچہ اگر آدھے سال یا کثر باندھ کر کھلایا تو وہ علوفہ کہلائے گا۔ اکثر سال کی صورت میں تو علوفہ اس لئے ہو گا کہ قلیل کثیر کے تابع ہوتا ہے پس جب سال کے اکثر
And there is no zakat on work animals, pack animals, and stall-fed animals, contrary to Malik who has apparent texts (as proof). And our proof is his (peace be upon him) saying: 'There is no zakat on pack animals, work animals, nor on the ox that plows.' And because the cause (sabab) is wealth that grows, and the evidence of growth is free grazing or preparation for trade, and that is not found. And because in stall-fed animals, expenses accumulate, so the meaning of growth is absent. Then the sa'imah (free-grazing animal) is that which is content with grazing for most of the year, so much so that if one feeds it for half the year or more, it becomes 'alufa (stall-fed), because the small (part) follows the large (part).
Translation: There is no zakat on 'awamil, hawamil, and 'alufa. Imam Malik disagrees; his proof is from apparent texts. Our proof is the saying of the Prophet (peace be upon him): 'There is no zakat on pack animals, work animals, and the ox that plows.' And the cause for zakat is wealth that grows, and the evidence of growth is free grazing or preparation for trade, and neither is found. And for 'alufa, continuous expense is incurred, so the meaning of growth is absent. Then the sa'imah is the animal that is content with grazing for most of the year; if one feeds it for half the year or more, it is 'alufa, because the small follows the large. Explanation: 'Awamil is plural of 'amila, animals used for work. Hawamil is plural of hamila, animals used for carrying loads. 'Alufa are animals that are fed (stall-fed) for the whole year or more than half, or according to the author of al-Hidayah, if fed for half the year. According to us and the Shafi'is, there is no zakat on these animals, but according to Imam Malik, there is. Imam Malik's proof is from apparent texts: Allah says, 'Take from their wealth sadaqah' (at-Tawbah 103) – the word 'amwal' includes all wealth. And the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'For every five camels, one sheep; for every thirty cattle, a tabi' or tabi'ah; and for every forty sheep, one sheep.' And in another hadith: 'Take from camels, camels.' All these texts are absolute (mutlaq), and their absoluteness requires that zakat is obligatory on all types of camels, cattle, and sheep, whether they are 'awamil or not, hawamil or not, 'alufa or sa'imah. Our proof is that Ali (may Allah be pleased with him) said that the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'There is no sadaqah on camels that carry loads,' and the hadith of Ibn Abbas from the Prophet (peace be upon him): 'There is no sadaqah on the plowing ox.' The author of al-Hidayah combined all three in one hadith. In any case, these hadiths prove that zakat is not obligatory on 'awamil and hawamil. The second proof is that the cause of zakat being obligatory is that the wealth is growing, and these properties are not growing, because the evidence of growth is that the animal grazes in the open pasture or is prepared for trade, and in 'awamil, hawamil, and 'alufa, neither is found. Therefore, the cause for zakat is negated, and when the cause is negated, zakat is also negated. The third proof is that in 'alufa (animals that are kept and fed), there is continuous expense (they need to be fed), so the meaning of growth is absent, and when growth is absent, the cause for zakat is not found, so zakat is not obligatory. Question: Here a question arises: Imam Malik presented the absolute (mutlaq) of the Book, 'Take from their wealth,' but you have nullified its absoluteness with a khabar wahid (single-narrator hadith) 'There is no zakat on pack animals...', whereas according to your principles, it is not permissible to nullify or abrogate the absolute of the Book with a khabar wahid. Also, you have carried the absolute upon the qualified (muqayyad), in that the hadith presented by Imam Malik, 'For every five camels...' is absolute, with no qualification of 'awamil or others, which obligates zakat absolutely on camels, cattle, etc., but you have carried it upon the hadith 'There is no sadaqah on pack animals and work animals,' whereas according to you, it is not permissible to carry the absolute upon the qualified. Answer: The absoluteness of the verse 'Take from their wealth' is not, by consensus, upon its apparent meaning. Indeed, you see that this verse is also absolute with respect to the condition of the passing of a year (hawalan al-hawl), yet zakat is only obligatory after a year. So it is known that this verse is to state the obligation of taking (zakat). That is, the verse only states the obligation of collecting zakat; all other matters are mujmal (ambiguous). And the interpretation of the mujmal is done by the hadith. Thus the hadith 'There is no zakat on pack animals...' is not an abrogator (nasikh) of the verse 'Take from their wealth...' but rather an explanatory statement (bayan tafsir). As for the claim that we carried the absolute upon the qualified in the hadiths, it is not that we carried a mutlaq hadith upon a muqayyad hadith. Rather, we consider the muqayyad to be later (mu'akhkhar) and the mutlaq to be earlier (muqaddam), and the later abrogates the earlier. Thus the mutlaq hadiths are abrogated by the muqayyad hadith 'There is no zakat on pack animals...'
Definition of sa'imah and 'alufa: The author of al-Hidayah says that sa'imah is the animal which is content with grazing for most of the year. So if it is fed for half the year or more, it is called 'alufa. In the case of more than half the year, it is 'alufa because the small follows the large. So when most of the year...
Source pages p. 71

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute between the Hanafi school and Imam Malik regarding zakat on work animals ('awamil), pack animals (hawamil), and stall-fed animals ('alufa). The Hanafi position, shared by the Shafi'is, is that no zakat is due on these animals. Imam Malik holds that zakat is obligatory on all livestock based on apparent general texts. The passage first states the ruling and then provides three Hanafi proofs: (1) Specific hadiths exempting these categories; (2) The cause (sabab) of zakat is growing wealth (mal nam), which is absent here because growth is evidenced by free grazing (sa'imah) or trade preparation, and these animals are not free-grazing nor trade goods; (3) Stall-fed animals incur continuous feeding expenses, which negates the meaning of growth. The passage then addresses an objection regarding the use of khabar wahid to restrict the general Quranic command. The answer explains that the Quranic verse is mujmal (ambiguous) and is interpreted by the hadith, not abrogated. Furthermore, the mutlaq hadiths (e.g., the hadith on zakat rates) are abrogated by the muqayyad hadith (the exemption hadith) because the latter is considered later. Finally, the passage defines sa'imah (free-grazing) as an animal that grazes for most of the year, and 'alufa as one that is fed for half the year or more, with the principle that the lesser follows the greater.

Key Terms
سائمہ (sā'imah): Free-grazing livestock that graze on open pasture for most of the year without being fed by the owner.
علوفہ ('alūfah): Stall-fed animals that are fed by the owner for half the year or more, hence not considered growing wealth.
عوامل ('awāmil): Work animals used for labor such as plowing.
حوامل (hawāmil): Pack animals used for carrying loads.
نامی (nāmī): Growing or increasing; wealth that has the potential to increase naturally (e.g., livestock through breeding) or through trade.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, when does an animal become 'alufa (stall-fed) and thus exempt from zakat?
A) When it is fed for any amount of time.
B) When it is fed for half the year or more.
C) When it is fed for the entire year.
D) When it is used for work.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, zakat on livestock is only due on sa'imah (free-grazing) animals; work, pack, and stall-fed animals are exempt because they lack the condition of growth.

Zakat — Almsgiving
intermediate
10 min
Responding to the Maliki Objection: Usul Principles in Zakat Exemption
Addressing the objection to the Hanafi ruling and providing usul justification

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain how the Hanafi school uses usul principles (mujmal, bayan, abrogation) to defend the exemption of work, pack, and stall-fed animals from zakat.

Core Idea
The Quranic command for zakat is mujmal; specific hadiths interpret it. General hadiths are abrogated by later specific exemptions.

In this lesson, we examine the objection raised by Imam Malik's school: how can a single-narrator hadith (khabar wahid) restrict the general Quranic command? The Hanafi response demonstrates how usul al-fiqh principles are applied to reconcile texts. We also refine the definitions of sa'imah and 'alufa.

Guided Path
1
Understand the Maliki objection
Imam Malik argues that the Quranic verse 'Take from their wealth sadaqah' and the general hadiths on zakat rates are absolute (mutlaq) and include all livestock. The Hanafi use of a specific hadith to exclude some animals seems to restrict the mutlaq with a khabar wahid, which Hanafis normally do not allow.
This is a methodological challenge based on Hanafi usul.
2
Analyze the Hanafi response: the Quranic verse is mujmal
The Hanafi school holds that the Quranic verse 'Take from their wealth' is mujmal (ambiguous) regarding the details of zakat. It only states the obligation of collecting zakat, not the specifics. Therefore, it is not a mutlaq that can be restricted; rather, it requires interpretation (tafsir) from the Sunnah.
Thus, the specific hadith does not restrict the Quran; it explains it.
3
Analyze the Hanafi response: abrogation of general hadiths
The general hadiths (e.g., 'For every five camels, one sheep') are mutlaq, but the specific exemption hadith is considered later (mu'akhkhar). According to Hanafi usul, a later specific text abrogates (naskh) an earlier general text. So the general hadiths are abrogated, not restricted.
This is a different operation: not haml al-mutlaq 'ala al-muqayyad, but naskh.
4
Define sa'imah and 'alufa precisely
The passage defines sa'imah as an animal that grazes freely for most of the year. 'Alufa is one fed for half the year or more. This definition is critical because only sa'imah animals are considered growing wealth.
The principle 'the lesser follows the greater' is applied.

سے کوئی بات نہیں پائی گئی ہے۔ اس لئے زکوۃ واجب ہونے کا سب منفی ہو گیا اور جب سبب منفی ہو گیا تو ز کو بھی منعی ہو جائے گی ۔ تیسری دلیل یہ ہے کہ علوفہ ( جن جانوروں کو باندھ کر کھلایا جاتا ہے) میں پیہم خرچہ کا بار پڑتا ہے یعنی ان کو چارہ دینا پڑتا ہے تو معنی علوفہ کے اندر نمو معدوم ہو گیا اور نمو جب معدوم ہو گیا تو زکوۃ واجب ہونے کا سبب نہ پایا گیا اور جب سبب ز کو نہیں پایا گیا تو زکوۃ بھی واجب نہ ہوگی۔ سوال: اس جگہ ایک سوال ہے وہ یہ کہ امام مالک نے اپنی دلیل میں اطلاق کتاب "خُذْ مِنْ اَمْوَالِهِمْ " کو پیش فرمایا ہے لیکن آپ نے خبر واحد لَيْسَ فِي الْحَوَامِل صَدَقَةٌ .. الحدیث سے اس کے اطلاق دُودٍ مِنَ الْإِبِلِ شَاةً وَفِي كُلِّ ثَلَثِيْنَ مِنَ الْبَقَرِ تَبِيعُ اَوْتَبِيعَةُ، مطلق ہے اس میں عوامل یا غیر عوامل کی کوئی قید نہیں ہے۔ جس سے مطلقاً اونٹ اور گائے وغیرہ میں زکوۃ کا وجوب ثابت ہوتا ہے لیکن آپ نے اس کو لَيْسَ فِي الْحَوامِلِ والعوامل الحدیث پر محمول کیا ہے حالانکہ آپ کے نزدیک مطلق کو مقید پر محمول کرنا جائز نہیں ہے۔ جواب: آیت " خُذ من متواریم کا اطلاق بالا جماع اپنے ظاہر پر نہیں ہے۔ چنانچہ آپ دیکھئے کہ یہ آیت حولان حول کی قید سے بھی مطلق ہے حالانکہ زکوة حولان حول کے بعد ہی واجب ہوتی ہے پس معلوم ہوا کہ یہ آیت وجوب اخذ کو بیان کرنے کے لئے ہے۔ یعنی آیت میں فقط " زکوۃ" وصول کرنے کے وجوب کو بیان کیا گیا ہے اس کے علاوہ تمام چیزوں میں مجمل ہے۔ اور مجمل کی تفسیر حدیث سے کی جاتی ہے پس حدیث لَيْسَ فِي الْحَوَامِلِ... الحديث آيت خُذْ مِنُ اَمْوَالِهِمْ صَدَقَةً (التوبہ (۱۰۳) تاریخ اور مبطل نہیں ہے بلکہ بیان تفسیر واقع ہے۔ اور رہا یہ کہنا کہ ہم نے اخبار و احادیث میں مطلق کو مقید پر محمول کیا ہے ایسا نہیں ہے کہ ہم نے مطلق حدیث کو مقید پر محمول کیا ہو ۔ بلکہ ہم نے مقید کو مؤخر مانا ہے اور مطلق کو مقدم اور مؤخر مقدم کے لئے ناسخ ہوتا ہے بس احادیث مطلقه حديث مقيده لَيْسَ فِي الْحَوَامِل الحدیث کی وجہ سے منسوخ ہو گئیں ہیں۔
سائمہ و علوفہ کی تعریف صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ سائمہ وہ جانور ہوتا ہے جو سال کے اکثر حصہ میں چرنے پر اکتفاء کرے۔ چنانچہ اگر آدھے سال یا کثر باندھ کر کھلایا تو وہ علوفہ کہلائے گا۔ اکثر سال کی صورت میں تو علوفہ اس لئے ہو گا کہ قلیل کثیر کے تابع ہوتا ہے پس جب سال کے اکثر
And there is no zakat on work animals, pack animals, and stall-fed animals, contrary to Malik who has apparent texts (as proof). And our proof is his (peace be upon him) saying: 'There is no zakat on pack animals, work animals, nor on the ox that plows.' And because the cause (sabab) is wealth that grows, and the evidence of growth is free grazing or preparation for trade, and that is not found. And because in stall-fed animals, expenses accumulate, so the meaning of growth is absent. Then the sa'imah (free-grazing animal) is that which is content with grazing for most of the year, so much so that if one feeds it for half the year or more, it becomes 'alufa (stall-fed), because the small (part) follows the large (part).
Translation: There is no zakat on 'awamil, hawamil, and 'alufa. Imam Malik disagrees; his proof is from apparent texts. Our proof is the saying of the Prophet (peace be upon him): 'There is no zakat on pack animals, work animals, and the ox that plows.' And the cause for zakat is wealth that grows, and the evidence of growth is free grazing or preparation for trade, and neither is found. And for 'alufa, continuous expense is incurred, so the meaning of growth is absent. Then the sa'imah is the animal that is content with grazing for most of the year; if one feeds it for half the year or more, it is 'alufa, because the small follows the large. Explanation: 'Awamil is plural of 'amila, animals used for work. Hawamil is plural of hamila, animals used for carrying loads. 'Alufa are animals that are fed (stall-fed) for the whole year or more than half, or according to the author of al-Hidayah, if fed for half the year. According to us and the Shafi'is, there is no zakat on these animals, but according to Imam Malik, there is. Imam Malik's proof is from apparent texts: Allah says, 'Take from their wealth sadaqah' (at-Tawbah 103) – the word 'amwal' includes all wealth. And the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'For every five camels, one sheep; for every thirty cattle, a tabi' or tabi'ah; and for every forty sheep, one sheep.' And in another hadith: 'Take from camels, camels.' All these texts are absolute (mutlaq), and their absoluteness requires that zakat is obligatory on all types of camels, cattle, and sheep, whether they are 'awamil or not, hawamil or not, 'alufa or sa'imah. Our proof is that Ali (may Allah be pleased with him) said that the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'There is no sadaqah on camels that carry loads,' and the hadith of Ibn Abbas from the Prophet (peace be upon him): 'There is no sadaqah on the plowing ox.' The author of al-Hidayah combined all three in one hadith. In any case, these hadiths prove that zakat is not obligatory on 'awamil and hawamil. The second proof is that the cause of zakat being obligatory is that the wealth is growing, and these properties are not growing, because the evidence of growth is that the animal grazes in the open pasture or is prepared for trade, and in 'awamil, hawamil, and 'alufa, neither is found. Therefore, the cause for zakat is negated, and when the cause is negated, zakat is also negated. The third proof is that in 'alufa (animals that are kept and fed), there is continuous expense (they need to be fed), so the meaning of growth is absent, and when growth is absent, the cause for zakat is not found, so zakat is not obligatory. Question: Here a question arises: Imam Malik presented the absolute (mutlaq) of the Book, 'Take from their wealth,' but you have nullified its absoluteness with a khabar wahid (single-narrator hadith) 'There is no zakat on pack animals...', whereas according to your principles, it is not permissible to nullify or abrogate the absolute of the Book with a khabar wahid. Also, you have carried the absolute upon the qualified (muqayyad), in that the hadith presented by Imam Malik, 'For every five camels...' is absolute, with no qualification of 'awamil or others, which obligates zakat absolutely on camels, cattle, etc., but you have carried it upon the hadith 'There is no sadaqah on pack animals and work animals,' whereas according to you, it is not permissible to carry the absolute upon the qualified. Answer: The absoluteness of the verse 'Take from their wealth' is not, by consensus, upon its apparent meaning. Indeed, you see that this verse is also absolute with respect to the condition of the passing of a year (hawalan al-hawl), yet zakat is only obligatory after a year. So it is known that this verse is to state the obligation of taking (zakat). That is, the verse only states the obligation of collecting zakat; all other matters are mujmal (ambiguous). And the interpretation of the mujmal is done by the hadith. Thus the hadith 'There is no zakat on pack animals...' is not an abrogator (nasikh) of the verse 'Take from their wealth...' but rather an explanatory statement (bayan tafsir). As for the claim that we carried the absolute upon the qualified in the hadiths, it is not that we carried a mutlaq hadith upon a muqayyad hadith. Rather, we consider the muqayyad to be later (mu'akhkhar) and the mutlaq to be earlier (muqaddam), and the later abrogates the earlier. Thus the mutlaq hadiths are abrogated by the muqayyad hadith 'There is no zakat on pack animals...'
Definition of sa'imah and 'alufa: The author of al-Hidayah says that sa'imah is the animal which is content with grazing for most of the year. So if it is fed for half the year or more, it is called 'alufa. In the case of more than half the year, it is 'alufa because the small follows the large. So when most of the year...
Source pages p. 71

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute between the Hanafi school and Imam Malik regarding zakat on work animals ('awamil), pack animals (hawamil), and stall-fed animals ('alufa). The Hanafi position, shared by the Shafi'is, is that no zakat is due on these animals. Imam Malik holds that zakat is obligatory on all livestock based on apparent general texts. The passage first states the ruling and then provides three Hanafi proofs: (1) Specific hadiths exempting these categories; (2) The cause (sabab) of zakat is growing wealth (mal nam), which is absent here because growth is evidenced by free grazing (sa'imah) or trade preparation, and these animals are not free-grazing nor trade goods; (3) Stall-fed animals incur continuous feeding expenses, which negates the meaning of growth. The passage then addresses an objection regarding the use of khabar wahid to restrict the general Quranic command. The answer explains that the Quranic verse is mujmal (ambiguous) and is interpreted by the hadith, not abrogated. Furthermore, the mutlaq hadiths (e.g., the hadith on zakat rates) are abrogated by the muqayyad hadith (the exemption hadith) because the latter is considered later. Finally, the passage defines sa'imah (free-grazing) as an animal that grazes for most of the year, and 'alufa as one that is fed for half the year or more, with the principle that the lesser follows the greater.

Key Terms
سائمہ (sā'imah): Free-grazing livestock that graze on open pasture for most of the year without being fed by the owner.
علوفہ ('alūfah): Stall-fed animals that are fed by the owner for half the year or more, hence not considered growing wealth.
مجمل (mujmal): A text that is ambiguous and requires external explanation to be understood.
ناسخ (nāsikh): Abrogating text; a later text that overrides an earlier one.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi response in this passage, how does the specific hadith relating to work and pack animals interact with the Quranic verse 'Take from their wealth sadaqah'?
A) It abrogates the verse.
B) It restricts the verse, which is mutlaq.
C) It explains the verse, which is mujmal.
D) It is in conflict with the verse and requires tarjih.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school resolves the apparent conflict between general and specific texts by classifying the Quranic command as mujmal and using the principle of abrogation for contradictory hadiths.

Zakat — Almsgiving
intermediate
6 min
Zakat on Working and Pregnant Animals
Dispute with Imam Malik over zakat on working livestock

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school exempts working and pregnant livestock from zakat and evaluate its response to the Maliki objection.

Core Idea
Zakat is wajib on livestock that grow; working and pregnant animals do not grow, so no zakat is due.

In this passage from al-Hidayah, the author defends the Hanafi exemption of working and pregnant livestock from zakat against the Maliki position. The debate centers on interpretation of absolute vs. restricted texts and the role of growth (nama') as the cause of zakat. Understanding this dispute reveals key Hanafi usul principles.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position and its evidence
Identify the explicit hadith cited by the Hanafis: 'There is no sadaqah on pregnant camels' and 'There is no sadaqah on working cattle'. Also note the rational proof: zakat requires growth, which is absent in these animals.
The hadith are ahad (zanni al-thubut), but accepted due to reliability.
2
Identify the opposing Maliki evidence
Imam Malik relies on absolute texts like the Quranic verse 'Take from their wealth sadaqah' and the hadith 'For every five camels, one sheep' without qualification.
These texts appear to include all camels and cattle.
3
Analyze the Hanafi response to the Maliki objection
The Hanafis argue that the Quranic verse is mujmal (ambiguous) and explained by hadith, not abrogated. The absolute hadith are abrogated by the restricted hadith (تخصيص), as the restricted hadith came later.
This is a sophisticated usul argument: the restricted hadith is not a restriction but an abrogation of the absolute.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf (practical difference)
The practical impact: a Hanafi farmer with working/pregnant livestock pays no zakat; a Maliki farmer pays zakat on the same animals.
This exemplifies legitimate ikhtilaf based on different usul methodologies.

مطلق حدیث کو مقید پر محمول کیا ہو ۔ بلکہ ہم نے مقید کو مؤخر مانا ہے اور مطلق کو مقدم اور مؤخر مقدم کے لئے ناسخ ہوتا ہے بس احادیث مطلقه حديث مقيده لَيْسَ فِي الْحَوَامِل الحدیث کی وجہ سے منسوخ ہو گئیں ہیں۔
For every five camels, one sheep; for every thirty cattle, a tabi' (one-year-old); for every forty sheep, one sheep. And in one hadith: 'Take from camels.' These texts are absolute, and their requirement is that zakat is fard on every type of camel, cow, and sheep, whether they are working or non-working, pregnant or non-pregnant, fed or grazing. Our proof is that Ali (ra) narrated that the Prophet (saw) said: 'There is no sadaqah on pregnant camels' and the hadith of Ibn Abbas: 'There is no sadaqah on working cattle.' These hadith prove that zakat is not fard on working and pregnant animals. The second proof: the cause for zakat being wajib is that the property grows, and these are not growing because their growth (nama') is evidenced by free grazing or preparation for trade, which is absent in working and pregnant animals. The third proof: 'ulufah involve continuous expense, eliminating growth, so the cause of zakat is absent. Objection: Imam Malik relies on the absolute texts of the Quran and hadith, and we abrogate them with ahad hadith, which we do not permit. Also we restrict absolute with restricted, which we also do not permit. Answer: The Quranic verse is not absolute on its face, as it is interpreted by hadith; the restricted hadith is not an abrogator but an explicator, and the absolute hadith are abrogated by the restricted hadith.
Source pages p. 72

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute. It begins by stating the absolute texts that would seem to require zakat on all livestock, then presents the Hanafi position that working and pregnant animals are exempt. The author cites hadith from Ali and Ibn Abbas that explicitly exempt pregnant camels and working cattle. The second argument is rational: zakat is only due on growing wealth, and these animals do not grow because they are not free-grazing or prepared for trade. The third considers 'ulufah: they incur constant cost, negating growth. Then a question from Imam Malik is raised: How can you restrict these absolute texts with a single ahad hadith? The Hanafi response clarifies: the Quranic verse is not absolute; it only commands collection, and the details come from hadith. Thus the hadith are explicators, not abrogators. As for the absolute hadith, the restricted hadith abrogates them because the restricted is later in revelation order. This is a sophisticated usul argument.

Key Terms
العوامل (al-‘awāmil): Working animals used for plowing or transport.
الحوامل (al-ḥawāmil): Pregnant or burden-carrying animals.
العلوفة (al-‘ulūfah): Animals that are fed at home, not grazing freely.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on zakat for working cattle (البقر المثيرة)?
A) Zakat must be paid.
B) No zakat is due.
C) Zakat is only paid if they are pregnant.
D) Zakat is paid at half the normal rate.

Key Takeaway
Working and pregnant livestock are exempt from zakat in the Hanafi school due to specific hadith and the absence of the cause of zakat (growth).

Definition of Sa'imah and 'Ulufah and Their Zakat Ruling
Defining grazing and fed livestock with zakat obligation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of sa'imah and 'ulufah, apply the majority-time rule, and determine the zakat obligation based on feeding duration.

Core Idea
Zakat on livestock depends on whether they graze freely most of the year.

In this lesson, we examine the classic Hanafi distinction between sa'imah (grazing livestock) and 'ulufah (fed livestock). The ruling on zakat obligation hinges on this category: zakat is wajib on sa'imah but not on 'ulufah. The key is the proportion of time the animal spends grazing versus being fed at home. The text from Al-Hidayah clarifies the threshold and applies the legal principle that the minor follows the major (taba'iyyah al-qalil li al-kathir).

Guided Path
1
Identify the Two Categories
Read the definition and note the two terms: sa'imah (animals that graze freely for most of the year) and 'ulufah (animals fed at home). Understand that the ruling (zakat wajib or not) flows from this classification.
The Arabic terms are السائمة and العلوفة.
2
Determine the Temporal Threshold
The passage specifies 'most of the year' (أكثر السنة) as the criterion. If an animal grazes for more than half the year, it is sa'imah. If it is fed at home for more than half the year, it is 'ulufah. Pay attention to exactly half (نصف السنة) as a special case.
The exact half case triggers doubt and default to no zakat.
3
Apply the Rule of the Minor Following the Major
Understand the principle that a small portion follows the larger portion. If most of the year is feeding, the entire year is considered feeding. This makes the animal 'ulufah even if it grazed briefly.
This is a key usul principle applied here.
4
Analyze the Half-Year Case
When exactly half of the year is grazing and half is feeding, there is doubt (shakk). The preferred ruling (mufta bihi) is that the animal is 'ulufah and no zakat is due, because the cause (sabab) of zakat (free grazing) is not established with certainty.
The principle of al-yaqin la yazulu bi al-shakk (certainty is not removed by doubt) is implicitly used.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
سائمہ و علوفہ کی تعریف صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ سائمہ وہ جانور ہوتا ہے جو سال کے اکثر حصہ میں چرنے پر اکتفاء کرے۔ چنانچہ اگر آدھے سال یا کثر باندھ کر کھلایا تو وہ علوفہ کہلائے گا۔ اکثر سال کی صورت میں تو علوفہ اس لئے ہو گا کہ قلیل کثیر کے تابع ہوتا ہے پس جب سال کے اکثر حصہ میں اس کو باندھ کر کھلایا ہے۔ تو سال کی وہ قلیل مدت جس میں چرنے پر اکتفاء کیا ہے وہ بھی اس کثیر کے تابع ہوگی۔ بس گویا پورے سال اس کو باندھ کر گھاس کھلایا ہے اور آدھے سال کی صورت میں زکوۃ واجب ہونے کے سبب کے ثبوت میں شک ہو گیا ۔ اس طور پر کہ اگر اس آدھے سال پر نظر کی جائے جس میں اس نے چرنے پر اکتفاء کیا ہے۔ تو زکوۃ واجب ہونی چاہئے ۔ اور اگر اس آدھے سال پر نظر کی جائے جس میں اس کو گھر باندھ کر گھاس کھلایا ہے تو زکوۃ واجب نہ ہونی چاہئے پس اس شک کی وجہ سے عدم وجوب کو تر جیح دی گئی ۔ اور کہا گیا کہ آدھے سال باندھ کر کھلانے کی صورت میں بھی وہ جانور علوفہ ہوگا۔ اور اس میں زکوۃ واجب نہ ہوگی۔
Definition of sa'imah and 'ulufah: The author of Hidayah says: Sa'imah are animals that suffice by grazing for most of the year. If they are fed at home for half a year or more, they are called 'ulufah. If fed at home for most of the year, then it is 'ulufah because the minor portion follows the major. So the entire year is considered as fed. In the case of half a year, doubt arises: if considering the half when it grazed, zakat would be wajib; if considering the half when fed, zakat would not be wajib. Due to this doubt, non-obligation is preferred, and it is ruled that even if fed at home for half the year, the animal is 'ulufah and no zakat is due.
Source pages p. 72

Commentary
This passage defines two key terms for zakat on livestock. Sa'imah are animals that spend most of the year grazing freely in the desert, without being fed at home. Such animals grow naturally and thus zakat is due. 'Ulufah are animals that are kept at home and fed by the owner. If fed for more than half the year, they are fully 'ulufah. If exactly half, doubt arises, and the default is no zakat. This is because the cause of zakat (growth) is present only in sa'imah. The principle that the majority determines the ruling (تبعیة القلیل للکثیر) is applied.

Key Terms
السائمة (as-sā'imah): Livestock that graze freely most of the year.
العلوفة (al-‘ulūfah): Livestock that are fed at home, not free-grazing.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person feeds his sheep at home for exactly half the year and lets them graze for the other half, what is the ruling according to the Hanafi school?
A) The animal is considered sa'imah and zakat is due.
B) The animal is considered 'ulufah and no zakat is due.
C) Zakat is due only on the half that grazed.
D) The owner must calculate zakat based on monthly estimation.

Key Takeaway
Zakat on livestock is only due on sa'imah (free-grazing for most of the year); if fed at home for half the year or more, the animal is 'ulufah and no zakat is wajib.

The Zakat Collector Must Take Average-Quality Animals
Ruling that collector should take neither best nor worst but medium

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the quality of animals taken by the zakat collector and explain the evidence.

Core Idea
Balance justice: collector must take average, neither best nor worst.

This lesson addresses a specific fiqh ruling concerning the zakat collector's selection of livestock. It clarifies that the collector may not take the best nor the worst, but only the middle grade. The ruling is supported by the Prophet's (saw) command and a rational argument that considers both the payer and the recipient.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What exactly is being ruled upon? The act of taking animals for zakat. The ruling: it is wajib (obligatory) to take average quality.
The level is wajib based on a command.
2
Locate the dalil
What proof does the author cite? The primary dalil is the hadith of the Prophet (saw): 'Do not take the valuable properties of the people... take from their peripheries.' Also the practice of Umar (ra) and instruction to Mu'adh (ra).
Multiple narrations strengthen the evidence.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How exactly does this dalil prove the ruling? The prohibition of taking 'khayar' (best) and command to take 'hawashi' (peripheries, explained as average) indicates that average is obligatory.
The hadith uses explicit prohibitive and imperative forms.
4
Note the rational argument
The author also provides a rational proof (ta'lil): taking average balances consideration for both the owner (not overburdened) and the poor (adequate quality).
This shows Hanafi use of nazar (consideration of interests).
5
Confirm the Hanafi position
There is no intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf; the mufta bihi is that the collector must take average quality.
The position is from Zahir al-Riwayah and relied upon.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مصدق چھانٹ کر اچھا مال لے نہ گھٹیا وَلَا يَأخُذُ المُصَدِّقُ خِيَارَ الْمَالِ وَلَا رُذَالَتَهُ وَ يَأْخُذُ الْوَسَطَ لِقَوْلِهِ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ لَا تَأْخُذُوا مِنْ حَرَزَاتِ أَمْوَالِ النَّاسِ أَى كَرَائِمِهَا وَخُذُوا مِنْ حَوَاشِي أَمْوَالِهِمْ أَى أَوْسَا طِهَا وَلِأَنَّ فِيهِ نَظَرًا مِنَ الْجَانِبَيْنِ ترجمہ اور مصدق نہ عمدہ مال لے اور نہ گھٹیا مال لے ۔ بلکہ اوسط درجہ کا مال لے۔ کیونکہ حضور پیے نے فرمایا ہے کہ لوگوں کے اموال میں سے عمدہ اور بہتر مال مت لو۔ اور ان کے اموال میں سے اوسط درجہ کا مال لو۔ اور اس لئے کہ اس میں طرفین کا لحاظ ہے تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ مصدق یعنی زکوۃ وصول کرنے والا ۔ نہ اعلیٰ درجہ کا مال لینے پر اصرار کرے اور نہ بالکل ردی اور گھٹیا مال لے ۔ بلکہ درمیانی درجہ کا مال لے۔ یعنی اعلیٰ مال سے ادنی ہو اور ادنی مال سے اعلیٰ ہو۔ دلیل قول بنی علیہ السلام " لَا تَأخُذُوا مِن حَرزَاتِ أمْوَالِ النَّاسِ وَخُدُ وَامِنُ حَوَاشِئ أموالهم حرزات حززة کی جمع ہے معنی ہیں عمدہ اور بہترین مال۔ خواہشی، حاشیہ کی جمع ہے۔ مصنف نے حاشیہ کی تفسیر وسط کے ساتھ فرماتی ہے۔ اب مطلب یہ ہوگا کہ رسول اکرم پیے نے اعلیٰ درجہ کا مال لینے سے منع فرمایا ہے۔ اور درمیانی درجہ کا مال لینے کا امر فرمایا ہے۔ موطا امام مالک میں ہی مَرَعُمَرُ رَضِيَ اللهُ عَنْهُ بِغَلَم الصَّدَقَةِ فَرَأَى فِيهَا شَاةُ حَافِلاً ذَاتَ ضَرعَ عَظِيمٍ ، فَقَالَ عَمَرَ مَاهَذِهِ الشَّاةُ فَقَالُوا شَاةٌ مِنَ الصَّدَقَهِ فَقَالَ عُمَرُ مَا أعطى هذه أهْلهَا وَهُم طَائِعُونَ لَا تَفْتِنُوا الناس لاتأخذوا حَزَرَاتِ الْمُسْلِمِينَ یعنی حضرت عمر رضی اللہ عنہ کا گذرز کوۃ کی بکریوں کی طرف ہوا تو ایک بکری موٹی تازی بڑے تھن والی دیکھ کر فرمایا کہ یہ بکری کیسی ہے لوگوں نے کہا کہ زکوۃ کی بکری ہے تو حضرت عمر نے فرمایا کہ اس بکری کے مالک نے اس کو خوشی سے نہ دیا ہو گا تم لوگوں کو فتنہ میں مت ڈالو۔ لوگوں کے عمدہ مال مت او ۔ اس حدیث سے بھی عمدہ مال زکوۃ میں وصول کرنے کی ممانعت ثابت ہوئی۔ اور حضور صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے حضرت معاذ رضی اللہ عنہ سے فرمایا تھا ایاك وَ كَرَائِم أموالهم خبر دار لوگوں کے اموال سے عمدہ مال مت لینا ۔ عقلی دلیل یہ ہے کہ اوسط درجہ کا مال لینے میں زکوۃ دینے والے اور فقیر دونوں کو رعایت ہے اور عمدہ مال لینے میں فقط فقیروں کی رعایت ہے اور گھٹیا مال لینے میں صرف زکوۃ دینے والے کی رعایت ہے پس دونوں کی رعایت کے پیش نظر اوسط درجہ کا مال لینے کا امر کیا گیا ہے۔
The collector should not take the best of the property nor the worst, but take the average, due to his (saw) saying: 'Do not take the valuable properties of the people, i.e., their best, and take from their peripheries, i.e., their average.' And because it takes into account both sides. ... Explanation: The collector should neither insist on taking the best nor the worst, but take the middle grade. Proof from the hadith of Umar (ra) and the hadith of Mu'adh (ra). Rational proof: Taking the average considers both the payer and the poor; taking the best only favors the poor; taking the worst only favors the payer.
Source pages p. 73

Commentary
This passage states the ruling that the zakat collector must take animals of medium quality. The author cites the hadith of the Prophet (saw) prohibiting taking the best and ordering the average. Additional evidence from the practice of Umar (ra) and the instruction to Mu'adh (ra). The rational argument balances the interests of both the owner (who should not be overburdened) and the recipient (who should get adequate quality). This is a clear example of Hanafi usul where maslaha and nazar (consideration) are applied.

Key Terms
المصدق (al-muṣaddiq): The zakat collector appointed by the state.
خيار المال (khiyār al-māl): The best quality animals.
الوسط (al-wasaṭ): The average quality.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following best describes the ruling on the quality of animals taken by the zakat collector?
A) He may take the best animals to benefit the poor.
B) He may take the worst animals to avoid burdening the owner.
C) He must take animals of average quality.
D) He may take any animal chosen by the owner.

Key Takeaway
The zakat collector must take animals of average quality to ensure fairness to both the owner and the poor.
